201 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bell


SC 17864


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 748; 931 A.2d 198; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 369


May 17, 2007, Argued 
September 11, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Bell, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 510 (Conn., Dec. 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender and with the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty of one count each of assault in the first degree, carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver; thereafter, the second part of the information was tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court, Devlin, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the verdicts and enhanced the defendant's sentence for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm and for being a persistent dangerous felony offender, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant directly appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him, after a jury trial, of assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(5); carrying a pistol without a permit, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a) (Rev. to 2001); and criminal possession of pistol or revolver, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217c(a)(1) (Rev. to 2001).


OVERVIEW: After a hearing by the trial court, defendant's sentence was enhanced for being a persistent dangerous felony offender, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a) and (h). On appeal, defendant claimed that certain prosecutorial improprieties deprived him of a fair trial and that his sentence enhancement as a persistent dangerous felony offender violated his Sixth Amendment right to a trial by jury, because a finding that was a necessary predicate to the enhancement was made by the trial court, rather than by the jury, which should have made that finding beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that defendant was improperly asked to judge the credibility of the State's witnesses but that the error did not deprive him of a fair trial. However, the court did find that the trial court violated the dictates of Apprendi and its progeny when it imposed the sentence enhancement after its determination that defendant's history and character, and the nature and circumstances of his criminal conduct, indicated that extended incarceration and lifetime supervision would best serve the public interest as such a determination was for the jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment only as to the sentence imposed and remanded the case to the trial court for a new sentencing proceeding. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

202 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Minn. Methane, LLC v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


SC 17692


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 700; 931 A.2d 177; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 341


March 12, 2007, Argued 
August 28, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the named defendant opening its prior decision involving an energy purchase agreement between the plaintiff and the defendant Connecticut Light and Power Company and ordering the plaintiff to transfer, inter alia, certain renewable energy certificates to the defendant Connecticut Light and Power Company, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, McWeeny, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for an order to reserve certain issues of federal law for adjudication in federal court; thereafter, the remaining issues were tried to the court; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Minn. Methane, LLC v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 846 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the owner of a landfill gas energy facility, filed an administrative appeal against defendants, the Department of Public Utility Control, a utility, and the Office of Consumer Counsel. Plaintiff challenged the Department's decision regarding certain renewable energy certificates. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) dismissed the appeal. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 2003, the utility filed a petition with the Department requesting that the Department reopen a 1996 proceeding and issue a declaratory ruling that plaintiff was required to transfer renewable energy certificates to the utility pursuant to a 1997 electricity purchase agreement. In 2004, the Department held that it had jurisdiction over the matter under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176 and other state statutes. It held that the utility was entitled to ownership of the certificates on the ground that plaintiff's renewable source of fuel was the necessary condition for the Department's approval of the 1997 agreement. The trial court upheld the Department's decision and dismissed the appeal. The court stated that in a companion case, it had addressed substantially identical claims and had concluded that the Department had jurisdiction over the dispute, that there was substantial evidence to support the 2004 decision, and that the 2004 decision was not an unconstitutional taking under Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. It adopted the reasoning and conclusions of the companion case. Accordingly, it rejected plaintiff's claims on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

204 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


SC 17271


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 280; 929 A.2d 278; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 303


January 5, 2007, Argued 
July 31, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder, attempt to commit murder and carrying a pistol without a permit and with three counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Schimelman, J., denied in part the defendant's motions to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Hadden, J., verdict of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, three counts of assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit; thereafter, the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, a jury convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55a, three counts of assault in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(5), and carrying a pistol without a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a). The Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) sentenced him to 48 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress on the ground that he did not have standing to challenge the legality of the search of a family member's apartment under Conn. Const. art. I, § 7. The supreme court disagreed, finding, inter alia, that Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 did not embody the automatic standing doctrine or the "legitimately on the premises" rules of standing. In order to have had standing, defendant needed to prove that he had a reasonable expectation of privacy, which defendant failed to do. Defendant also argued that the evidence was insufficient to establish his identity as the shooter. The supreme court disagreed, noting that the jury could reasonably have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that he had a motive to shoot the victims, was present at the time of the shooting, and possessed the gun that was used. Finally, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the reasonable doubt standard in violation of his federal constitutional right to a fair trial. The supreme court found no error, noting that the instructions, when considered as a whole, were not improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

205 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saucier


SC 17502


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 207; 926 A.2d 633; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 289


October 25, 2006, Argued 
July 17, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Saucier v. Comm'r of Corr., 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 595 (Conn. App. Ct., Dec. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with six counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of four counts of sexual assault in the first degree and one count of kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and McLachlan and Gruendel, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Saucier, 90 Conn. App. 132, 876 A.2d 572, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 293 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, upon the grant of certification, a judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a trial court judgment that convicted him of sexual assault and kidnapping, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-70(a)(1) and 53a-92(a)(2)(A). The appellate court had affirmed the trial court's preclusion into evidence of a statement by the victim in reference to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asked the victim to cover a shift at a restaurant. Rather than drive the victim home, defendant drove her to various locations where he brutally and repeatedly sexually assaulted her. She managed to escape and police were called. Defendant was convicted after a jury trial of the kidnapping charge, and of four out of six sexual assault charges. He was sentenced and sought review. The appellate court affirmed the convictions, and it agreed with the trial court's evidentiary ruling regarding the victim's statement to an acquaintance that "she got him." The court held that the statement, which indicated a potential fabrication, was not within the state of mind hearsay exception under Conn. Code Evid. R. 8-3(4), as it was a statement of past intent or motive after an act, rather than a statement of present or future intent. On certified review, the court initially held that the appropriate standard of review of an evidentiary ruling was based on the specific nature of the claim. Defendant was deemed to have abandoned the claim that the statement was not hearsay. The trial court's determination that the statement was inadmissible under the hearsay exception was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

206 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Walsh v. Jodoin


SC 17837


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 187; 925 A.2d 1086; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 287


April 16, 2007, Argued 
July 17, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal by the state from the decision of the family support magistrate, Harris T. Lifshitz, terminating a child support order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich, where the court, Swienton, J., rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the state appealed.
Mallove v. Jodoin, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2878 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 25, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of Connecticut, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London at Norwich (Connecticut), which dismissed its appeal from the decision of a family support magistrate terminating the child support orders against defendant father, retroactive to the 18th birthday of his minor child. The State was the party plaintiff on behalf of the named plaintiff, the child's mother.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father were never married. The child was born on November 8, 1986, and the father was the acknowledged father of the child. The State had been providing public assistance for the child and applied to the trial court in 1990 for a support order, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172(b) (Rev. to 1989). In 2004, the family support magistrate ordered the father to appear to show cause why he should not be held in contempt of court for failing to pay. The family support magistrate ordered termination of the support order as of November 8, 2004, since the child attained his 18th birthday at that time, though the child was still in high school. The trial court determined that 2004 Conn. Pub. Acts 04-100, which extended the obligation of child support for non-married individuals until the child was 19 years old or graduated from high school, whichever occurred first, did not apply retroactively. The court disagreed, concluding that though P.A. 04-100 did not set forth explicitly that it applied retroactively, applying the public act differently to children of married parents versus unmarried parents violated equal protection of the laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with directions for it to sustain the State's appeal.

 

207 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Comm'r of Envtl. Prot.


SC 17592


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 86; 925 A.2d 1071; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 283; 37 ELR 20168


January 4, 2007, Argued 
July 10, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, the constitutionality of a statute regulating the location of asphalt batching facilities, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Hon. Samuel Freed, judge trial referee; judgment for the defendant from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the court, Hon. Samuel Freed, judge trial referee, denied the plaintiff's motion for articulation; subsequently, the Appellate Court granted the plaintiff's motion for review of the trial court's denial of its motion for articulation but denied the relief requested, and the appeal was transferred to this court.
Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 9 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 5, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hartford Superior Court (Connecticut) entered a judgment for defendant commissioner after plaintiff limited liability company filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a determination that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-196, regulating the location of asphalt batching facilities, was unconstitutionally applied to it, and that the statute had been improperly applied retroactively to it. The limited liability company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The limited liability company applied to the commissioner for a permit to construct an asphalt batching facility. The commissioner issued a permit to the limited liability company, which included both a permit to construct an asphalt plant and a conditional permit to operate a plant. However, the permit expired after the limited liability company failed to fulfill a condition. The legislature then enacted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-196 (Rev. 1999), which restricted where an asphalt batching plant could be placed. As a result, the asphalt batching facility could not be placed on its property. It filed an action seeking a determination that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court, however, entered judgment for the commissioner. On appeal, the state supreme court found that since no fundamental right or suspect class was involved, the rational basis test applied and the statute was rationally related to the legitimate goal of protecting public health and the environment. It also found that the statute was not improperly applied retroactively to the limited liability company since it could not obtain a permit to operate the asphalt batching plant in the proposed location.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

208 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Coppola v. Logistec Conn. Inc.


SC 17604


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


283 Conn. 1; 925 A.2d 257; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 265; 2007 AMC 2623


October 24, 2006, Argued 
July 3, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district dismissing the plaintiff's application for benefits for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed from the decision of the compensation review board (Connecticut), which affirmed the decision of appellee, the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district, that dismissed plaintiff's claim for benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act (the state act), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-275 et seq., which arose from an injury while working for defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was in the business of unloading ships in a harbor and was injured while descending a ship's hold after a step broke beneath him. Plaintiff filed a claim under the Longshore and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act, 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq., and was awarded compensation. Plaintiff subsequently filed his claim under the state act, which the commissioner dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, plaintiff claimed that the board improperly concluded that the commissioner lacked jurisdiction over his claim because the injury occurred on the navigable waters of the United States and, therefore, the federal government had exclusive jurisdiction over the claim under U.S. Const. art. III, § 2 and the longshore act. The court agreed with plaintiff and held that the state has concurrent jurisdiction with the federal government over claims involving injuries incurred on navigable waters when the employer and the employee are locally based, the employment contract is performed within the state and partly on land, the injury took place on the state's territorial waters and the employer was required under the state act to secure compensation for any land based injuries.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that plaintiff's claim was governed by federal case law and fell squarely within the twilight zone doctrine as adopted by the United States Supreme Court in those cases. As such, the court held that the board improperly determined that the claim was not within the jurisdiction of the commissioner. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the board with direction to sustain plaintiff's appeal.

 

209 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Weber v. U.S. Sterling Secs., Inc.


SC 17623


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


282 Conn. 722; 924 A.2d 816; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 235


October 1, 2006, Argued 
June 19, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Class action to recover damages for the defendants' violation of the federal Telephone Consumer Protection Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and transferred to the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the court, Rogers, J., granted the motion of the named defendant et al. to dismiss the claims against them for lack of personal jurisdiction; subsequently, the court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the defendant Shawn Orr et al., and rendered judgment thereon in favor of those defendants, and the plaintiff appealed.
Weber v. U.S. Sterling Secs., 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1031 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 8, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Stamford-Norwalk Superior Court (Connecticut) granted summary judgment to defendant alleged wrongdoers' upon finding that their membership in a Delaware limited liability company meant that they could not be held personally liable under federal law regarding the sending of fax advertisements. It also found that New York law barred the claimant's class action complaint and his individual action. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sued, inter alia, the alleged wrongdoers, doing business as a limited liability company and asserted that they had sent an unsolicited fax ad to the claimant in violation of the Telephone Consumer Protection Act, 47 U.S.C.S. § 227. The fax advertised the services of their Delaware limited liability company. The alleged wrongdoers were both residents of Connecticut; the fax ads at issue were allegedly sent entirely within New York state. The claimant brought the action in his individual capacity and as a class action. The trial court granted the alleged wrongdoers' summary judgment motion after concluding that their membership in the Delaware limited liability company precluded their personal liability. The trial court also concluded that CPLR 901(b) barred the claimant's class action claim, while General Business Law § 396-aa barred the claimant's individual action. On appeal, the state supreme court found that they could be held liable under Delaware law for liability arising from their tortious conduct and that the claimant had an individual action claim, but also concluded that his class action complaint was properly barred.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment grant that found New York law barred the claimant's class action complaint was affirmed. However, its judgment finding that the alleged wrongdoers' membership in a limited liability company meant they could not be held personally liable and its finding that his individual action was barred, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

210 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Am. States Ins. Co. v. Allstate Ins. Co.


SC 17651


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


282 Conn. 454; 922 A.2d 1043; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 197


February 15, 2007, Argued  
May 15, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring the rights and liabilities of the parties under an automobile liability insurance policy issued by the defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Hon. Jerry Wagner, judge trial referee, granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment as to liability only; thereafter, the issue of damages was tried to the court, Bryant, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, McLachlan, Harper and Peters, Js., which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to that court with direction to render judgment for the defendant, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Am. States Ins. Co. v. Allstate Ins. Co., 94 Conn. App. 79, 891 A.2d 75, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 84 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an umbrella policy insurer (UPI), appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed a trial court judgment and held that judgment should be entered for the UPI in a declaratory judgment action regarding the rights and liabilities of the parties under a policy issued by defendant automobile liability insurer (ALI). The matter arose due to the insureds' involvement in an accident.


OVERVIEW: The driver was a domiciliary of Connecticut. Her passenger was a domiciliary of Florida, the vehicle owned by both parties was principally garaged there, and the ALI for both parties was issued in Florida. During an extended visit by the passenger with the driver, her daughter, in Connecticut, the passenger was injured in an automobile accident. The UPI provided a defense to an action brought by the passenger, and it paid her damages pursuant to an arbitration award. The UPI then filed suit against the ALI, seeking indemnification. The trial court granted the UPI's motion for summary judgment on the issue of liability, finding that the matter was controlled by Connecticut law, and that the household exclusion was not valid under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-335(d). The appellate court reversed that decision and remanded the matter with directions to enter judgment for the ALI, finding that Florida law was controlling and accordingly, the exclusion applied. On further review pursuant to certification, Florida was deemed to have the most significant relationship with the claims, as it was the principal location of the insured risk and application thereof did not offend Connecticut law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

211 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Knybel


SC 17650


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 707; 916 A.2d 816; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 96


October 23, 2006, Argued  
March 20, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with a violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the court, Swords, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hartford Superior Court (Connecticut) revoked defendant's probation imposed in connection with a prior conviction after it found him guilty of operating an all-terrain vehicle on a public highway while his license was under suspension and it found that he violated the special probation condition not to operate a motor vehicle while his license was suspended. The state supreme court transferred his appeal to the appellate court to its court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two criminal offenses involving operation of a motor vehicle. As a sentence, he received, inter alia, three years of probation. The probation terms included a general condition prohibiting him from violating any state criminal law and a special condition prohibiting him from operating a motor vehicle while his license was suspended. Eventually, he started serving his probation. He then operated an all-terrain vehicle on a public highway and was later charged with operating a motor vehicle while his license was suspended in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c) and with a violation of his probation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32. The trial court found that he violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c) and the special probation condition. On appeal, the state supreme court rejected his vagueness argument regarding Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c), found that an ordinary person of reasonable intelligence would know that it prohibited him from operating an all-terrain vehicle on a public highway with a suspended license, and that he should have known that "not operating a motor vehicle" included not operating an ATV.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

212 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Pasquariello v. Stop & Shop Cos.


SC 17595


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 656; 916 A.2d 803; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 98


January 4, 2007, Argued  
March 20, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district awarding the plaintiff temporary total disability benefits, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which reversed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed; thereafter, Diana Milner, executrix of the plaintiff's estate, was substituted as the plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Workers' Compensation Review Board (North Carolina) entered a decision that reversed the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district and concluded that defendant employer could reduce plaintiff claimant's total disability benefits by the amount of social security benefits that the claimant received, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e) (Rev. 1997). The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant retired and started receiving social security benefits. Thereafter, he began working for the employer and continued receiving such benefits. He then sustained a work-related compensable injury. The employer contended that it did not have to pay him total incapacity benefits because, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e), it was entitled to reduce his total disability benefits by the amount of his social security benefits, which appeared to exceed his total disability benefits. He filed a claim for total disability benefits. The workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district concluded that an offset was not intended for persons receiving social security benefits prior to their employment. The employer appealed. The workers' compensation review board reversed. On further review, the state supreme court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e) allowed for total disability benefits to be offset by social security benefits, that the statute was rationally related to the goal of lowering employers' workers compensation costs, and that the claimant's rights under the state and federal constitution's equal protection clauses were thus not violated.


OUTCOME: The decision of the workers' compensation review board was affirmed.

 

213 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKenzie-Adams


SC 17451


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 486; 915 A.2d 822; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 70


September 21, 2006, Argued  
February 27, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McKenzie-Adams v. Conn., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11022 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Four informations charging the defendant with fourteen counts of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Devlin, J., joined the informations and granted the state's motion to admit certain evidence of uncharged misconduct; subsequently, the court granted the state's motion to admit certain constancy of accusation evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty of fourteen counts of sexual assault in the second degree; subsequently, the court granted the defendant's motion for acquittal as to one of the counts and rendered judgments of guilty on the remaining thirteen counts of sexual assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. McKenzie-Adams, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1043 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 16, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant, a teacher, guilty of 14 counts of sexual assault in the second degree, against students, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(8). Defendant moved for judgments of acquittal. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) granted the motion with respect to one count and rendered judgments of conviction in accordance with the jury's verdict on the remaining counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a) violated his right to sexual privacy under the state and federal constitutions. The supreme court agreed with the State that, even if defendant had a right to engage in noncommercial consensual sexual intercourse with individuals over the age of consent, that right did not protect sexual intimacy in the context of an inherently coercive relationship, such as the teacher-student relationship, wherein consent might not easily be refused. The supreme court further concluded that joinder of the offenses against two victims was proper because, if the cases had been tried separately, the evidence of defendant's uncharged sexual misconduct with each victim would have been admissible to establish a common scheme or plan; among other things, the victims were both juniors in high school, the conduct began with kissing, and the conduct occurred in similar settings. Finally, the supreme court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that the probative value of the constancy of accusation testimony by friends of the victims outweighed its prejudicial effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

214 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Batte-Holmgren v. Comm'r of Pub. Health


SC 17505


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 277; 914 A.2d 996; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 56


February 8, 2006, Argued  
February 13, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring unconstitutional the law banning smoking in public establishments licensed to serve alcoholic liquor, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Lavine, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike the complaint; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment and rendered judgment thereon for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Batte-Holmgren v. Galvin, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3313 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 5, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owners filed an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against defendant officials. Plaintiffs argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-342, which prohibited smoking in restaurants and cafes, violated the Equal Protection Clause and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) granted defendants' motion to strike. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first noted that plaintiffs had not provided notice to interested persons under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-56(b). Overruling its past precedent, the court held that the failure to notify interested persons in a declaratory judgment action, like noncompliance with joinder rules, did not implicate the court's subject matter jurisdiction. As for due process concerns, the interests of nonparties who might be interested in the present action were represented adequately by the current parties. Next, in exempting existing private clubs from the ban, the legislature reasonably might have been endeavoring to protect the financial investment and settled expectations of their members. This was a rational basis for the exemption. As for the exemption of casinos, Connecticut casinos were operated by Native American tribes pursuant to gaming compacts. Uncertainties concerning the legislature's power to regulate the tribes, as well as the state's ability to enforce such a regulation, were sufficient to provide a rational basis for the casino exemptions. The legislature might have also had concerns about the tribes' sovereignty or their relationships with the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

215 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 17575


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 241; 914 A.2d 1034; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 57


November 21, 2006, Argued  
February 13, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, White, J., pursuant to a stipulation of the parties, granted the motion to cite in the board of parole as a respondent; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Flynn and Dupont, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the respondents, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Baker v. Comm'r of Corr., 91 Conn. App. 855, 882 A.2d 1238, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 433 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, filed a habeas corpus petition alleging that respondents, the Commission of Correction and the Board of Pardons and Paroles, improperly classified him as a violent offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b)(2) and (c) (Rev. to 2001). The trial court dismissed the petition. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed the judgment. Respondents moved for certification, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether an inmate had a cognizable liberty interest in his parole eligibility status sufficient to invoke the subject matter jurisdiction of a habeas court. The state supreme court concluded such a liberty interest did not exist. There was no constitutional or inherent right of a convicted person to be conditionally released before the expiration of a valid sentence. Whether and to what extent a State created a liberty interest in parole by statute was entirely at the discretion of the State. The state supreme court held that there was no indication in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a (Rev. to 2001) that the legislature intended to assure an inmate's parole eligibility status upon serving 50 percent of his or her sentence. Thus, the statute did not create a liberty interest sufficient to invoke habeas corpus jurisdiction. The state supreme court held that the inmate's claim that parole eligibility was an integral part of a criminal sentence was unavailing, as parole eligibility statute was not within the terms of the sentence imposed. Thus, the state supreme court held that the appellate court erred in reversing the dismissal of the petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

 

216 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Sullins v. Rodriguez


SC 17642


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 128; 913 A.2d 415; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 27


October 27, 2006, Argued  
January 30, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for injuries sustained as a result of the defendants' alleged violation of the plaintiff's federal constitutional rights, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Corradino, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss and granted the plaintiff's motion to strike certain defenses and to strike the defendants' claim for setoff, and the defendant Larry Myers appealed.
Sullins v. Rodriguez, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1532 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate sued defendant former warden and correction officer, in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for personal injuries, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court denied defendants' motion to dismiss and granted the inmate's motion to strike defenses and defendants' setoff claim. The Connecticut Supreme Court transferred the warden's appeal to the Appellate Court (Connecticut) to itself.


OVERVIEW: The inmate said the officer confined him with another inmate, who assaulted him. The supreme court held state sovereign immunity law did not govern the warden's asserted sovereign immunity defense because a federal right's vindication, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, was at issue, and state law could not immunize wrongful conduct under § 1983. Under federal law, sovereign immunity did not bar the inmate's claim, which was unambiguously stated against the warden individually. The state's agreement to indemnify the warden was irrelevant to whether the Eleventh amendment barred the claim against him, as he gave no reason why the relief the inmate sought could not come solely from him. Thus, the inmate's claim was not actually against the state. The only issue was whether, regardless of its strength, sovereign immunity barred the inmate's claim, not whether the inmate's conclusory allegation of inadequate training was a "fact" sufficient to establish the warden's individual liability. Whether the pleaded facts showed liability did not bear on an analysis of whether, under federal substantive law, the warden was sued in his individual capacity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Lagassey v. State


(SC 17603)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


281 Conn. 1; 914 A.2d 509; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 8


November 30, 2006, Argued  
January 9, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged medical malpractice of certain of the defendant's employees in connection with the death of the plaintiff's decedent, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Beach, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed; thereafter, this court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings; subsequently, the court, Stengel, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon for the defendant; thereafter, the court, Stengel, J., granted the motion of Paul Lagassey to be substituted as the plaintiff and the plaintiff subsequently appealed.
Lagassey v. State, 50 Conn. Supp. 130, 913 A.2d 1153, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2810 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, individually and as the executrix of her decedent husband's estate, brought a wrongful death action against defendant State. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) granted the State's summary judgment motion on the grounds that the action was time barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(d). Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court agreed with the State's construction of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(d) that the two-year limitations period was only suspended when plaintiff filed a notice of claim pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq.; the limitations period did not begin again when the claims commissioner granted plaintiff permission to sue. Plaintiff argued that the trial court's interpretation of § 4-160(d) rendered language in the statute superfluous. The appellate court adopted the trial court's well reasoned decision as a statement of the facts and applicable law since it would have served no useful purpose to repeat the discussion therein.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

218 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aloi


(SC 17350)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


280 Conn. 824; 911 A.2d 1086; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 2


March 9, 2006, Argued  
January 2, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant, in three cases, with two counts each of the crimes of burglary in the third degree, criminal mischief in the third degree and criminal trespass in the first degree, and with one count each of the crimes of tampering with a motor vehicle, interfering with an officer, disorderly conduct and attempt to commit criminal mischief in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the court, Shortall, J.; judgment of guilty in one case of criminal trespass in the second degree as a lesser included offense and criminal mischief in the third degree, and judgment of guilty in a second case of interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Bishop and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed only as to the conviction of interfering with an officer and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of that crime, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Aloi, 86 Conn. App. 363, 861 A.2d 1180, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 547 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court found defendant guilty of interfering with a police officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a (Rev. to 2001). The appellate court (Connecticut) reversed the judgment of conviction pertaining to that count. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for certification to appeal limited to the issue of whether the appellate court properly construed and applied Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a (Rev. to 2001).


OVERVIEW: The police responded to a report that defendant had vandalized a truck. An officer found defendant on public property near the truck. Defendant refused to produce identification upon the officer's request. The charge of interfering with a police officer was based on that refusal. The appellate court found that the refusal to produce identification did not constitute a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a (Rev. to 2001). The supreme court found that the statute did not categorically exclude from its purview a refusal to provide identification to a police officer who had sought such identification pursuant to a valid Terry stop, as such a refusal could hamper or impede a police investigation into apparent criminal activity. The supreme court further held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. The complainant had identified defendant by name. Thus, obtaining the identity of the individual found near the truck was a logical and necessary step in the investigation. Although the police eventually ascertained the identity of defendant, his refusal to comply with the officer's request for identification delayed the progress of the police investigation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed in part and the case was remanded to the appellate court with direction to affirm the judgment of conviction with respect to the charge of interfering with an officer. The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Lopez


(SC 17198)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


280 Conn. 779; 911 A.2d 1099; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 1


September 20, 2006, Argued  
January 2, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Lopez, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 820 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 24, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lopez v. Comm'r of Corr., 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3295 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of murder, and two counts each of the crimes of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Harper, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), two counts of attempted murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a) and 53a-54a(a), and two counts of assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(5).


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with defendant that, as new defense counsel had been appointed after trial and before sentencing, the trial court, as a general rule, should have allowed counsel an opportunity to review the trial transcript before holding a sentencing hearing. However, it concluded that there was no need to determine whether the trial court abused its discretion in denying a motion for a continuance on the basis of the record before it because, even if it did, defendant had made no claim that he was prejudiced in any way by the denial. One of the shooting victim's testimony was admissible under Conn. Code Evid. R. 4-5(b) on the issue of motive where he testified that, two to three weeks before the shooting, defendant had had an angry confrontation with an eyewitness during which he displayed a gun and that he also threatened the victim with the gun. The testimony tended to show that defendant harbored hostility toward the eyewitness and the victim. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the conclusion beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had been one of the shooters. The jury reasonably could have found that defendant intended to kill a bystander.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. George J.


SC 17577, SC 17578


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


280 Conn. 551; 910 A.2d 931; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 447


September 8, 2006, Argued  
November 28, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by George J. v. Conn., 167 L. Ed. 2d 573, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3865 (U.S., Apr. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in one case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, and substitute information, in a second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Parker, J., granted the motion to consolidate the cases; thereafter, the cases were tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdicts of guilty; subsequently, the court, Hadden, J., denied the defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, and rendered judgments in accordance with the verdicts, from which the defendant filed two separate appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases involving two victims, a jury in the Superior Court, New London, Connecticut, convicted defendant of first degree sexual assault, second degree sexual assault, and risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-70(a)(2) (1993), as amended by 1993 Conn. Acts 340, § 14; 53a-71(a)(1) (1993), as amended by 1993 Conn. Acts 340, § 2; and 53-21 (1993), respectively. Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that (1) his prosecution on all charges, except the second degree sexual assault charge, were time barred, and (2) the trial court improperly admitted victim one's testimony, which was allegedly the product of hypnosis. With respect to the first issue, the supreme court agreed with the State that defendant's prosecution for the abuse of victim one was timely because the limitations period under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-193a (1993), as amended by 1993 Conn. Acts 340, § 11, began to run when victim one directly reported the abuse to the police. Furthermore, defendant's prosecution for the two counts of risk of injury to a child were timely given the absence of persuasive evidence to support defendant's contention that the legislature intended § 54-193a to be limited to crimes for which an express element of the offense was sexual abuse, sexual exploitation, or sexual assault. As for the second issue, the record did not support a finding of an abuse of discretion in the trial court's finding that victim one's recollection of his abuse by defendant was not a product of hypnosis. Thus, defendant's motion to exclude victim one's testimony was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.

State v. Fagan


SC 17562


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


280 Conn. 69; 905 A.2d 1101; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 325


January 3, 2006, Argued  
September 26, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fagan v. Connecticut, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2916 (U.S., Mar. 5, 2007)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction from the trial court (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of one count of criminal violation of a protective order, one count of reckless driving, and one count of attempt to escape or elude a police officer. Defendant also appealed from the judgment revoking his probation imposed on a previous conviction after a trial to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from an incident involving his ex-girlfriend, who had a protection order against defendant. Defendant had called 911 indicating his name and that he just shot his ex-girlfriend in the face. The police went to the ex-girlfriend's home to check on her and observed defendant in his vehicle less than 33 feet away from the home. Defendant attempted to elude police by driving away. However, the court held that the mere intention to violate the order was sufficient to support a conviction under § 53a-223. The court further found that the trial court properly enhanced defendant's sentence, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40b, for violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-223(b), since no factual determination was required with regard to his probation revocation as the trial court properly took judicial notice of the same.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

State v. Scruggs


SC 17587


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 698; 905 A.2d 24; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 315



September 5, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and one count of the crime of cruelty to persons, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Frazzini, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Scruggs, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1380 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 8, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven at Meriden (Connecticut), which convicted defendant after a jury trial on one charge of risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1). After the jury rendered its verdict, defendant filed a motion for judgment of acquittal, which the trial court denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's 12-year-old son was a victim of intense bullying at his school. School authorities and investigators had found the child's personal hygiene lacking. The child hung himself in defendant's apartment. The trial court denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal upon concluding that, although there was no evidence to support a finding that defendant's conduct was likely to cause physical injury to the child, the jury reasonably could have found that by maintaining a cluttered and unclean residence, defendant wilfully had caused her son to be placed in a situation that was likely to injure his mental health. The court held that § 53-21(a)(1) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct. The court found that the trial court should have applied an objective standard in determining whether defendant had notice that her conduct fell within the scope of § 53-21(a)(1) since, although defendant reasonably could have been aware that the conditions in her apartment were not optimal, the court was not persuaded that the nature and severity of the risk were such that defendant reasonably could not have believed that they were within the acceptable range.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to grant defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal.

State v. Luster


SC 17268


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 414; 902 A.2d 636; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 303


March 14, 2006, Argued  
August 15, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Thompson, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55a. He appealed directly to the present court under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not object to a charge that his flight could be used as circumstantial evidence of consciousness of guilt. The court held that the unpreserved claim was not of constitutional magnitude and thus could not be addressed on the merits. It rejected defendant's argument that the charge tended to undermine his self-defense claim. Evidence of flight after using deadly force did not logically compel a conclusion that the reason for the flight was self-defense. Next, it was misconduct for the prosecutor to say that it was "fashionable of late to put the police department on trial." This remark, to which defendant had not objected, implied that criticizing the police investigation was a standard tactic used by defense counsel to divert a jury's attention from the "real" issues. This misconduct, however, did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. It was not frequent or severe; the State's case was strong enough to support a conclusion that an isolated instance of prosecutorial misconduct did not deprive the defendant of a fair trial; and the trial court's general instructions, which stated that arguments by counsel were not evidence, adequately addressed the improper remarks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Kerrigan v. Comm'r of Pub. Health


(SC 17563)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 447; 904 A.2d 137; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 298


February 9, 2006, Argued  
August 15, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to declare unconstitutional any state statute, regulation or common-law rule that is applied to deny a person the right to marry another person of the same gender, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the Family Institute of Connecticut filed a motion to intervene as party defendant; thereafter, the court, Pittman, J., denied the motion to intervene, and the Family Institute of Connecticut appealed.
Kerrigan v. State, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 618 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), denied intervention to movant institute, in a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiffs, seven same sex couples (couples), against defendant department of health (department), challenging the constitutionality of Connecticut's marriage laws insofar as they precluded the issuance of marriage licenses to same sex couples. The institute appealed.


OVERVIEW: The institute claimed that the trial court should have permitted it to intervene in the litigation either as a matter of right or permissively. The instant court disagreed. As to denial of intervention as a matter of right, the institute failed to identify an interest of direct and immediate character which would cause it to gain or lose anything as a result of the judgment in the present case. Second, it did not allege, much less demonstrate, that the judgment herein would affect any specific right or interest possessed by it or its members. All that it had established was its strong and capable commitment to championing a particular cause, which the trial court properly concluded was insufficient to require its intervention as a matter of right. As to its permissive intervention request, the trial court reasonably could have determined that the institute's interest in defending the constitutionality of the marriage laws would be adequately represented by the attorney general. Moreover, the present action was not one involving a multiplicity of divergent interests that needed to be represented separately because of different ways by which the merits might be resolved.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Brown


(SC 17533), (SC 17534)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 493; 903 A.2d 169; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 300


January 10, 2006, Argued  
August 15, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell and possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Flynn, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; thereafter, petition, in the second case, for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in New Haven, and tried to Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment granting in part the petition and restoring the petitioner's right to appeal his criminal conviction but denying his claims for other relief, and the defendant in the first case and the petitioner in the second case filed separate appeals that were subsequently consolidated and transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a)) and possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of a school (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b)). He also challenged the denial in part his amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that deprivation of defendant's constitutional right to counsel at a probable cause hearing did not prejudice his defense at trial or taint his conviction; because the record was devoid of any indication that defendant was harmed by the constitutional violation, the deprivation of counsel at the probable cause hearing was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. There was no evidence that defendant's attorney was prejudiced in his ability to prepare for cross-examination of an officer by the attorney's absence at the probable cause hearing. The transcript of the probable cause hearing was available to and reviewed by the attorney prior to cross-examination of the officer. Officers possessed a reasonable and articulable suspicion sufficient to justify a detention of defendant for investigative purposes under the Fourth Amendment, as the police had received an anonymous tip that specifically indicated that narcotics were being sold on that day in that location, which was a high trafficking area for narcotics. The police observed defendant standing in a group in the area identified by the caller as the location of the illegal drug sales.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

State v. Sawyer


SC 16972


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 331; 904 A.2d 101; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 285


November 21, 2005, Argued  
August 8, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, threatening and reckless endangerment in the first degree, and with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, and tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Dranginis, Flynn and Healey, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Sawyer, 74 Conn. App. 743, 813 A.2d 1073, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 38 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged, following the court's grant of certification, a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirming his conviction, after a jury trial, of, among other crimes, sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(1), and sexual assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant first challenged the Appellate Court's conclusion that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the State to introduce evidence of a threatening telephone call to establish the identity of the victim's assailant (Conn. Code Evid. R. 4-5(b)). The appeals court agreed with defendant. Because there were no significant and compelling similarities between the charged and uncharged offenses and thus no evidence of a distinctive "criminal logo," the trial court abused its discretion in permitting the State to introduce the evidence of the threatening telephone call. A lapse of three years between the charged and uncharged offenses could not be considered proximate in time. Improper admission of the uncharged misconduct evidence resulted in harmful error. A nonconstitutional error was harmless when an appellate court had a fair assurance that the error did not substantially affect the verdict. As the State's case was not particularly strong, the admission of the uncharged misconduct evidence was harmful because it suggested that defendant had a bad character and a propensity for criminal behavior, and thus improperly influenced the jurors' deliberations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Appellate Court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to that court for a new trial.

Putman v. Kennedy


SC 17392, SC 17396


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 162; 900 A.2d 1256; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 253


April 11, 2006, Argued  
July 18, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by Putman v. Kennedy, 104 Conn. App. 20, 932 A.2d 439, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 386 (2007)
On remand at Putman v. Kennedy, 104 Conn. App. 26, 932 A.2d 434, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 389 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Applications for, inter alia, relief from abuse and a temporary injunction, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland where the court, Kaplan, J., granted the applications and ordered the suspension of the defendant's visitation rights with the parties' minor children over whom the plaintiff earlier had been granted sole custody; thereafter, following a hearing, the court modified and extended the restraining order as to the plaintiff and one of the parties' minor children and denied the defendant's motion to reargue, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the court, Klaczak, J., granted the application for a second ex parte restraining order filed by the plaintiff, ordered the suspension of the defendant's visitation rights as to two of the parties' minor children, and, following a hearing, extended the restraining order; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to reargue and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the Appellate Court dismissed as moot the defendant's appeals and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which granted the defendant's motion to [***2] consolidate the appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, following a grant of his petitions for certification, from the judgments of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) dismissing his appeals from the trial court's grant of two separate applications by plaintiff for domestic violence restraining orders pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-15.


OVERVIEW: After the parties were divorced, plaintiff filed two applications pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-15 for relief from abuse against defendant, and requested that the court suspend his visitation with the parties' children. The trial court granted the applications and entered restraining orders against defendant, and defendant filed appeals of the orders. The appellate court dismissed the appeals as moot because the restraining orders had expired. The appellate court held that the expiration of a domestic violence restraining order did not render an appeal from that order moot because it was reasonably possible that there would be significant collateral consequences for the person subject to the order. The threat of reputation harm was particularly significant in this context because domestic violence restraining orders would not issue in the absence of the showing of a threat of violence, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-15(a). Furthermore, once filed, such orders were available to agencies investigating future allegations involving the same family, and a trial judge making a future custody determination might consider the issuance of such orders in making that sensitive decision.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the appellate court were reversed and the cases were remanded to that court for consideration of the merits of defendant's appeals.

W. Farms Mall, LLC v. Town of W. Hartford


SC 17464


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


279 Conn. 1; 901 A.2d 649; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 309


March 6, 2006, Argued  
July 11, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Sadler v. Mineta, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69122 (D. Conn., Sept. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a declaratory judgment determining the legality of the named defendant et al. in approving and establishing a special services district for a certain real estate development project of the defendant Blue Back Square, LLC, et al., brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the named defendant et al. filed a counterclaim; thereafter, the court, Booth, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to disqualify counsel for the named defendant et al.; subsequently, the court granted the defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of standing and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the action; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion for reargument and the plaintiff appealed.
W. Farms Mall, LLC v. Town of W. Hartford, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 197 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 27, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a shopping mall, filed an action for a declaratory judgment to determine the legality of the actions of defendant, a town, in approving and establishing a special services district for a certain real estate development project of defendant, a company. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) granted defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of standing. The mall appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mall claimed that the town's authorization of an agreement for the construction of a commercial project on land which housed various municipal buildings, issuance of bonds, and the conveyance of public land to the company were unlawful. On appeal, the mall contended that the trial court improperly imposed a heightened burden of proof as to taxpayer standing. The appellate court held that the trial court applied the proper standard by considering whether the mall demonstrated that its taxes would increase if the project were to proceed as planned and concluded that the mall failed to meet that burden. The mall's theory of standing was predicated on the notion that the mall was vindicating a right common to all taxpayers and consequently was relieved of its obligation to prove personal, special injury under the general standing rule. A majority of the town's voters twice approved by referendum the plans for the project. The appellate court held that the challenged actions of the town had been checked pursuant to a political process because the voters in essence ratified the action that the mall sought to have declared as unlawful on the taxpayers' behalf.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Tutson


SC 17287


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


278 Conn. 715; 899 A.2d 598; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 220


November 29, 2005, Argued  
June 27, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 7, 2006.
On remand at State v. Tutson, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 69 (Conn. App. Ct., Feb. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Flynn, Bishop and McLachlan, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Tutson, 84 Conn. App. 610, 854 A.2d 794, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 369 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree. The court sentenced defendant to 20 years' incarceration after merging the sentences for each offense. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State claimed that the Appellate Court improperly reversed defendant's conviction on the ground that the trial court's exclusion of certain alibi testimony deprived defendant of the right to present a defense under the United States Constitution. The state specifically challenged the Appellate Court's conclusion that the trial court improperly determined that the testimony of a key defense witness constituted an alibi, and abused its discretion in excluding the proffered testimony as a reasonable sanction for defendant's failure to satisfy the alibi notice provision of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 40-21. The supreme court agreed with the State, noting that the trial court properly characterized the subject testimony as an alibi for purposes of the notice provision of § 40-21. The supreme court further concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding the testimony as a sanction for noncompliance with the applicable rules of practice. Finally, the supreme court concluded that the testimony was not admissible under Conn. Code Evid. R. 8-3(4), as it was being offered for its truth, and was not relevant to proving defendant's state of mind.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Appellate Court was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to consider the State's sentencing claim and defendant's claim regarding instructional impropriety.

State v. Nash


SC 17570


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


278 Conn. 620; 899 A.2d 1; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 210


March 10, 2006, Argued  
June 20, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Nash, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3621 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 24, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Nash v. Warden, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3038 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, Alexander, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Alexander, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted defendant of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) and possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b). Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Among other errors, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence. Defendant argued that the police violated his Fourth Amendment rights by performing a patdown search. The appellate court found that the police had a reasonable and articulable suspicion that the defendant might have been armed and dangerous. The stop took place in a high crime area, and police observed defendant undertaking actions that appeared to be narcotics transactions. Immediately upon being stopped, defendant engaged in verbal resistance. The appellate court also held that the police did not exceed the scope of a permissible Terry stop by transporting defendant to a police substation. Defendant's resistance to the officers caused a large crowd to form to watch the action. This put the officer's safety at risk, and taking defendant to the substation was a reasonable action under the circumstances. Furthermore, the patdown search conducted at the substation while defendant was handcuffed did not exceed the scope of a justifiable search. The officers had only been able to frisk defendant's upper torso, and they still had a reasonable belief that defendant was armed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
