Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen


SC 17347, SC 17348


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


278 Conn. 500; 899 A.2d 542; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 186


January 4, 2006, Argued  
June 6, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant approving the application by the defendant Anthony DelMonaco Family Limited Partnership for a planned development district, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Radcliffe, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Schaller and Peters, Js., which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to sustain the plaintiffs' appeal, and the defendant Anthony DelMonaco Family Limited Partnership et al. and the named defendant, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals to this court.
Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen, 85 Conn. App. 820, 859 A.2d 586, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 472 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a partnership, appealed a decision by defendants, a city board of aldermen and others, which imposed conditions on the approval of an application for a planned development district. The trial court dismissed. The Connecticut Court of Appeals reversed the judgment. The parties filed cross-appeals, and the state supreme court granted certification.


OVERVIEW: The conditions placed on the planned unit development limited the size of a new building, the number of parking spaces, the hours of operation, and project phasing. On appeal, defendants argued that the trial court erred in concluding that there was no source of enabling authority for New Haven, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 65, and that the requirements for a valid planned development district under that ordinance were not sufficiently specific to be valid. The state supreme court held that the authority for zoning in the city was governed by the language incorporated into its municipal charter and approved by the General Assembly by way of a special act, 1925 Conn. Spec. Acts 490. The state supreme court held that this special act provided the city with the necessary enabling authority for New Haven, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 65, which allowed the board of aldermen to divide the city into zones, and consequently gave the board the power to form a new zoning district when it granted the application. The state supreme court further held that the zoning regulation was not unconstitutionally vague. Thus, the board's decision was valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

Cox v. Aiken


SC 17399


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


278 Conn. 204; 897 A.2d 71; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 163; 179 L.R.R.M. 2851


February 6, 2006, Argued  
May 16, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to compel the defendants to reinstate the plaintiff to his employment with the defendant department of social services, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Doherty, J., denied in part the defendants' motion to dismiss, and the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Schaller and Dranginis, Js., which affirmed the trial court's decision, and the defendants, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Cox v. Aiken, 86 Conn. App. 587, 862 A.2d 319, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 555 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a discharged employee, sued defendants, an agency and its director of human resources, to compel defendants to reinstate the employee to his employment with the agency, and for other relief. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss, except as it pertained to a claim for retroactive compensation. The Connecticut Court of Appeals affirmed the judgment. Defendants appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that his layoff violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-241 because that he was laid off while a person with less time in the same position was not laid off. The state supreme court held that the appellate court's analysis did not consider the effect of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-278(e), which provided that, when there was a conflict between the terms of a collective bargaining agreement and a statute, the terms of the collective bargaining agreement controlled, so long as they were approved by the legislature in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-278(b). The appellate court did not have the opportunity to consider the employee's statutory claims in the necessary context of the relevant collective bargaining agreement, which provided for superseniority for union stewards, the conflicting provisions of which had been approved properly by the legislature. Thus, because the facts alleged by the employee indicated that defendants acted consistently with the legislatively approved superseniority provision of the relevant collective bargaining agreement, defendants did not exceed their statutory authority, and they were entitled to sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to the appellate court with direction to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment dismissing the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Graff v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


SC 17356, SC 17357


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 645; 894 A.2d 285; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 106


November 21, 2005, Argued  
April 11, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the named defendant upholding a cease and desist order issued by the zoning enforcement officer of the town of Killingworth limiting the number of dogs the plaintiffs could have on their residential property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Robinson, J., granted the motion by Kerry O'Connell et al. to intervene as party defendants, and where the plaintiff Andrew Graff withdrew from the action; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Driscoll, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which, on the granting of certification, the intervening defendants and the named defendant filed separate appeals.
Graff v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of the Town Killingworth, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1008 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 14, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a town zoning board, and intervening defendants, several complainants, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which sustained the appeal of plaintiff, an owner of multiple dogs, and reversed the board's decision to uphold a cease and desist order that required plaintiff to reduce the number of pet dogs on her property in accordance with the town's zoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was alleged to have at least 14 dogs on her residential property. The board received numerous complaints from neighbors, the complainants, with regard to the noise generated by prolonged barking, aggressive behavior toward a complainant and her family, and unattended dogs roaming on the neighboring properties. The town commission adopted a resolution allowing four dogs or less per household as a permissible accessory use. The trial court determined that pet dogs were not regulated as an accessory use under the town regulations, that setting an enforceable limit on the number of dogs kept in each residence was a substantive change to the town regulations that required notice, and that keeping over four pet dogs was a permissible use of property in the town's rural residential district. The court determined that the trial court misconstrued the town regulations as plain and unambiguous when, in fact, they were not. The court found that caselaw precedent and secondary sources on land use and zoning supported the conclusion that household pets such as dogs were subject to regulation as an accessory use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to dismiss plaintiff's appeal.

Chatterjee v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs.

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 681; 894 A.2d 919; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 105


November 29, 2005, Argued  
April 11, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the defendant's disallowance of claims for the refund of certain capital gains, dividends and interest income taxes paid by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, and referred to Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee, who remanded the matter to the defendant for further proceedings; thereafter, the defendant again disallowed the plaintiffs' claims, and the plaintiffs filed a motion for judgment, which was denied by Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee, who, subsequently, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Chatterjee v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs., 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 746 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 10, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain, Tax Session (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from the decision of defendant, the commissioner of revenue services, that denied their request for a tax refund, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-39s.


OVERVIEW: In 1989 and 1990, the taxpayers filed capital gains, dividends, and interest income tax returns in Connecticut, reporting taxes due. They also filed Connecticut personal income tax returns for the years 1991 through 1993. In 1993, the State of New York performed a personal income tax audit on the taxpayers that resulted in paying the State of New York $ 2.4 million to settle their tax liabilities as New York residents. The court determined that the trial court properly concluded that refunds under § 12-39s were committed to the commissioner's sole discretion. The court also held that the trial court was without jurisdiction to evaluate the merits of the taxpayers' claim for a refund under § 12-39s since the three-year statute of limitations period contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-515 had expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Morris v. Congdon


SC 17336


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 565; 893 A.2d 413; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 93


November 28, 2005, Argued  
March 28, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 27, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for a writ of mandamus to compel the defendants to call a special town meeting, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Hon. D. Michael Hurley, judge trial referee, granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, DiPentima and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Morris v. Congdon, 85 Conn. App. 555, 858 A.2d 279, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 442 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town residents appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) which affirmed the judgment of the trial court rendering summary judgment in favor of defendant board of selectmen of the town (board) and its individual members. The issue was whether the board was required to warn a special town meeting in accordance with the residents' petition for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The residents submitted an application to the town clerk which called for the board to warn a special town meeting to consider and act upon a motion to eliminate the position of a town planner. The board refused to warn a meeting. The residents sought a writ of mandamus to compel the board to warn a town meeting pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-1(a). The lower appellate court reasoned that under § 7-1, the board was not required to warn a special town meeting as the meeting's purpose to eliminate the town planner position was improper because the board solely was responsible for hiring and firing town employees. The supreme court held the purpose of the meeting was not to fire an employee, but rather to eliminate a town position. The board had authority to create or eliminate the town planner position. The elimination of the position of town planner was a proper purpose for the town meeting. Since that purpose was proper, the board was required to warn a special town meeting under § 7-1. Finally, the proposed legislation was not an unconstitutional bill of attainder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was reversed.

Kinsey v. Pac. Emplrs. Ins. Co.


SC 17182


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 398; 891 A.2d 959; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 65


January 7, 2005, Argued  
March 7, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for an order to compel the defendant to proceed with arbitration of the plaintiff's claim for underinsured motorist benefits under a commercial fleet automobile insurance policy issued by the defendant to the plaintiff's employer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, the matter proceeded to a bifurcated arbitration; thereafter, the arbitrator determined that the request of the plaintiff's employer for a reduction in uninsured and underinsured motorist coverage was invalid; subsequently, the court, Lewis, J., denied the defendant's motion to vacate the arbitrator's decision and rendered judgment confirming the arbitrator's decision, from which the defendant appealed.
Kinsey v. Pac. Emplrs. Ins. Co., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3303 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sought, in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) to arbitrate a claim for underinsured motorist benefits under a commercial fleet policy issued to his employer. The trial court confirmed an arbitrator's decision that the employer's reduced coverage election was invalid, defendant insurer appealed, and the matter was transferred to the Connecticut Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was hurt by an underinsured motorist while driving his employer's vehicle, which was insured under a commercial fleet policy. The employer had elected underinsured motorist coverage less than that statutorily provided, but a statutorily required notice in the election form was not in 12-point type, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-336(a)(2), so an arbitrator and the trial court found the election invalid. The supreme court held, in analyzing the application of § 38a-336(a)(2) to a commercial fleet policy, it could not be determined from the text of the statute if the legislature intended its typeface requirements to strictly apply to commercial fleet policies, so, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-2z, extratextual evidence could be considered. This evidence showed a company insuring a fleet of vehicles to carry on a large commercial enterprise did not fall within the class of consumers the legislature sought to protect in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-336(a)(2), so there was no reason to require strict adherence to the requirement of a notice in 12-point type in the context of a commercial fleet policy, and the employer's election of reduced coverage was not invalid.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.


 

239 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Greco v. United Techs. Corp.


SC 17231


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 337; 890 A.2d 1269; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 56


January 13, 2005, Argued  
February 28, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Greco v. United Techs., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2431 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 3, 2003)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, surviving spouses and representatives of the estates of deceased former employees, appealed a judgment from a trial court (Connecticut), which granted in part defendant employers' motion to strike wrongful death claims on the ground that the action was time-barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that toxic substances in the workplace had caused the decedents' deaths from chemical poisoning and cancer. The motion to strike asserted that the action was untimely because it was brought on behalf of decedents who either had died more than two years before the action was filed or had ceased working for the employers more than five years before the action was filed. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577c(b), the statute of limitations for personal injury or property damage caused by toxic substances, did not preempt Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555. In addition, § 52-555 was not preempted by 42 U.S.C.S. § 9658(a)(1), which specified the applicable limitations period for actions under the Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act (CERCLA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 9601 et seq. Toxic exposure solely within a workplace was excluded from CERCLA's definition of the term "release," as provided in § 9601(22). Although the complaint alleged that toxic particles clung to the decedents' clothing and were carried into their cars and houses, such enclosed areas were not considered to be part of the environment for purposes of 42 U.S.C.S. § 9658(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Harris


SC 17326


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 378; 890 A.2d 559; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 54


October 25, 2005, Argued  
February 28, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to continue the commitment of the acquittee, who had been found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of arson in the first degree and refusing fingerprinting and committed for a period not to exceed ten years, to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Maiocco, J., denied the acquittee's motion to strike the report by the psychiatric security review board recommending continued commitment and the acquittee's motion to dismiss the petition, and rendered judgment recommitting the acquittee for a period not to exceed five years, and the acquittee appealed.
State v. Harris, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3572 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 4, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State petitioned the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for appellant acquittee's continued commitment. The trial court granted the petition, after denying the acquittee's motions to dismiss and strike the Psychiatric Security Review Board's report. The acquittee appealed to the Appellate Court, and the Supreme Court transferred the appeal to it.


OVERVIEW: Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(d), the Psychiatric Security Review Board had to report to the court whether or not to continue the acquittee's commitment after the expiration of his maximum prison term. The supreme court held the report was relevant as it assessed his mental state. Any bias only affected weight, rather than admissibility. It was not unfairly prejudicial as it did not arouse the fact finder's emotions, created no side issue, did not consume undue time, and the acquittee anticipated it. Admitting it did not violate his right to confrontation because that right did not apply to these civil proceedings. Its admission did not deprive him of a meaningful opportunity to be heard, as the procedures used adequately protected his liberty interest. Counsel represented him before the Psychiatric Security Review Board and he could have presented evidence there. He could have cross-examined all witnesses there and presented his own expert at state expense. The report was not subject to deferential review. The acquittee was free to rebut it. He had constitutionally adequate procedural protections.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Notopoulos v. Statewide Griev. Comm.


SC 17341


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 218; 890 A.2d 509; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 30


October 25, 2005, Argued  
February 14, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Notopoulos v. Statewide Griev. Comm., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5872 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant reprimanding the plaintiff for violation of the Rules of Professional Conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Murray, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal in part, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Schaller and Dranginis, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Notopoulos v. Statewide Griev. Comm., 85 Conn. App. 425, 857 A.2d 424, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 418 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant statewide grievance committee reprimanded plaintiff attorney for the attorney's letter criticizing a judge, under, inter alia, Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 8.2(a) and 8.4(4). On judicial review, the trial court sustained the attorney's appeal in part and dismissed it in part. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed, and the attorney was granted further review.


OVERVIEW: The attorney accused a probate judge of, inter alia, extortion regarding a case in which the attorney was conservator of his mother's estate. The supreme court held the trial court properly affirmed the committee's finding, by clear and convincing evidence, that the attorney violated Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 8.2(a) and 8.4(4). Its finding as to Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 8.2(a), barring an attorney's statements critical of a judge's qualifications, was not clearly erroneous, because the attorney's accusations were wholly conclusory. His letter, his testimony, and other documentary evidence showed a knowing or reckless disregard as to the truth or falsity of his statements. Rule 8.2(a) applied to him personally, as it did not indicate it was not so intended. Given his disregard for his statements' truth or falsity, the First Amendment did not protect them. They eroded public confidence in the judiciary, undermining the administration of justice, so his violation of Rule 8.2(a) showed he violated Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 8.4(4), barring conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice. Rule 8.4(4) did not say it was not intended to apply to attorneys personally.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

 

242 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Aselton v. Town of East Hartford


SC 17383


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 120; 890 A.2d 1250; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 25


October 17, 2005, Argued  
February 7, 2006, Officially Released


NOTICE:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence and for violation of the decedent's state and federal constitutional rights, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the action was dismissed as against the named defendant, and where the action was transferred to the judicial district of Tolland, Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the court, Sferrazza, J., granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the defendant James Shay et al. and rendered judgment thereon in their favor, from which the plaintiff appealed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Aselton v. Town of E. Hartford, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3377 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 3, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the administrator of the estate of a deceased police officer, appealed the decision of the Judicial District of Tolland, Complex Litigation Docket (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a town, its police chief, and various dispatch employees. The administrator brought a wrongful death suit, asserting that the police department employees provided inadequate and misleading information to the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was fatally shot when he unexpectedly encountered a home robbery in progress after having been dispatched to response to a 911 check welfare call. The administrator had asserted negligence claims as well as substantive violations of the federal constitution, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and the Connecticut Constitution. At trial, the administrator conceded that the workers' compensation exclusivity provision barred the negligence counts. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment upon concluding that there was no wilful misconduct and that no reasonable person could have concluded that defendants acted with the intent to expose the decedent to deadly force. On appeal, the administrator challenged the trial court's judgment only with respect to his asserted substantive due process claims under both the federal and state constitutions. The court acknowledged its adoption of the state created danger theory of liability but that the administrator failed to prove that the harm inflicted by the shooter, a private actor, was in any way attributable to defendant nor that defendants' conduct met the conscience shocking degree of culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Sorabella


SC 17215


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 155; 891 A.2d 897; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 29


March 14, 2005, Argued  
February 7, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sorabella v. Conn., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5841 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in which two cases were consolidated, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of attempt to commit sexual assault in the second degree, five counts of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child, two counts of attempt to entice a minor and one count each of importing child pornography, obscenity, and attempt to employ a minor in an obscene performance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the jury before Shortall, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty of two counts of attempt to commit sexual assault in the second degree, five counts of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child and one count each of attempt to entice a minor, importing child pornography, and obscenity, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Sorabella, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3422 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 23, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of attempt to commit sexual assault in the second degree, two counts of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child by sexual contact, three counts of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child, one count of attempt to entice a minor to engage in sexual activity, and pornography and obscenity crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an Internet undercover operation wherein a police officer posed as a 13-year-old girl online. The online profile for the purported victim clearly indicated that she was 13 years of age and instant messages between defendant and the victim also confirmed that defendant knew her age. Approximately 20 to 30 online conversations were engaged in wherein defendant was very explicit as to what sexual acts he wanted from the victim. Two meetings were set up, with defendant apprehended at the second one. Defendant contended on appeal that the attempt to commit sexual assault, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(a)(2) (2001), and attempt to commit risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 (Rev. to 1999) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(a)(1) (2001), were not cognizable crimes since they were strict liability crimes. The court disagreed and held that neither crime was a specific intent crime since each was a general intent crime. Therefore, it was enough that the State proved that defendant intended to have sexual intercourse with the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Pierre


SC 17227


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


277 Conn. 42; 890 A.2d 474; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 15


September 7, 2005, Argued  
January 31, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pierre v. Connecticut, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 4608 (U.S., June 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court Schimelman, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of kidnapping in the first degree and one count each of felony murder, robbery in the first degree and the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed; subsequently, the Appellate Court, Foti, West and Hennessy, Js., affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Pierre, 83 Conn. App. 28, 847 A.2d 1064, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 212 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of kidnapping in the first degree and one count each of felony murder, robbery in the first degree, and manslaughter in the first degree. Defendant was sentenced to 85 years' imprisonment. The court granted certification, permitting defendant to appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from the killing of a man, along with the assistance of a co-defendant, who had sought to purchase drugs from defendant. Prior to trial, defendant had moved to suppress written and oral statements obtained by the police based upon the argument that his right to counsel had attached at the State's signing of the information. Defendant also sought to suppress a prior inconsistent statement of a third party, namely a former co-worker of defendant who had provided the police with a seven page written statement describing incriminating statements made by co-defendant in his presence. The trial court denied defendant's motion. The court upheld that denial finding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the co-worker's prior inconsistent statement into evidence as the co-worker had claimed no memory of any incriminating statements made by co-defendant, which were squarely against co-defendant's penal interest and were, therefore, sufficiently trustworthy to have been admitted as an exception to the rule against hearsay. Defendant's right to counsel did not attach until the information was filed, which was at his arraignment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Skakel


SC 16844


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


276 Conn. 633; 888 A.2d 985; 2006 Conn. LEXIS 9


January 14, 2005, Argued  
January 24, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Request denied by, Objection sustained by Skakel v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 984 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 28, 2006)
Motion denied by Skakel v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1114 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 19, 2006)
Motion denied by Skakel v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2789 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 12, 2006)
Motion denied by Skakel v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3411 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 9, 2006)
Motion denied by Skakel v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3414 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 9, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Skakel v. Connecticut, 549 U.S. 1030, 127 S. Ct. 578, 166 L. Ed. 2d 428, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8617 (2006)
Motion granted by, in part, Reserved by, in part Skakel v. State, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 483 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 8, 2007)
Summary judgment denied by Skakel v. State, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 926 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 3, 2007)
Petition denied by, Motion for new trial denied by Skakel v. State, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2857 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Juvenile Matters at Stamford, where the court, Dennis, J., granted the state's motion to transfer the case to the regular criminal docket, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, which denied without prejudice the state's motion to dismiss the appeal; thereafter, the appeal was transferred to this court, which dismissed the appeal for lack of a final judgment; subsequently, the court, Kavanewsky, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss and motions in limine, and the matter was tried to the jury before Kavanewsky, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court, Kavanewsky, J., denied the defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and to set aside the verdict, and the defendant's amended motion for a new trial and request for an evidentiary hearing, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; the appeal thereafter was transferred to this court.
State v. Skakel, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3548 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 11, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54 (Rev. to 1975) after a jury verdict in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), from which defendant appealed to the Appellate Court. The appeal thereafter was transferred to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: In 1975, the fifteen-year-old victim was found bludgeoned to death in a wooded area on the grounds near her family home. No one was charged in connection with her murder until twenty-five years later, when defendant, a fifteen-year-old neighbor of the victim at the time of her death, was arrested and charged with the crime. Among other rulings, the supreme court rejected defendant's claim that the juvenile court improperly transferred his case to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court. In addition, the State's prosecution of defendant for the murder was not time barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-193. As the five-year limitation period of the pre-amendment version of § 54-193 had not expired with respect to the October, 1975 murder when a 1976 amendment to that statutory provision became effective, 1976 Conn. Acts 35, § 1 was the operative statute of limitations. Because § 1 applied and excluded all Class A felonies, including murder, from its five-year limitation period, the State's prosecution of defendant was not time barred. The court rejected its holding in Paradise that the canon of strict construction required the conclusion that § 1 had prospective effect only.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

247 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Albahary v. City of Bristol


SC 17265, SC 17266


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


276 Conn. 426; 886 A.2d 802; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 530; 61 ERC (BNA) 2015


September 23, 2005, Argued  
December 20, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a statement of compensation filed in connection with the partial taking by condemnation of certain property rights of the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Wiese, J.; judgment increasing the amount of compensation, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, McLachlan and Peters, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and, on the granting of certification, the plaintiffs and the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.
Albahary v. City of Bristol, 84 Conn. App. 329, 853 A.2d 577, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 338 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners, sued defendant, a city, challenging the statement of compensation filed by the city in connection with its taking by condemnation of certain interests in the owners' property. The trial court rejected the owners' claim for monetary damages, and the Connecticut Appellate Court affirmed the judgment. The parties filed separate appeals.


OVERVIEW: The groundwater under the owners' property was contaminated by leakage from a landfill operated by the city. The owners argued that the proper method of calculating damages for the inverse condemnation of the property was comparing the value of the land in its uncontaminated state to the value of the land in its contaminated state, and awarding the difference in monetary damages. The state supreme court held that the trial court properly rejected this measure because a federal court in an earlier action had rejected that proposed measure of damages, and thus the claim was barred by collateral estoppel. The federal court concluded that the contamination of the property was a result of the city's negligence and granted relief designed to restore the owners to the position that they would have been in had the contamination never occurred. This included injunctive relief which required the city to provide the owners with a potable water source and to indemnify, hold harmless, and defend the owners and subsequent owners against any claims of environmental liability. Thus, the appellate court held that owners' claims for monetary damages were barred by collateral estoppel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

248 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Commins


SC 17248


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


276 Conn. 503; 886 A.2d 824; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 533


September 21, 2005, Argued  
December 20, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 4, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and, in the second part, with having twice previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, where the court, White J., denied in part the defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the first part of the information was tried to the jury before White, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, West, McLachlan and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Commins, 83 Conn. App. 496, 850 A.2d 1074, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 267 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Thereafter, he pled nolo contendere to being a third offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g). He appealed the affirmation of his conviction by the Connecticut Appellate Court which held that defendant had waived his claim regarding his nolo contendere plea.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant as a third offender on the basis of two prior convictions in New York for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol or drugs in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1192 (1996). Defendant did not check the box indicating that his plea was conditional. Defendant claimed that he did not intend to admit that the elements of the New York offenses were substantially similar to the elements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g). The Supreme Court held that because the information set forth the statutory name of the crime, it was constitutionally sufficient. Defendant did not move to withdraw his plea. Therefore, his claim was not preserved for appellate review. Because the trial court never denied a motion to dismiss or a motion to suppress, there was no appealable issue under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a. Therefore, the lower appellate court correctly refused to apply Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a in order to review the merits of defendant's claim. The lower appellate court properly concluded that defendant waived his right to challenge the trial court's determination that he was a third offender pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed.

Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


(SC 17059), (SC 17060)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


276 Conn. 168; 884 A.2d 981; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 482


September 14, 2004, Argued  
November 15, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2529 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the plaintiffs as a result of the defendants' alleged negligent supervision of employees, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Levin, J., granted the defendants' requests for the protection of discovery materials from disclosure; thereafter, the matter was transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket, where the actions subsequently were withdrawn as against the defendants; thereafter, The New York Times Company filed a motion to intervene and to vacate the protective orders, and The Hartford Courant Company et al. filed motions to intervene; subsequently, the court, McWeeny, J., ordered the creation of a new file for the purpose of docketing the motion to vacate the protective orders and the motions to intervene, and the named defendant et al. and the intervenor John Doe et al. appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the court, McWeeny, J., ordered, inter alia, the unsealing and disclosure of certain documents in the custody of the clerk of the Superior Court, and the defendant Charles Carr et al., the named defendant et al., the intervenor [***2] John Doe I et al., and the defendant Martin Frederici filed separate appeals with the Appellate Court, Foti, Flynn and West, Js., which reversed the orders of the trial court concerning the motion to vacate the protective orders and the disclosure of the sealed documents, and the intervenors The Hartford Courant Company and The New York Times Company et al., on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals with this court.
Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 77 Conn. App. 690, 825 A.2d 153, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 280 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed a decision of the trial court granting intervenor newspaper company's motion to vacate protective orders (later joined by other intervenor newspaper companies) and the court's subsequent orders concerning the disclosure of sealed and protected materials. The court granted the companies' petitions for certification to appeal and set forth four revised certified questions.


OVERVIEW: The case arose from lawsuits alleging sexual abuse of minors by clergymen employed by the Roman Catholic Church. Protective orders were issued with respect to certain documents and information. Prior to trial, all of the lawsuits were settled and withdrawn. One company later moved to intervene and sought to vacate the orders sealing the documents. The appellate court held that because the cases had been withdrawn more than one year prior to the company's request, the trial court's actions were precluded by the four-month limitation period of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a. The supreme court concluded that the trial court retained continuing jurisdiction over the withdrawn cases insofar as the documents filed under seal in those cases were concerned, and just as a court had continuing jurisdiction to vacate or to modify an injunction after the four-month limitation period expired, so too did a court have continuing jurisdiction to vacate or to modify a protective order after the expiration of that limitation period. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in restoring the withdrawn cases to the docket. The companies had a strong interest in challenging the protective orders.


OUTCOME: The appellate court judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded (1) to affirm the trial court's decision effectively restoring the withdrawn cases to the docket and granting the companies intervenor status; (2) to vacate the orders issued in connection with the trial court's decision of May 8, 2002; and (3) to remand the case for a de novo determination of the merits of one company's request to unseal court files in the withdrawn cases.

State v. Brunetti


(SC 16788)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


276 Conn. 40; 883 A.2d 1167; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 456


October 20, 2004, Argued  
November 1, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Superseded by State v. Brunetti, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 248 (Conn., July 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the court, Holden, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain statements and evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Holden, J., verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) denied defendant's motions to suppress certain statements and evidence. A jury found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim engaged in sexual intercourse. The victim asked defendant to stop, and he refused. The victim threatened to go to the police, and defendant killed her. Defendant then went back to his parents' home. When the police took defendant to the station for questioning, his mother refused to grant consent to search the house, but his father granted consent. During the search, the police found defendant's clothes, which were stained with the victim's blood. Defendant then confessed to the crime. On appeal, defendant argued that because his mother declined to consent to the search of his home, the search was illegal and the evidence found pursuant to the search improperly was admitted into evidence by the trial court. The state supreme court held that under Conn. Const. art. I, § 7, when joint occupants had equal control over the premises, and both were present when consent to the search was sought, both joint occupants had to give their consent in order for the ensuing search to be valid pursuant to the consent exception. Therefore, the consent given by the father was not valid, and evidence discovered during the search should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Kelly v. City of New Haven


SC 17331


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


275 Conn. 580; 881 A.2d 978; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 345


April 15, 2005, Argued  
September 27, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in each case, for declaratory and injunctive relief to prohibit, inter alia, certain scoring practices used by the defendants on promotional examinations for police officers in the city of New Haven, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Pittman, J.; partial judgment in each case for the plaintiffs declaring the promotional practices to be violative of the New Haven charter and enjoining the defendants from utilizing those practices, from which the defendant city of New Haven appealed. Dismissed in part; affirmed in part; further proceedings.
Kelly v. City of New Haven, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 68 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 9, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court transferred to itself from the Connecticut Appellate Court defendant city's appeal from a partial judgment, by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, upholding challenges by plaintiff police officers to certain civil service promotion practices as violative of New Haven, Conn., Charter art. XXX.


OVERVIEW: The city had revised its application of the rule of three, a traditional civil service rule that gave managers discretion to choose among the top three candidates for promotion, to allow police department officials to consider more than three candidates in the event of tie scores on promotional examinations. Another change in practice, rounding exam scores, resulted in larger tied groups, and in the placement of some candidates, including the officers who were plaintiffs, in pools with lower priority than would have been their positions under the old system. Although there were too many unresolved issues in the trial court's rulings in two of the three consolidated cases, in one case, the ruling invalidating the rounding practice had resolved all the outstanding issues in that case, so the court reviewed that ruling, providing an interpretation that would also govern later trial proceedings in the other two matters. The civil service rules in art. XXX were to apply strictly, because the whole point of civil service legislation was to limit managerial discretion. Practices that resulted in promotional pools with 45 candidates were subversive of that legislative intent.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed two of the appeals for lack of appellate jurisdiction, but affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the third. It remanded the matter for further proceedings in all the cases.

 

252 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


(SC 16973)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


275 Conn. 205; 881 A.2d 160; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 329


February 14, 2005, Argued  
August 30, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information, in one case, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault of a peace officer and one count of the crime of intimidating a witness, and amended information, in a second case, charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, where the court, Foley, J., granted the state's motion for joinder; thereafter, the charge of criminal possession of a firearm was withdrawn and the court granted the state's motion in limine to introduce certain evidence and denied the defendant's motion to sever the trials; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury before Foley, J.; following the court's denial of the defendant's motion to strike certain testimony offered by the state, verdict of guilty; the court thereafter denied the defendant's motions for a new trial and for judgment of acquittal, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham (Connecticut), which convicted him for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), assault of a peace officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c(a)(1), and intimidation of a witness in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151a(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly: (1) admitted statements under the state of mind exception to the hearsay rule attributable to the victim; (2) charged the jury that they could infer intent to cause death from the use of a deadly weapon; and (3) included improper language in its jury charge on the presumption of innocence and proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Testimony on the victim's statements that she feared defendant fell under the state of mind exception in Conn. Code Evid. R. 8-3(4) and defendant's romantic relationship with the victim made her state of mind relevant to motive and to question a defense theory that someone else killed the victim. The exception was firmly rooted, so admissibility was proper under the Confrontation Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VI. Since defendant did not preserve his challenges to the jury charges, the court was limited to constitutional, plain error, and supervisory authority review. Though both challenged instructions contained language previously held to be improper, no manifest injustice occurred because the instructions as a whole eliminated any reasonable likelihood of the jury misunderstanding them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, assault of a peace officer, and intimidation of a witness.

Genesky v. Town of E. Lyme


(SC 17152)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


275 Conn. 246; 881 A.2d 114; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 331


October 18, 2004, Argued  
August 30, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the eighth district dismissing the plaintiff's claim for heart and hypertension benefits, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a constable claiming benefits under the Heart and Hypertension Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c, appealed from a decision of a compensation review board (Connecticut), which affirmed a workers' compensation commissioner's dismissal of the claim for heart and hypertension benefits.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the constable was a regular member of a paid municipal police department for purposes of § 7-433c benefits. The court affirmed, holding that the constable was not a regular member of a paid municipal police department. Although § 7-433c did not contain a functional definition of the term "paid municipal police department," the court reviewed several other statutes, including Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-294a and 7-277a, to determine that Connecticut differentiated between sworn members of organized local police departments and constables. The fact that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c did not expressly reference constables was dispositive of the court's finding that § 7-433c did not generally apply to them. The court also concluded that the town the constable worked for did not have a paid municipal police department. The town's ordinances vested the authority to appoint constables in the town board of selectmen, not the police commission required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-724 for establishing a police department. Also, the town had contracted for a resident state trooper, an action that could only be taken by towns without regular police departments.


OUTCOME: The board's decision was affirmed.

 

254 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carpenter v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 17155


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 834; 878 A.2d 1088; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 293


February 15, 2005, Argued  
August 9, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Graziani, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, West, DiPentima and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Carpenter v. Comm'r of Corr., 81 Conn. App. 203, 840 A.2d 1, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 33 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a habeas corpus petition challenging his manslaughter conviction. The trial court granted a motion by respondent, the Commissioner of Correction, to dismiss. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. The Commissioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner argued that the appellate court erred in ruling that the prisoner was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on the habeas corpus petition. The state supreme court concluded that the prisoner adequately pled ineffective assistance of counsel and, therefore, that the appellate court properly remanded for an evidentiary hearing. The prisoner alleged in his petition that his right to a jury trial in the underlying action was violated when the state supreme court ordered the trial court to modify the judgment to reflect a conviction of manslaughter because the jury never had considered whether he had the state of mind required for manslaughter. He then alleged in the reply that the ineffective assistance of his counsel excused his failure to raise the issue during the appeal or to challenge the decision after it was made. In other words, he claimed that the ineffective assistance of counsel constituted cause and prejudice permitting review of his claim despite the claimed procedural default, a claim that properly was raised by way of a reply. However, the state supreme court held that the appellate court improperly determined that the petition was not successive.


OUTCOME: The portion of the appellate court's judgment concluding that the petition was not a successive petition was reversed. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

State v. D'Antonio


SC 17096, SC 17095


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 658; 877 A.2d 696; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 316


March 15, 2005 Argued  
August 2, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in one case, charging the defendant with the crime of criminal trespass in the first degree, and substitute information, in a second case, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of interfering with an officer and one count of criminal trespass in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Clifford, J.; after the court granted in part the defendant's oral motion for a judgment of acquittal as to one count of criminal trespass in the first degree, verdicts and judgments of guilty of one count of criminal trespass in the first degree and two counts of interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Dranginis and DiPentima, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgments and remanded the cases for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court. Reversed; judgment directed. Two informations each charging the defendant with one count of violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical [***2] area number nine, and tried to the court, Clifford, J.; judgments revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Dranginis and DiPentima, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgments and remanded the cases for a new revocation of probation hearing, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. D'Antonio, 79 Conn. App. 683, 830 A.2d 1187, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 427 (2003)
State v. D'Antonio, 79 Conn. App. 696, 830 A.2d 1196, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 424 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State was granted certification to appeal from judgments of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed judgments of a trial court. The trial court's judgments found defendant to be in violation of his probation and also convicted defendant on two counts of interfering with an officer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a(a).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court ruled that the trial court's participation in an unsuccessful plea negotiation with defendant and its participation in defendant's trial and sentencing constituted plain error under Niblack. The court reversed, holding that 1) a Niblack violation was not reviewable under Golding but could be reviewed for plain error; 2) establishing a Niblack violation did not excuse defendant from demonstrating that the failure to grant relief would result in manifest injustice; 3) a trial court presiding over a trial after having first participated in unsuccessful plea bargaining efforts was not, by itself, plain error; 4) to the extent that State v. Falcon, 68 Conn. App. 884, 793 A.2d 274 (2002), was to the contrary, it was overruled; 5) the trial court presided over the probation violation hearing in a fair and evenhanded manner, and the record revealed no manifest injustice; 6) the totality of the record demonstrated that defendant received a fair trial on the § 53a-167a(a) charges, and there was no vindictiveness in defendant's sentence; 7) defendant knowingly waived his right to counsel; and 8) the multiple § 53a-167a(a) charges did not constitute double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgments were reversed and the cases were remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgments of the trial court.

Lebron v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 17209


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 507; 876 A.2d 1178; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 286


March 7, 2005, Argued  
July 26, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Lebron v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 280 (Conn. App. Ct., May 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Fuger, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Bishop and McLachlan, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Lebron v. Comm'r of Corr., 82 Conn. App. 475, 844 A.2d 946, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 156 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his conviction and the sentence imposed. The trial court granted a motion to dismiss by respondent, an agency, and rendered judgment thereon. The prisoner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Connecticut Appellate Court, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the prisoner, on the granting of certification, appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of assault in the third degree and was sentenced to a term of six months. After serving the sentence, the prisoner pled guilty to a charge of manslaughter. In the habeas corpus petition, the prisoner argued that he received ineffective assistance of counsel during the proceedings on the assault charge and that the assault conviction was used to enhance the sentence on the manslaughter charge. The trial court dismissed the motion on grounds that it lacked jurisdiction because the prisoner had already served the sentence. The prisoner argued that the collateral consequences of the assault conviction were sufficient to render him in custody within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-466. The state supreme court held that a petitioner whose conviction had expired fully prior to the filing of a habeas corpus petition was not in "custody" on that conviction, despite the alleged existence of collateral consequences flowing from that conviction. Although the custody requirement had been construed liberally, it had never been extended to the situation where a habeas petitioner suffered no present restraint from a conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pink


(SC 16971)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 241; 875 A.2d 447; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 255


November 29, 2004, Argued  
July 5, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute informations charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, tampering with physical evidence, conspiracy to commit murder and to tamper with evidence, criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, threatening in the second degree, tampering with a witness and intimidating a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the informations were joined, and where the court, Gordon, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and granted the state's motions for protective orders to preclude the defendant from gaining access to certain other evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Dyer, J.; verdict and judgments of guilty, and sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; the appeal subsequently was transferred to this court, which treated the defendant's motion for articulation as a motion for review and granted the motion as to the denial of the motion to suppress; thereafter, the court, Gordon, J., issued an articulation of the decision denying the defendant's motion to suppress.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a (a), tampering with evidence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-155 (a)(1), and conspiracy to commit murder and to tamper with evidence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48 (a).


OVERVIEW: The victim was last seen leaving a cafe with defendant's accomplice. Two years later, defendant made an unscheduled visit to his probation officer, and the men had a conversation wherein defendant stated that he had shot the victim in the head. He also indicated that he and another man had stabbed the victim and that "they" had taken the body behind a building before moving it to the woods. Towards the end of defendant's murder trial, the State indicated that it had discovered a police report containing information gathered from a confidential informant that defendant's accomplice had bragged about killing the victim. Defendant unsuccessfully moved for a mistrial on the ground that the report constituted exculpatory evidence within the meaning of Brady. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the State's untimely disclosure did not violate defendant's constitutional right to a fair trial or to due process because the trial court granted a continuance to allow him to review the materials and to attempt to locate the accomplice. Further, the court noted that defendant did not explain how the late disclosures forced him to reformulate his trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

184 Windsor Ave., LLC v. State


(SC 17243)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 302; 875 A.2d 498; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 256



July 5, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged breach of a lease agreement, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Housing Session, where the court, A. dos Santos, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.
184 Windsor Ave., LLC v. State, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 828 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 1, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed its action for damages and declaratory relief against appellee State of Connecticut. The property owner had alleged that the State's failure to pay rent due under a tax escalation clause of a lease agreement between the parties constituted a breach of contract and an uncompensated taking.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's predecessor entered into two leases with the State for the use of two suites by the state education board. Both leases contained tax escalation clauses. The State's representative signed amended lease agreements. However, the State refused to pay the additional sums it allegedly owed under the tax escalation clauses and expressed an unwillingness to make such payments in the future. The education board continued to occupy the property owner's premises. The appellate court held the language of the relevant statutes, including Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-61, 4-142, 4-158, and 4-159, did not provide any waiver of sovereign immunity with respect to the lease agreements. In light of Connecticut's express statutory scheme, the trial court properly granted the motion to dismiss with regard to the contract claim. The property owner's takings claim was similarly unavailing because the State's failure to pay the full amount of rent allegedly due was not, as a matter of law, a taking. The trial court properly concluded that the tax escalation clause was an invalid lease term because it had not been approved by the review board pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4b-23(e).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ.


(SC 17184)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


274 Conn. 92; 874 A.2d 742; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 214


November 29, 2004, Argued  
June 14, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ., 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8394 (U.S., Nov. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a certain state statute vesting regional boards of education with the authority to determine and to assess the amount that each town in their respective regional districts must pay for educational expenses, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, DiPentima, J., granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by the town of Salisbury; thereafter, the court, Cremins, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Richard Blumenthal and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the plaintiffs' action, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the appeal was transferred to this court, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a hearing with respect to the issue of the plaintiffs' standing as taxpayers; subsequently, the trial court, DiPentima, J., granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by the town of Canaan and the plaintiff Thomas R. Coolidge et al. withdrew from the action; on remand, the court, Black, J., following an evidentiary hearing, granted the defendants'  [***2] motion to dismiss for lack of standing and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the action, from which the named plaintiff et al. appealed.
Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2637 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 22, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which granted the motion to dismiss for lack of standing of defendants, a regional school district and two towns. The taxpayers had brought a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-51(b), which authorized regional boards of education to determine and assess educational expenses per town.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers had essentially argued that the total educational expenses of the regional school district divided by the number of a town's resident students served deprived the taxpayers, who were from a relatively property tax poor town, of their state and federal constitutional rights to due process of law and equal protection of the laws. The taxpayers asserted that the only way in which that alleged unconstitutionality was subject to remedy was to make the regional school district into a single taxing district for the purposes of education, with a uniform mill rate. The trial court had determined that the taxpayers' suit asserted a political question and, therefore, the taxpayers lacked standing. The court agreed and upheld the dismissal. Though the court found clear error as to the trial court's factual findings that the taxpayers paid approximately the same in property taxes as similarly situated taxpayers, the taxpayers failed to demonstrate that they suffered any kind of injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Lewis


SC 17283


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


273 Conn. 509; 871 A.2d 986; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 156


March 11, 2005, Argued  
May 10, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with, inter alia, the crime of violation of the Home Improvement Act, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, Rodriguez, J., granted in part the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(8) for failing to refund the payment for a home improvement within 10 days of a written request. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the information. The State appealed to the Appellate Court (Connecticut). The state supreme court transferred the appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the State argued that the trial court improperly granted the motion to dismiss without holding an evidentiary hearing. Specifically, the State argued that a hearing was required because the State neither stipulated to the admissibility or accuracy of the documents that defendant attached to his motion nor conceded that the evidence in the arrest warrant application would constitute its entire proof. Defendant's claim was that a home improvement contractor of ordinary intelligence would not have had fair warning that his conduct was proscribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-427(b)(8). Accordingly, to establish the unconstitutionality of the statute as applied to him, it was incumbent on defendant to present a factual record demonstrating how the statute was in fact applied to him. The state supreme court concluded that the trial court improperly granted defendant's motion to dismiss. In the absence of either undisputed facts, concessions by the State that the arrest warrant application constituted the pertinent evidence in its entirety, or a full evidentiary hearing, the trial court could not have made the factual findings essential to a determination of the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to deny defendant's motion to dismiss, and for further proceedings according to law.

State v. Wright


(SC 17239)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


273 Conn. 418; 870 A.2d 1039; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 126


January 5, 2005, Argued  
April 19, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of interfering with an officer and criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, and tried to the jury before White, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of criminal violation of a protective order, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which found him guilty of one count of criminal violation of a protective order (CVPO) in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-110b (1999), as amended by 1999 Conn. Acts 240, § 4, and codified as amended at Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-223.


OVERVIEW: As a condition of defendant's release on charges of assaulting his girlfriend's sister, a protective order was issued under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-38c (1999) that barred him from contacting the sister or entering an apartment where she sometimes resided but which was also the apartment he shared with the girlfriend. He violated that order and was charged with CVPO. At trial, defendant was precluded from introducing evidence that the sister was not a member of his household and did not qualify for the protective order that was issued. On appeal of his conviction, defendant claimed that he was deprived of his U.S. Const. amend. VI and XIV right to present a defense, that the State was required to prove the validity of the order, and that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to counsel was deprived at the protective order hearing. The court found that the collateral bar rule prevented defendant from attacking the validity of the protective order at his CVPO trial and that validity of the order was not an element of CVPO. His challenge based on the lack of counsel at the protective order hearing was also an impermissible collateral attack on that order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal violation of a protective order.
