State v. Robert H.


SC 16873


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


273 Conn. 56; 866 A.2d 1255; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 54


September 10, 2004, Argued  
March 8, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and one count of the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the court, A. Robinson, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Dranginis and Hennessy, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty on three counts of risk of injury to a child, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Robert H., 71 Conn. App. 289, 802 A.2d 152, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 409 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certification to an appeal by the State from a judgment of the Appellate Court of Connecticut that set aside convictions on three of five counts on which defendant had been convicted in connection with misconduct with his granddaughters. The convictions that were set aside on grounds of insufficiency of evidence involved charges of risk of injury to a child under the "act" prong of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53.21(1) (Rev. to 1997).


OVERVIEW: The court noted that while § 53.21 had been amended several times in preceding years, none of the changes affected the gloss that its case law had placed on § 53.21(1)'s proscription of acts creating a risk of injury to a child, so that to avoid unconstitutional vagueness, that proscription had to be read as involving some sort of acts of physical touching. While the conduct involved in the three counts that had been reversed was reprehensible, there was no physical contact with the victims, so prosecution under that theory failed. At trial, one of the victims mentioned another incident that had involved physical contact, but the State had not known about that incident before, so that it was not part of its theory of the case. It would have violated defendant's due process rights to allow the State to change its theory liability on appeal, so the evidence relied on at trial had to be sufficient to support conviction under the "act" prong, as opposed to the "situation" prong of that subsection, and there could be no reliance on evidence that had not been the focus of the State's case at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

263 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Teresa T. v. Ragaglia


(SC 17033)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 734; 865 A.2d 428; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 26


September 23, 2004, Argued  
February 8, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, violations of the plaintiffs' civil rights as a result of the alleged negligence of the defendants in failing to protect the plaintiffs from domestic physical abuse by removing them from their home, and for other relief, brought to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut, where the court, Covello, J., granted, in part, the defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint, and the plaintiffs, with permission to pursue an interlocutory appeal of the District Court's order of dismissal, appealed to the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit, F. I. Parker, Straub and Sack, Js., which certified to this court certain questions of law regarding the scope of the defendants' obligation regarding the removal of children from their home following a finding of probable cause to believe that they were subject to an imminent risk of physical harm.
Sealed v. Sealed, 332 F.3d 51, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 11720 (2d Cir. Conn., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff children's federal action for civil rights damages from defendant Commissioner of the Department of Children and Families, the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit certified two questions of law regarding the scope of the commissioner's obligation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101g(c) to remove the children from their home after finding probable cause to believe they were under an imminent risk of physical harm.


OVERVIEW: The children brought an action in federal court against the commissioner due to the failure to remove them from their home though there was probable cause to believe their stepfather was being physically abusive. Procedural due process claims were dismissed by the federal district court and an interlocutory appeal of that order was allowed. The federal appellate court certified two questions. The first was whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101g(c) required the commissioner to remove the children if probable cause existed to believe they were in imminent risk of physical harm. The second was, if the commissioner authorized removal, whether the commissioner's designated employees were required, or merely authorized, to remove the children. The court held that despite the use of the word "shall" in § 17a-101g(c), the statute granted the commissioner discretionary authority to remove the children, along with a host of other options. Removal was not mandated. Moreover, even if the commissioner authorized removal under § 17a-101g(c), Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17a-101-13(b) allowed the designated employees discretion on whether to remove the children.


OUTCOME: The court answered both certified questions in the negative, holding that the commissioner had discretionary authority, and was not mandated, to remove the children and that even if the commissioner authorized removal, the designated employees or law enforcement personnel were not statutorily required to remove the children.

In re Ross


SC 17342, SC 17343


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 676; 866 A.2d 554; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 45


January 21, 2005, Argued  
January 27, 2005, Officially Released * 


* January 27, 2005, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 5, 2005.
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Ross v. Lantz, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 908 (D. Conn., Jan. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Ross, 272 Conn. 674, 866 A.2d 541, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 24 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in error, the office of the chief public defender (PD) and the next friend of defendant who was condemned to the death penalty (next friend), brought separate writs of error, challenging orders of a habeas court (Connecticut), which dismissed their respective petitions for a writ of habeas corpus on behalf of defendant. The PD and the next friend also filed motions to stay defendant's execution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant exhausted his appellate process for a death sentence, including the mandatory review provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46b (1987). The PD and the next friend sought next friend status to pursue postconviction relief on his behalf, including participation in an ongoing consolidated habeas litigation based on racial bias that was filed for other defendants who were sentenced to death. The habeas court dismissed the petitions and the court dismissed their writs of error, finding that they lacked standing. Petitions to stay defendant's execution pending the consolidated habeas litigation thereby became moot. The court determined that, while § 53a-46b required review of defendant's sentence, the statute did not create a non-waivable right to review of any postconviction claims, regardless of when and by whom the claim was raised. During the entire 20 years of defendant's litigation, he never claimed that his death sentence was the product of systemic racial bias and he expressly stated that he did not wish to participate in the consolidated litigation. Defendant's waiver of those issues prevented the PD and the next friend from obtaining standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders dismissing the PD's and the next friend's petitions for writs of habeas corpus on behalf of defendant and, therefore, dismissed their writs of error challenging those dismissal orders. The court dismissed the motions to stay defendant's execution as moot.

 

265 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Denardo v. Bergamo


(SC 17200)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 500; 863 A.2d 686; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 5


October 18, 2004, Argued  
January 18, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the plaintiff father for custody and visitation rights relative to the parties' minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where Richard S. Denardo, Sr., et al., the minor child's paternal grandparents, intervened as plaintiffs and where the court, Kenefick, J., granted them certain visitation rights with the child; thereafter, following several modifications by the court, Leheny, J., of the intervening plaintiffs' visitation rights, Hon. Romeo G. Petroni, judge trial referee, granted the defendant mother's motion to modify and terminate visitation by the intervening plaintiffs, vacated the previous order of visitation and terminated the intervening plaintiffs' visitation rights, and the intervening plaintiffs appealed.
DeNardo v. Bergamo, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3435 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sought custody and visitation rights relative to a minor child, in the Superior Court, Waterbury Judicial District (Connecticut). The child's paternal grandparents intervened and were granted visitation rights. Following several modifications of the grandparents' visitation rights, defendant mother's motion to modify and terminate visitation by the grandparents was granted. The grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's retrospective application of the court's decision in Roth was proper. Roth applied equally irrespective of whether a grandparent moved to secure an initial order of visitation or a parent moved to modify such an order, and the grandparents' failure to satisfy the Roth standards mandated termination of the visitation order. Because the grandparents were not the child's legal guardians, and the child's interests were represented by an attorney, the grandparents could not assert the child's legal rights. The trial court was compelled to grant the motion to terminate visitation. The grandparents failed to allege or attempt to prove that their relationship with the child was similar to a parent-child relationship and denial of visitation would cause real and significant harm to the child. Without those specific, good faith allegations or such proof, the trial court's prior order of visitation was rendered without subject matter jurisdiction. Accordingly, the mother's motion to modify and terminate the grandparents' visitation rights properly was granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

266 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ross


(SC 17335)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 577; 863 A.2d 654; 2005 Conn. LEXIS 19



January 14, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Missionary Soc'y of Conn. v. Bd. of Pardons & Paroles, 272 Conn. 647, 866 A.2d 538, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 44 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Writ dismissed by In re Ross, 272 Conn. 653, 866 A.2d 542, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 25 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] January 14, 2005, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes. Writ of error from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, Cliffford, J., denying the motion by the office of the chief public defender for permission to appear in the litigation of this matter. Orders affirmed; writ of error dismissed.
State v. Ross, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3757 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 15, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error, the office of the chief public defender of Connecticut (office), brought a writ of error to challenge the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London's (Connecticut) denial of its motion for permission to appear as next friend of a criminal defendant and as a party in interest, an intervenor or amicus curiae in postconviction judicial proceedings in three criminal cases against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of six counts of capital felony and sentenced to death. The office claimed the trial court improperly denied its motion to appear as defendant's next friend without providing the opportunity to present evidence and to cross-examine witnesses at defendant's competency hearing. The supreme court found the office had not presented any meaningful evidence that defendant was incompetent within the meaning of Demosthenes v. Baal. In the absence of such evidence, the office was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing at which it could attempt to establish defendant's incompetence and its standing to appear as next friend under Whitmore v. Arkansas. Accordingly, the office's motion to appear as next friend was denied. The office also claimed the trial court abused its discretion by denying its motion to appear as an amicus curiae. The supreme court disagreed. The office had not cited a single authority directly supporting its argument that a court was required to grant a request to appear as amicus curiae if the parties to a proceeding had taken nonadversarial positions on an issue on which the person seeking to be admitted as an amicus curiae took an opposing view.


OUTCOME: The orders of the trial court denying the office's motion to appear as defendant's next friend and its request to appear as amicus curiae were affirmed and the writ of error was dismissed.

 

267 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Colon


(SC 16446)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 106; 864 A.2d 666; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 527


October 30, 2003, Argued  
December 28, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Colon v. Connecticut, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6418 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the state filed a notice of the aggravating factors that it intended to prove during the penalty phase of the proceedings and where the court, D'Addabbo, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found the existence of an aggravating factor and one or more mitigating factors and that the aggravating factor did not outweigh the mitigating factor or factors, and the court accepted the verdict; after being informed of a mistake by the jury on the verdict form, the court reassembled and polled the jury, which indicated that it had found that the aggravating factor did outweigh the mitigating factor or factors; the jury thereafter returned a second verdict form finding the existence of an aggravating factor and one or more mitigating factors and that the aggravating factor outweighed the mitigating factor or factors; subsequently, the court vacated the jury's [***2] initial verdict, accepted the second verdict and merged the two charges of the information; thereafter, the court, D'Addabbo, J., and Damiani, J., denied the defendant's various postverdict motions and the court, D'Addabbo, J., rendered judgment of guilty of capital felony and sentenced the defendant to death, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Colon, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3549 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 14, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Conviction of capital felony and murder affirmed; death sentence judgment reversed and case remanded to trial court for new penalty phase hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) convicting him of capital murder and murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: The victim, a two-year-old child, was beaten to death. Defendant, the boyfriend of the victim's mother, was convicted of murder and capital murder, and was sentenced to death. Defendant challenged the conviction and the sentence raising numerous points of alleged error. The court noted that the pervasive standard of review with regard to all of defendant's points of error was whether the trial court abused its discretion. The court concluded that under all the circumstances the trial court did not abuse its discretion in any ruling made during the trial process. However, with regard to the penalty phase of the trial, the court found reversible error. The court held that the jury instructions given in the penalty phase, namely that the jury must be persuaded beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating factor or factors outweighed the mitigating factor or factors and that, therefore, it was persuaded beyond a reasonable doubt that death was the appropriate punishment, did not conform to the judicial system's rigid standards. Accordingly, reversal of the sentence was mandated. The conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the death sentence was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

268 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Allard


(SC 17175)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


272 Conn. 1; 860 A.2d 1223; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 520


September 21, 2004, Argued  
December 7, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to correct an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, D. Michael Hurley, judge trial referee, granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by the department of consumer protection; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Martin, J.; judgment denying the application to correct the award, from which the plaintiff appealed.
DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Allard, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2649 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car company sought to correct an arbitration award which awarded appellee buyer a new vehicle under the lemon law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179 et seq. The car company appealed the determination by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) which denied the application to correct the award. The car company argued the new vehicle was not comparable to the defective vehicle.


OVERVIEW: The buyer purchased a vehicle which experienced several serious problems with its first 24,000 miles of operation, including noise from the muffler and a banging noise from the transmission. As a result, the buyer had the vehicle serviced on eight separate occasions during its first 24,000 miles of operation, rendering it unusable for a total of approximately 35 days. The repairs included replacing the transmission, readjusting the rear hatch, and replacing the air conditioning system. After the vehicle surpassed the 24,000 mile mark, the buyer experienced further problems, including gas seeping into the passenger compartment and continued banging in the transmission. The arbitration panel found the buyer was entitled to relief under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179 et seq., and ordered the car company to accept return of the buyer's defective vehicle and furnish her with a new vehicle. The appellate court held there was substantial evidence in the record of the arbitration proceeding to support the panel's finding that the replacement vehicle awarded was comparable to the buyer's original vehicle where there was no exact replacement. Thus, the trial court properly upheld the award.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

269 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirk R.


(SC 16940)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


271 Conn. 499; 857 A.2d 908; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 463


March 11, 2004, Argued  
October 19, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Mihalakos and Bishop, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defen dant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court. Affirmed. 
State v. Kirk R., 74 Conn. App. 376, 812 A.2d 113, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 658 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the court's grant of certification, defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant, convicting him of two counts of sexual assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2) (1997), and two counts of risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(2) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from certain incidents involving his two minor stepdaughters. Defendant contended on appeal that the appellate court improperly concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(b) (1997), which provided for a mandatory minimum sentence of 10 years imprisonment if a victim was less than 10 years of age, did not require a finding by the jury, as opposed to a finding by the sentencing court, that the victims were in fact less than 10 years of age. The court agreed with defendant that the issue of whether the victims were less than 10 years of age should have been submitted to the jury. However, the court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court upon determining that the absence of such a jury finding was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt in the case. The court found that it was beyond a reasonable doubt that the victims were less than 10 years of age and their age was never contested by defendant. The fact that there was overwhelming evidence of the victims' age, coupled with defendant's failure to contest the issue at any time, made the trial court's error harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

270 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perkins


(SC 17099)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


271 Conn. 218; 856 A.2d 917; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 365



September 28, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle, misconduct with a motor vehicle and evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before Kavanewsky, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle, misconduct with a motor vehicle, and evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle. Defendant asserted, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his motion for acquittal and for a new trial, and that the waiver rule was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim had been drinking prior to leaving in defendant's car. The car skidded off the wet road and the victim was killed. Defendant left the scene of the accident and called his supervisor to pick him up. Witnesses testified defendant did not appear to be intoxicated. Defendant's motion for acquittal was denied. Defendant then presented a witness who testified that defendant had told him that he had consumed one and one-half beers and three glasses of scotch on the evening of the accident. The appellate court concluded that the waiver rule was not unconstitutional and it saw no persuasive reason not to apply it in defendant's case. On the basis of all of the evidence presented to the jury, there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The waiver rule simply was one of a myriad of considerations that defendant had to take into account when planning his defense. Although defendant's statements regarding his desire to be taken back to the accident site fell within the state of mind exception to the hearsay rule, they were not improperly excluded by the trial court because they were irrelevant to the charge of evading responsibility.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

271 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bloom v. Gershon


(SC 17030), (SC 17031), (SC 17032)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


271 Conn. 96; 856 A.2d 335; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 360



September 14, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, medical malpractice, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Hon. Mary R. Hennessey, judge trial referee, granted the plaintiffs' motion to cite in Mandell and Blau, P.C., as a party defendant; thereafter, the defendants filed an apportionment complaint against Kevin Shea et al., and the plaintiffs amended their complaint to include claims against the defendant Kevin Shea et al.; subsequently, the state claims commissioner filed an appearance as an interested party, and the defendant Henry Maresh filed an apportionment complaint against the state of Connecticut and an application for a writ of mandamus to require the claims commissioner to authorize an action against the defendant Kevin Shea; the court thereafter denied the defendant Kevin Shea's motion to dismiss the medical malpractice claim and the apportionment complaint against him, denied the defendant state of Connecticut's motion to dismiss the apportionment complaint filed against it by the defendant Henry Maresh, and granted the defendant Henry Maresh's application for a writ of mandamus, and rendered judgment thereon,  [***2] and the defendant Kevin Shea, the state claims commissioner and the defendant state of Connecticut filed separate appeals to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the appeals were transferred to this court.
Bloom v. Gershon, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 432 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice action by plaintiff patient against defendant, apportionment plaintiff radiologists, the court transferred to itself from the Connecticut Appellate Court an appeal by apportionment defendants, a state employee, the State, and its claims commissioner (collectively, the State), from orders that denied the State's motion to dismiss and issued a writ of mandamus compelling the commissioner to allow such a complaint.


OVERVIEW: The patient alleged that the radiologists negligently failed to detect his lung cancer and the radiologists in turn argued that certain state employees' negligence was largely to blame, and they filed a complaint for apportionment of liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-102b. Since the State had not legislatively waived immunity in medical malpractice actions, they sought a waiver of sovereign immunity from the claims commissioner under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160, and then one of the state employees further sought such a waiver to allow him to seek apportionment of liability against the State directly. While the matter was pending, the State's highest court decided that § 4-160 allowed the commissioner to authorize only suits seeking monetary awards, not apportionments of liability. In light of that decision, the commissioner clearly lacked jurisdiction to authorize the apportionment actions against the State and its employees as well. Therefore, none of the relief sought in the trial court should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter to that court with directions to deny requests for declaratory and mandamus relief and to grant the State's motions to dismiss the apportionment complaints.

State v. DeJesus


(SC 16782)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 826; 856 A.2d 345; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 355


April 21, 2004, Argued  
September 7, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Espinosa, J., granted the state's motion in limine to exclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court; subsequently, the trial court denied the defendant's motion for rectification and this court granted the defendant's motion for review of that denial but denied the relief requested, and the defendant filed an amended appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut) that convicted defendant sexual assault and kidnapping, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-70(a)(1) and 53a-92(a)(2)(A), respectively. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in excluding evidence pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86f as irrelevant and as having insufficient probative value.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a motion in limine requesting that the trial court prohibit defendant from presenting evidence that the victim had engaged in prostitution, without a prior judicial ruling on the admissibility of such evidence. Defendant claimed that the trial court deprived him of his constitutional rights to confront witnesses against him and to present a defense by precluding him from questioning the victim about her prior history of prostitution. The State claimed that this evidence was irrelevant and prejudicial to the State's case. The State also claimed that the introduction of that evidence would violate Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86f, the rape shield statute. Because the primary issue was whether the sexual intercourse was consensual, any evidence that was so relevant and material to the issue of consent that excluding it would have violated defendant's constitutional rights was admissible under § 54-86f (4). Further, defendant's knowledge of her prostitution on prior occasions was sufficiently relevant to the issue of consent, in that it supported defendant's claim that the victim consented to the sexual intercourse and suggested a motive for the victim to testify falsely.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and a new trial was ordered.

River Bend Assocs. v. Zoning Comm'n


(SC 17026)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


271 Conn. 1; 856 A.2d 973; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 356


March 10, 2004, Argued  
September 7, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at River Bend Assocs. v. Planning Comm'n, 271 Conn. 41, 856 A.2d 959, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 353 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiffs' application for a zone change and master site plan approval for the construction of a residential development, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Shortall, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiffs' appeal subject to certain conditions, from which the named defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed.
River Bend Assocs. v. Conservation & Inland Wetlands Comm'n, 269 Conn. 57, 848 A.2d 395, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 194 (2004)
River Bend Assocs. v. Simsbury Water Pollution Control Auth., 262 Conn. 84, 809 A.2d 492, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 441 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning commission appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), where the trial court sustained plaintiff owners' appeal. The commission had denied the owners' application for certain amendments to the zoning regulations, zoning map, and a master site plan, all relating to the construction of an affordable housing development within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-30g.


OVERVIEW: The owners submitted an application to the zoning commission for an amendment to the town zoning regulations in order to create a new housing opportunity development district and an amendment to the town zoning map, rezoning the property to the new district. Ultimately, all of the applications were denied. Initially, as part of the application process, the water pollution control authority voted to deny the sewer connections on the ground that 55 of the residences with septic systems were located within the sewer service area and, if any of the septic systems failed, connection to the sewer system would be required. Additionally, the commission was entitled to consider whether the more intense use of the land proposed by the owners created a risk to the public health that otherwise would not have existed. However, evidence of a mere possibility of harm did not constitute sufficient evidence that a substantial public interest was threatened for purposes of § 8-30g(g). Accordingly, the zoning commission did not meet its burden under the first prong of § 8-30g(g). As such, that portion of the decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed only to the extent that it sustained the owners' appeal from the commission's denial of the site plan application. The case was remanded with directions to dismiss that portion of the owners' appeal. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities v. Bd. of Educ.


(SC 17014), (SC 17015)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 665; 855 A.2d 212; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 350


October 24, 2003, Argued  
August 31, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the commission on human rights and opportunities dismissing a complaint of racial discrimination filed by a public school student against the named defendant et al., brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal in part and remanding the matter to the commission on human rights and opportunities for further proceedings, from which the plaintiff and the named defendant et al. filed separate appeals.
Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities v. Cheshire Bd. of Educ., 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3545 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 13, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commission on human rights and opportunities (commission) challenged a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which dismissed an appeal, as to complainant student only, of a race discrimination complaint against defendants, a town board of education and a principal (board). The board appealed a judgment sustaining the appeal on jurisdiction grounds and remanding to the commission.


OVERVIEW: The student filed a racial discrimination complaint with the commission, but a presiding referee granted the board's motion to dismiss. The commission appealed. The superior court dismissed the appeal only as to the student on the ground of mootness. It sustained the commission's appeal alleging that it had jurisdiction over the student's complaint and the case was remanded to the commission. The commission challenged dismissal as to the student. The board claimed that the state education board had exclusive administrative jurisdiction over discrimination complaints in the public schools and that the remand meant no appeal was available. The court found that: (1) the remand was a final judgment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(j) for purposes of appeal; (2) the student's appeal was not moot because the commission could grant compensatory damages under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-86(c) as a remedy for discrimination; (3) the commission's authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-58(a) allowed it to correct discrimination claims in public schools under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-15c; and (4) the state board and the commission had concurrent administrative jurisdiction over such claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal regarding the student's complaint. The court affirmed the judgment sustaining the commission's jurisdiction over the student's complaint, and the court affirmed the order remanding the complaint to the commission for further proceedings.

 

275 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garner


(SC 16710)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 458; 853 A.2d 478; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 308


February 17, 2004, Argued  
August 3, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of murder and capital felony and with one count of the crime of conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hartmere, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and his motion to dismiss certain of the charges; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Hartmere, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for two counts of murder, a capital felony, and conspiracy to commit murder. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court improperly denied his motion to exclude identifications and denied his motion to dismiss the charges of murder and capital felony. Defendant also argued the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: A witness testified that another individual wished to kill the victims, a little boy and his mother, as the individual thought the boy was a witness to an attempted murder. The witness saw defendant walking back and forth in front of the victims' house. The witness was asked to help the shooter gain entrance to the victims' house. Defendant sat in a car as the shooter entered the house and killed the victims. Defendant threatened to kill the witness if she talked to anyone about the murder. The appellate court held the witness's identifications were reliable under the totality of the circumstances. The jury reasonably could have inferred that, at the time of the murders, defendant was scoping out the area for witnesses, that he knew the shooter's purpose was to kill the victims, and that he facilitated the shooter's escape. The evidence supporting the murder charges supported the conviction for conspiracy to commit murder. Because defendant had not previously been tried for the offenses, the Double Jeopardy Clause was not implicated. The extent of defendant's participation was not so attenuated that it was unjust to hold him responsible for the conduct of his coconspirator.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

UFCW, Local 919 v. Crystal Mall Assocs., L.P.


(SC 16956)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 261; 852 A.2d 659; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 304; 175 L.R.R.M. 2347


March 23, 2004, Argued  
July 27, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from denying the plaintiff access to the common areas of a shopping mall to distribute literature and to address mall patrons regarding employees' legal rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Berger, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to cite in Simon Property Group, L.P., as a party defendant; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Quinn, J., on a stipulation of facts; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a union, filed an action to enjoin defendants, the owner and manager of a shopping mall, from denying access to the common areas of a shopping mall to distribute literature and to address mall patrons regarding employees' legal rights. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), entered judgment in favor of defendants. The union appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The union claimed that the mall violated its right to freedom of speech under Conn. Const. art. I,, §§ 4 and 5, and its right to freedom of assembly under Conn. Const. art. I, § 14. The trial court determined that the mall was a private actor, and therefore, not subject to the guarantees afforded by the state constitution. The appellate court agreed that there was inadequate state action to trigger state constitutional protection. Nothing in the record suggested that the involvement of state agencies in the construction of the mall was unusual or extensive, particularly for a large commercial property. Neither the mall nor any other commercial business in the community was billed for general police patrol services, unless it is was a specific request for an extra duty job. Likewise, the state fire code applied to all municipalities within the state. An area set aside for police use at the mall did not constitute a police substation. There was no exclusive permanent police presence. Instead, officers were assigned to the mall as part of a patrol zone. There was also no evidence that the city paid for any of the improvements to the land.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Jeisean M.


SC 17012


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 382; 852 A.2d 643; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 301



July 27, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at In re Jeisean M., 270 Conn. 406, 852 A.2d 657, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 302 (Conn., July 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the parental rights of the respondents with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters, where the court, Swienton, J., rendered judgment of default against the respondent father; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Dannehy, J., as against the respondent mother; judgment terminating the respondent mother's parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed.
In re Jeisean M., 74 Conn. App. 233, 812 A.2d 80, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 641 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon a petition filed by petitioner agency commissioner, the Superior Court, in the Judicial District of Hartford, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), terminated the respondent mother's parental rights to her minor child. The mother appealed. The minor child's motion to transfer the appeal to the state's highest court, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-19(c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-2, was granted.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j) was facially unconstitutional or unconstitutional as applied to the facts of the case. The state's highest court held that the mother's challenge failed as the constitutional protection afforded parents applied to fit parents. Further, the record supported the trial court's finding that the commissioner had proved by clear and convincing evidence that the mother had failed to attain a degree of rehabilitation sufficient to warrant the belief that, at some time in the foreseeable future, she would be capable of assuming a responsible position with respect to her child's care. There was ample evidence of the mother's documented struggle with drug abuse, inability to secure and maintain adequate employment and income, inability to live independently and inexplicable absences from scheduled visits to see her son. The record was sufficient to support the trial court's finding without testimony from an expert. Finally, the trial court did not improperly conclude that clear and convincing evidence established that it was in the child's best interest to terminate the mother's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

278 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lutters


(SC 16982)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


270 Conn. 198; 853 A.2d 434; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 299


October 29, 2003, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Harper, J., denied without prejudice the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's renewed motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the information, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.
State v. Lutters, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2327 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 22, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six (Connecticut), which, after denying defendant's motion to dismiss the information charging defendant with carrying a pistol without a permit, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a), granted defendant's renewed motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: When operating his taxicab, defendant carried a handgun in a pack on his waist. Defendant did not obtain a permit for the handgun. Prior to trial, defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information, claiming that, although he had possessed a handgun without a permit as alleged, he had done so while operating a taxicab in which he had a proprietary interest, and, therefore, his possession of the handgun without a permit was not prohibited. Specifically, defendant argued that his possession met the "place of business" exception under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a). In opposing defendant's motion to dismiss, the State claimed that a taxicab was not a place of business within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35 (a). In analyzing the statute, the legislature merely intended for a taxicab driver, like any other person whose business may have relied on a motor vehicle, to obtain a permit to carry a handgun before bringing it into his or her vehicle. However, such an exemption mandated an application for a permit, which defendant did not do. Finally, such an interpretation and requirement for a permit constituted sound public policy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

279 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bergeson v. City of New London


(SC 17005)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


269 Conn. 763; 850 A.2d 184; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 235


March 8, 2004, Argued  
June 22, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the second district ordering, inter alia, that the defendant second injury fund reimburse the named defendant for certain cost of living adjustment payments made to the plaintiff on her award of survivor's benefits pursuant to the Heart and Hypertension Act, brought to the compensation review board, which reversed the commissioner's decision, and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and its insurer, appealed a decision of the workers' compensation review board, which concluded that the second injury fund was not required, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-306(a)(2)(A), to reimburse the city for cost-of-living adjustments (COLA) paid to plaintiff claimant in connection with her death benefits claim arising under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's husband, a city police officer, suffered a fatal heart attack, and the claimant was awarded survivor's benefits under the Heart and Hypertension Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c. The city had paid the claimant's benefits, including COLAs pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-306(a)(2)(A), on a without-prejudice basis. The city contended that it was entitled to reimbursement from the fund under § 31-306(a)(2)(A). Affirming the board's decision, the court held that the fund was not required to reimburse a municipal employer, like the city, for COLAs paid in connection with a claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c. Although the Workers' Compensation Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-275 et seq., was used as a procedural avenue for administration of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c benefits, an award under § 7-433c was not a workers' compensation award. Moreover, although the city had standing to challenge the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-433c and 31-306(a)(2)(A), the court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-433c and 31-306(a)(2)(A) were a rational means to further a legitimate legislative purpose and, accordingly, satisfied the requirements of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decision.

Office of the Governor v. Select Comm. of Inquiry


(SC 17211)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


269 Conn. 850; 850 A.2d 181; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 263


June 18, 2004, Argued  
June 18, 2004 *, officially released


* June 18, 2004, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in full at Office of the Governor v. Select Comm. of Inquiry, 271 Conn. 540, 858 A.2d 709, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 443 (Conn., June 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to quash a subpoena to compel the governor to testify in proceedings before the defendant investigating whether grounds exist to impeach the governor, and action to enjoin the defendant from enforcing the subpoena and to declare the enforcement of the subpoena unconstitutional as a violation of the separation of powers, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Langenbach, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss and issued a memorandum of decision denying the motion to quash and the request for injunctive and declaratory relief, and the plaintiff, upon certification from the Chief Justice that a matter of substantial public interest is at issue, appealed to this court.
Office of the Governor of Conn. v. Select Comm. of Inquiry, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1476 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 7, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; stay of subpoena vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the officer of the governor, moved to quash a subpoena to compel the governor to testify before defendant, a select committee, and to enjoin the committee from enforcing the subpoena and to declare the enforcement of the subpoena unconstitutional. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), denied the committee's motion to dismiss and denied the motion to quash. The office of the governor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The committee was investigating whether grounds existed to impeach the governor. The principal issue on appeal was whether the office of the governor was categorically immune, by virtue of Conn. Const. art. II, the separation of powers provision, from a subpoena issued by the select committee pursuant to Conn. Const. art. IX to compel the governor to testify. The state supreme court rejected the committee's jurisdictional claims, and concluded that the governor was not categorically immune from compelled testimony by this subpoena, and that the subpoena was not inconsistent with the separation of powers provision of the state constitution. The state supreme court therefore concluded that the trial court properly denied the motion by the office of the governor to quash the subpoena and for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the stay of the subpoena was vacated, effective immediately.

 

281 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Office of the Governor v. Select Comm. of Inquiry


(SC 17211)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


271 Conn. 540; 858 A.2d 709; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 443


June 18, 2004, Argued  
June 18, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to quash a subpoena to compel the governor to testify in proceedings before the defendant investigating whether grounds exist to impeach the governor, and action to enjoin the defendant from enforcing the subpoena and to declare the enforcement of the subpoena unconstitutional as a violation of the separation of powers, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Langenbach, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss and issued a memorandum of decision denying the motion to quash and the request for injunctive and declaratory relief, and the plaintiff, upon certification from the Chief Justice that a matter of substantial public interest is at issue, appealed to this court.
Office of the Governor v. Select Comm. of Inquiry, 269 Conn. 850, 850 A.2d 181, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 263 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff governor's office appealed from orders of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), that denied its motions, based primarily on separation of powers, to quash a subpoena issued by defendant select committee of the legislature to compel the governor to testify in proceedings before the committee as it considered whether to recommend impeachment and for injunctive relief against the enforcement of the subpoena.


OVERVIEW: Although the governor had resigned and the committee had disbanded after issuance of the high court's earlier summary decision, it nonetheless issued a complete opinion articulating its reasoning. First, the committee was not correct in arguing that separation of powers, under Conn. Const. art. II, as amended by Conn. Const. amend. art. XVIII, or justiciability principles prevented courts from exercising review in matters involving impeachment. Connecticut law had always allowed review of certain issues arising in impeachment settings, and since a governor, unlike other officials, faced at least temporary removal from office as soon as impeachment articles were filed, it was critical to allow review in any case where a colorable claim of constitutional violations was made. Separation of powers also, however, failed to protect the governor from the duty to comply with the efforts by the committee, primarily responsible for the initial stages of an impeachment, to carry out its constitutional duties. Federal constitutional case law suggesting that a president might be immune from judicial process in certain situations was not apt, because it did not arise in an impeachment setting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

State v. Lasaga


(SC 16707)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


269 Conn. 454; 848 A.2d 1149; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 215


October 20, 2003, Argued  
June 1, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with three counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and promoting a minor in an obscene performance, and ten counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Thompson, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Fasano, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to two counts each of sexual assault in the first degree, risk of injury to a child and promoting a minor in an obscene performance; thereafter, the remaining charges were nolled, and the court, Fasano, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Lasaga, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 25 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 2, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts each of sexual assault and promoting a minor in an obscene performance, and 10 counts of risk of injury to a child. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied. Defendant pled nolo contendere to two counts each of sexual assault, risk of injury, and promoting a minor. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) rendered judgment in accordance with the plea. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the videotapes that formed the basis for the charges against him because, inter alia, the search warrant affidavit was based on information supplied by an employee of defendant's employer who had been monitoring defendant's computer use and who defendant alleged was acting as an agent of the police. The supreme court held that the evidence sufficiently supported the trial court's finding that the employee was in no way acting as an agent of the government; the police did not seek out the employee and were not involved in his decision to obtain information regarding defendant. Defendant also claimed that the trial court violated his right to counsel under the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8, by denying his motion for a continuance to change counsel prior to the suppression hearing. The supreme court concluded that this claim was not reviewable because it neither fell within the narrow scope of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a, nor established good cause meriting a rare exception to the general rule of unreviewability of claims following a plea of nolo contendere.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Rocque v. Farricielli


(SC 17022)

269 Conn. 187; 848 A.2d 1206; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 210

Robert J. Hale, judge trial referee, issued an order of default against the defendant Hamden Salvage, Inc., et al.; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Robert J. Hale, judge trial referee; judgment permanently enjoining the named defendant et al. from, inter alia, continuing to operate their unpermitted solid waste disposal areas, imposing fines and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the court clarified its memorandum of decision and denied the motion to stay the permanent injunction pending appeal filed by the named defendant et al., and the named defendant et al. appealed.

The court found, first, that there were no internal inconsistencies in the trial court's judgment, so the due process claim failed. The court also rejected the company's argument that the definition of "solid waste" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-207(3) was unconstitutionally vague so that the company therefore did not have notice as to which waste operations required permits. Finally, the trial court made findings, properly weighed the evidence, and specifically discredited the company's arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding defendant violated the orders and imposing a civil penalty and an injunction.

State v. Ross


(SC 16328)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


269 Conn. 213; 849 A.2d 648; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 214


September 10, 2003, Argued  
June 1, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Ross, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3757 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations, in three cases, charging the defendant with eight counts of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the cases were consolidated and where the court, Hendel, J., granted, in part, the defendant's motion to dismiss and dismissed two of the four counts of capital felony in the second case; thereafter, the cases were transferred to the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of capital felony in each case; subsequently, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and the court, Ford, J., rendered judgment of guilty in each case in accordance with the verdicts and imposed the death penalty on each of the six counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which affirmed the judgments of the trial court with respect to the finding of guilt but reversed the judgments with respect to the imposition of the death penalty and remanded the cases to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing; on remand to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, the jury found aggravating [***2] factors and no mitigating factor and the court, Miano, J., imposed the death penalty on each of the six counts, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Ross, 251 Conn. 579, 742 A.2d 312, 1999 Conn. LEXIS 409 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's convictions for the 1983-1984 capital felony kidnappings, rapes, and murders of four women (four counts in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(5) and two counts in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(6)), and a remand for resentencing, a Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) found aggravating factors and no mitigating factors. The trial court imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury had evidence from which it could unanimously find (1) the aggravator that defendant's kidnapping, raping, and strangulation murders of four women were each done in an especially heinous, cruel, or depraved manner--inflicting physical or psychological pain or suffering, or both, proven beyond a reasonable doubt, and (2) no culpability statutory or non-statutory mitigator, proven by a preponderance of the evidence, and the jury recommended death. The jury members each had to find a mitigator, although not necessarily the same one, for the jury to have unanimously found a mitigator requiring the trial court to impose a life sentence, but no jury member found that defendant proved even one mitigator to possibly have obtained a mistrial. Even assuming defendant was in fact a sexual sadist, there was substantial evidence (1) that he was competent to stand trial, to understand the proceedings, and to assist counsel, and (2) that he was not so mentally impaired, under the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(g)(2) (Rev. to 1987) mitigator (a test requiring less proof than the guilt phase insanity defense), such that he could not have conformed his behavior to social norms.


OUTCOME: The highest court (1) found no error committed during the penalty phase hearing, (2) defined the population of cases to use in its required proportionality review, compared the facts and sentences in those cases to the facts and death penalty imposed upon defendant in the instant matter, and concluded defendant's death penalty was proportionate, and (3) affirmed the judgments imposing the death penalty for each count of capital felony.

State v. Cruz


(SC 16990)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


269 Conn. 97; 848 A.2d 445; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 205



May 25, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Thompson, J.; verdict of guilty of one count of assault in the first degree; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Mihalakos and Dranginis, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Cruz, 75 Conn. App. 500, 816 A.2d 683, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 83 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) that affirmed a trial court decision convicting defendant of assault, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1). On appeal, defendant argued that the lower court improperly concluded that defendant could not prevail on the merits of an unpreserved challenge to a jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the defendant claimed that he was acting in self-defense when he stabbed the victim and, therefore, his use of force was justified. Defendant testified that he stabbed the victim, but that he believed that his use of force was necessary to defend himself from the victim's attack. At the conclusion of the evidence, defendant submitted a request to charge on the issue of self-defense. In its self-defense charge, the trial court included the exact language that defendant had requested. After the court excused the jury to begin its deliberations, the court asked counsel if there were any objections to the jury charge. Defense counsel indicated that he had no objection. By affirmatively requesting language of deadly force to the exclusion of language of non-deadly force, defendant induced the claimed error. As such, defendant failed to satisfy the third prong of Golding because he has failed to establish that a constitutional violation clearly existed and clearly deprived him of a fair trial because the challenged jury instruction repeated the exact language that the defendant had requested.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

286 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lagassey v. State


(SC 16986)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


268 Conn. 723; 846 A.2d 831; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 183


December 1, 2003, Argued  
May 4, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Summary judgment granted by Lagassey v. State, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2810 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for medical malpractice in connection with the death of the plaintiff's decedent while in the care of state medical employees, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Beach, J., granted the state's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Lagassey v. State, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 226 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a decedent's estate's executor, sued defendant State of Connecticut after 1996 Conn. Acts 16 (Spec. Sess.) authorized her suit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148. The Hartford, Connecticut, Superior Court granted the State's motion to dismiss based on the suit being untimely under § 4-148 and 1996 Conn. Acts 16 (Spec. Sess.) being an unconstitutional exclusive public emolument under Conn. Const. art. I, § 1. The executor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died at a hospital owned and operated by the State in 1992 from complications involving an aneurysm that grew in size and ruptured. The suit alleged negligence. The executor had been first informed that the State's medical treatment was proper, and then later learned from a specialist that there might have been malpractice. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148 provided a time limit for a suit against the State, which the highest court redefined in detail. Generally, the Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-148(a), 52-584 limitation period for actions in negligence began to run on the date when the injury was first discovered or in the exercise of reasonable care should have been discovered. The term "injury" was synonymous with "legal injury" or "actionable harm." "Actionable harm" occurred when the executor discovered, or, in the exercise of reasonable care, should have discovered the "essential elements" of a cause of action. After defining the remainder of the test, the highest court decided the executor pleaded discovery sufficiently to survive a motion to dismiss. As the suit was not untimely as a matter of law, 1996 Conn. Acts 16 (Spec. Sess.) did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 1.


OUTCOME: The highest court decided that (1) the executor's suit was not untimely as a matter of law under the limitations statutes for suits against the State, (2) the special act was not an unconstitutional public emolument, and (3) the motion to dismiss was not to be granted, and reversed the judgment and remanded the suit for further proceedings, which included to determine if, in fact, the suit was timely based on discovery of a legal injury.

In re Samantha C.


(SC 16890)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


268 Conn. 614; 847 A.2d 883; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 167


September 24, 2003, Argued  
April 27, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the parental rights of the respondents with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Juvenile Matters, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the case was tried to the court, Levin, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondents appealed.
In re Samantha C., 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2332 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 18, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), granting the petition of petitioner commissioner of children and families to terminate their parental rights with respect to their minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the parents failed to achieve sufficient rehabilitation, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B)(ii), and, accordingly, granted the petition. In doing so, however, the trial court expressly drew an adverse inference against the parents for their failure to testify at the termination proceeding. The supreme court found the evidence credited by the trial court adequately supported its conclusion that the parents failed to achieve sufficient rehabilitation. There was adequate evidence on which the trial court could have concluded the department had made reasonable efforts to reunify the family. Because Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 34-1(f) (2001) (repealed and replaced by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 32a-1(e)) was designed to implement its statutory counterparts, it did not prohibit an adverse inference from being drawn against the parents. However, the trial court was required to give them prior notice of its intent to draw such an inference. They were entitled to be notified by the court of the prospect that an adverse inference might be drawn from their silence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new termination proceeding.

State v. Long


SC 16899


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


268 Conn. 508; 847 A.2d 862; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 192


October 22, 2003, Argued  
April 27, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Long v. Connecticut, 543 U.S. 969, 125 S. Ct. 424, 160 L. Ed. 2d 340, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7300 (2004)
On remand at, Objection overruled by State v. Long, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Long, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2883 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 3, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court (Connecticut) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the State's petition for recommitment based on its conclusion that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) was unconstitutional. Rather than pursue a civil commitment, the State appealed from the trial court's judgment of dismissal to the Appellate Court (Connecticut). The state supreme court granted the State's motion to transfer the appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c), which governed the recommitment of insanity acquittees. The statute permitted a court to extend the commitment of an acquittee past his initial term of commitment if his discharge would constitute a danger to himself or others. The state supreme court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c), as applied to defendant, provided him with periodic judicial review sufficient to satisfy his state procedural due process rights. In addition, defendant had standing to bring equal protection challenges. His federal equal protection rights were not violated because a rational basis existed for the disparate treatment accorded an acquittee and a civilly committed inmate. Because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) discriminated among, rather than between, the protected class of psychiatrically disabled individuals, Connecticut judicial decisions required review of the statute under a rational basis standard, rather than a strict scrutiny standard. Because a rational basis existed for the disparate treatment under federal equal protection, defendant's state equal protection guarantees were also necessarily satisfied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Spencer


(SC 17045)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


268 Conn. 575; 848 A.2d 1183; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 166



April 27, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Connecticut v. Spencer, 543 U.S. 957, 125 S. Ct. 409, 160 L. Ed. 2d 320, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7147 (2004)
Motion granted by Spencer v. City of Stamford, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28809 (D. Conn., Apr. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Hickey, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Hickey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of narcotics, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after the trial court denied his motion to suppress evidence, was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of possession of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers were notified that a parcel containing marijuana was being delivered at an address to a certain person. The address appeared to be a multifamily house, with no record of that person there. The officers took possession of the parcel and made a controlled delivery of the parcel to the house. Defendant answered the door and told an officer that he would accept the package. Police officers then arrested defendant, and, while standing in a common hallway of the house, the officers observed that defendant's apartment door was approximately six inches ajar. They asked defendant whether anyone was in the apartment, but received no response. The officers entered the apartment and, in defendant's bedroom, they observed in plain view on top of defendant's bed a homemade crack pipe, a dinner plate containing crack cocaine residue, and a rolled up $ 1 bill containing crack cocaine. On appeal, the court found that based on the totality of all the facts and the reasonable inferences drawn therefrom, the warrantless search of defendant's apartment was not a justifiable protective sweep. Therefore, suppression of the evidence found therein was warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to grant defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

Kelo v. City of New London


(SC 16742)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


268 Conn. 1; 843 A.2d 500; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 54


December 2, 2002, Argued  
March 9, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Kelo v. City of New London, 542 U.S. 965, 125 S. Ct. 27, 159 L. Ed. 2d 857, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5008 (2004)
Affirmed by Kelo v. City of New London, 545 U.S. 469, 125 S. Ct. 2655, 162 L. Ed. 2d 439, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5011 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory and injunctive relief to prohibit the defendants from taking by eminent domain for municipal development purposes certain real properties owned by the plaintiffs, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the court, Corradino, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiffs and in part for the defendants permitting the taking of certain of the properties, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendants cross appealed.
Kelo v. City of New London, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 789 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 13, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory and injunctive relief to prohibit defendants, a city and a development company, from taking by eminent domain properties owned by plaintiff property owners, the owners appealed and the development company cross appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) granting permanent injunctive relief to, and dismissing the pending eminent domain actions against the owners.


OVERVIEW: A municipal development plan area was approximately 90 acres in size. It included residential and commercial areas, and was comprised of approximately 115 land parcels. The development plan itself was divided into seven parcels of land. The development company voted to use the power of eminent domain to acquire properties within the development area whose owners had not been willing to sell them. After several owners objected, the appellate court construed the ambiguous term "unified land and water areas" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-186 as not being impermissibly broad. The owners claimed that the condemnation of property for economic development by private parties was inconsistent with prior public use decisions. However, municipal economic development was, in and of itself, a constitutionally valid public use under the well established broad, purposive approach. Accordingly, any private benefit from such economic development was secondary to the public benefit resulting from significant economic growth in a community. Finally, the owners did not prove that the use of eminent domain was facially unconstitutional when used in furtherance of an economic development plan.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the owners' appeal, and reversed as to the city and development company's cross-appeal.
