Pane v. City of Danbury


(SC 17041)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


267 Conn. 669; 841 A.2d 684; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 49


November 26, 2003, Argued  
March 2, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in five counts, to recover damages for, inter alia, invasion of privacy and intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress as a result of the defendants' unauthorized release of the plaintiff's personnel records, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Rush, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment as to the named defendant on all counts and as to the defendant Emanuel Merullo on counts one, two, four and five of the amended complaint, and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiff appealed; thereafter, the plaintiff withdrew count three of the amended complaint as against the defendant Emanuel Merullo.
Pane v. City of Danbury, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3360 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an employee of defendant city, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) that granted summary judgment in favor of the city on the employee's five claims that alleged defendant personnel director improperly allowed a reporter to read the employee's personnel file, pursuant to a request made under the Connecticut Freedom of Information Act (FOIA), Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The city hired the employee as a public health inspector. The personnel director received a FOIA request from a newspaper reporter to review the employee's personnel file. The director then reviewed the file to determine whether it contained any material that was unrelated to matters of legitimate public concern or contained information the disclosure of which would have been highly offensive to a reasonable person. After determining to his own satisfaction that it contained no such materials, he made the file available to the reporter. The employee's substitute complaint made no allegations as to any statute abrogating governmental immunity to the tort of invasion of privacy. Further, although the FOIA recognized certain privacy interests, the act as a whole was not intended to protect those interests. Also, the employee failed to provide any evidence that the release of her personnel file was pursuant to a final government policy or custom with regard to individual privacy rights. Finally, the employee's claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress was barred by governmental immunity, and thus, summary judgment was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

292 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turner


(SC 16711)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


267 Conn. 414; 838 A.2d 947; 2004 Conn. LEXIS 9


September 11, 2003, Argued  
January 20, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turner v. Connecticut, 543 U.S. 809, 125 S. Ct. 36, 160 L. Ed. 2d 12, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5530 (2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Appeal dismissed by Turner v. Comm'r of Corr., 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 30 (Conn. App. Ct., Jan. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Turner, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, B. Kaplan, J., on a plea of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to withdraw the plea and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Dranginis and Dupont, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to grant the defendant's motion to withdraw the guilty plea and to accept the defendant's plea of nolo contendere and to render judgment thereon, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Turner, 67 Conn. App. 708, 789 A.2d 1058, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 64 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of guilty in the trial court to sexual assault and risk of injury to a child; subsequently, the trial court denied his motion to withdraw the plea and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea. Defendant appealed. The Appellate Court of Connecticut reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with directions to grant defendant's motion to withdraw the guilty plea. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant voluntarily went to the police station. He was told several times that he was not under arrest and was free to leave at any time. He left as soon as the police finished questioning him. Defendant filed a motion to suppress a statement that he made to the police, claiming that he was not informed of his Miranda rights. On appeal, he claimed that he was denied due process of law due to ineffective assistance of counsel because his attorney did not inform him of the possibility of entering a conditional plea of nolo contendere pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a (Rev. to 1999) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 61-6, thereby preserving the right to appeal from the denial of his motion to suppress. On appeal, the court found that defendant failed to establish ineffective assistance of counsel because he failed to establish that he had nonfrivolous grounds to appeal from the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress. Defendant's interview with the police was not a custodial interrogation for Miranda purposes. Because defendant's claim on appeal was frivolous, counsel was not required to consult with defendant regarding a conditional plea of nolo contendere.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court with directions to affirm the trial court's judgment of conviction.

Burton v. Mottolese


(SC 16655)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


267 Conn. 1; 835 A.2d 998; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 488


September 9, 2003, Argued  
December 16, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Burton v. Mottolese, 541 U.S. 1073, 124 S. Ct. 2422, 158 L. Ed. 2d 983, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3867 (2004)
Related proceeding at Matter of Burton, 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1359 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Feb. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Mottolese, J., disbarring the plaintiff in error from the practice of law; thereafter, this court granted the defendant in error's motion to dismiss a portion of the writ of error. Writ of error dismissed.
Burton v. Statewide Griev. Comm., 48 Conn. Supp. 94, 830 A.2d 1205, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1371 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error, an attorney, brought a writ of error claiming that defendant in error, the trial court, improperly concluded that the attorney had violated several rules of professional conduct, and that the imposition of the sanction of disbarment violated her due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Specifically, the attorney claimed that the trial court: (1) violated her due process rights by failing to give her prior written notice of the charges against her; (2) lacked the authority to initiate disciplinary proceedings because such proceedings could be instituted only by filing a formal written complaint with the statewide grievance committee; (3) violated her due process rights because the trial court displayed actual bias toward her; (4) improperly concluded that she had engaged in professional misconduct; and (5) improperly imposed the sanction of disbarment. The appellate court found that the allegations of misconduct did not violate the attorney's due process rights. Further, the trial court properly credited the testimony of the witnesses who testified that they did not understand that, by signing a sign-up sheet, they were authorizing the attorney to bring an action in their names. The appellate court rejected the contentions that the evidence did not support the determination that the attorney violated multiple rules of professional conduct. Finally, it was clear the attorney's unauthorized representation was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The writ of error was dismissed.

 

294 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Malchik v. Div. of Crim. Justice


(SC 17016)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


266 Conn. 728; 835 A.2d 940; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 483


September 25, 2003, Argued  
December 9, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the second district dismissing as untimely the plaintiff's claim for benefits, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a detective, sought to recover workers' compensation benefits from respondents, the State, an agency, and others, for the detective's coronary artery disease. The Workers' Compensation Commissioner for the Second District dismissed the claim as untimely. The Connecticut Workers' Compensation Review Board affirmed the decision. The detective appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The detective retired in September 1998. He filed a claim for benefits in October 1999. The detective argued that the Commissioner improperly determined that the heart disease was not an occupational disease under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-275(15). The appellate court held that the detective failed to offer evidence that job stress and the resulting disease were peculiar to or so distinctively associated with his occupation that there was a direct causal connection between the duties of the employment and the disease. Therefore, the detective did not prove that his heart disease was an occupational disease. The appellate court discounted the detective's claim that his heart disease was an occupational disease pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 5-145a, 5-145c, and 7-433c(a). Those statutes were also subject to the jurisdictional and procedural requirements of the Connecticut Workers' Compensation Act. The detective also argued that his notice of claim was timely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-294c. The appellate court found that the Commissioner properly determined that the detective's last date of employment was more than one year prior to the filing of the claim.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

295 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Stuart v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 16914


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


266 Conn. 596; 834 A.2d 52; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 450



November 18, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the court, Hon. Thomas H. Corrigan, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed.
Stuart v. Warden, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1557 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 11, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed his amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus. At issue was the interplay between U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d (Rev. to 1993).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was charged with crimes in Connecticut and was soon thereafter arrested in Pennsylvania in connection with those charges and held as a fugitive. The inmate could not post bond and contested Connecticut's efforts to extradite him, serving 128 days in Pennsylvania before extradition. He pleaded guilty and was sentenced. Following sentencing, the inmate sought credit toward his sentence under § 18-98d. Respondent Commissioner of Correction denied the request and the trial court denied the inmate's habeas petition. On appeal, the sole issue was whether the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment required that the inmate be awarded presentence confinement credit for the period of time that he was incarcerated in Pennsylvania. The court concluded that the inmate was not entitled to such credit. The Equal Protection Clause was not implicated because persons such as the inmate who were confined in another state pending extradition were not similarly situated to persons who were confined in Connecticut pending trial. The inmate faced extradition only because he chose to flee to Pennsylvania after he had committed the assault that led to his conviction in Connecticut.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

296 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rizzo


(SC 16197)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


266 Conn. 171; 833 A.2d 363; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 394


October 14, 2002, Argued  
October 14, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Motion denied by State v. Rizzo, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1685 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the defendant was presented to the court, Holden, J., on pleas of guilty as to both charges; thereafter, the penalty phase of the proceedings was tried to the jury before Holden, J.; verdict finding the existence of an aggravating factor and one or more mitigating factors and that the aggravating factor outweighed the mitigating factor or factors; subsequently, the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the defendant's pleas, merged the counts and, in accordance with the jury's verdict, sentenced the defendant to death, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Rizzo, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2194 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 12, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded to trial court for new penalty phase hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered convictions, based on his guilty pleas, for murder and capital felony, and sentenced defendant to death upon a finding that the aggravating factor of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(4) (Rev. to 1997) outweighed the one unspecified mitigating factor found.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lured a 13-year old victim to his backyard and brutally killed him by hitting him repeatedly on the head, back, and shoulders with a sledgehammer. He was convicted of a capital felony and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found the weighing provisions of § 53a-46a(e), (f) constitutional under a Geisler factor analysis. The court found that the U.S. and Connecticut Constitutions did not impose any specific standard to be employed in the weighing process, and accordingly, a finding that the aggravating factor outweighed the mitigating factor was sufficient. However, the court held that the jury's subjective level of certitude in reaching the determination that the death penalty was the appropriate punishment was to be "beyond a reasonable doubt." The court also found reversible error in the multiple improprieties in the prosecutor's closing argument. Evidence regarding lack of remorse was properly admitted to infer cruelty as an aggravator. Various evidentiary rulings were reviewed, there was no Eighth Amendment violation by the "facts and circumstances" language of § 53a-46a(d), expert testimony was properly admitted, and a special verdict was not required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for a new penalty phase hearing.

Conn. Light & Power Co. v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


(SC 16887)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


266 Conn. 108; 830 A.2d 1121; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 378


May 23, 2003, Argued  
September 30, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant approving the sale of certain real property held by the plaintiff and ordering the plaintiff to apply the net proceeds from the sale to reduce certain costs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Owens, J.; judgment dismissing the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Conn. Light & Power Co. v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2533 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility company sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut) which affirmed the decision by appellee department of public utility control which approved the sale of certain real property held by the utility company and ordered the utility company to apply the net proceeds from the sale to reduce certain costs.


OVERVIEW: The utility company questioned, among other things, whether the judgment was correct in regard to the sale of nonutility land. The appellate court held that if the legislature had intended to limit the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-245e(h)(4)(C) to utility property, it easily could have done so. The utility company provided no authority or analysis in support of its specific claim that requiring it to apply the proceeds from the sale of nonutility land to reduce its stranded costs constituted a taking. The trial court properly declined to consider the constitutional claim. Only reasonable expenses that had been incurred in connection with the transaction that resulted in the actual sale could be deducted from the sales price under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-244f(a)(2). The trial court properly determined that certain testimony constituted substantial evidence supporting the department's finding that the expenses incurred by the utility company in prior years in connection with the negotiations with a purchasing company were not related to the actual sale. There was substantial evidence to support the disallowance of the utility company's internal labor costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

298 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Tappin v. Homecomings Fin. Network, Inc.


(SC 16724)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 741; 830 A.2d 711; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 347



September 16, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Writ of error from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Hon. Donald W. Celotto, judge trial referee, denying the motion by the plaintiff in error to enjoin her ejectment from certain rental premises that were subject to a mortgage foreclosure proceeding to which the plaintiff in error was not a party. Writ of error dismissed.



DISPOSITION: Writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant moved to enjoin the execution of ejectment against her brought by defendant, an assignee of a mortgagee that had foreclosed its mortgage on the leased premises. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, Connecticut, denied the tenant's motion to enjoin but stayed the execution of ejectment. The tenant filed a writ of error under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-272.


OVERVIEW: The assignee's predecessor brought a foreclosure action against the mortgagor and recorded a lis pendens. After the foreclosure action had gone to judgment, the mortgagor and tenant signed a lease; the tenant was unaware of the foreclosure. She was never added as a party to the foreclosure action, nor did the assignee foreclose her interest as an omitted party under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-30. The supreme court found that the writ of error was moot, the tenant having moved out, but that the exception to the mootness doctrine applied because the issue was one of public importance and was capable of repetition, yet evaded review. The denial of the tenant's motion to enjoin the ejectment was a final judgment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-263, since the order so concluded her rights that further proceedings could not affect them. As the supreme court could consider the assignee's right to possession without opening the judgment of foreclosure, it had subject matter jurisdiction. As to the merits, the supreme court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-22(a) prohibited the issuance of an execution of ejectment against a tenant who was not named as a party to the foreclosure action.


OUTCOME: The supreme court held that a tenant had to be joined as a party to the foreclosure action in order to be ejected under the applicable statute, but dismissed the writ of error as moot.

State v. March


(SC 16776)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 697; 830 A.2d 212; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 340


December 3, 2002, Argued  
September 9, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the jury before Susco, J.; verdict and judgment of not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect and committing the defendant to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board; thereafter, the court, DiPentima, J., denied the defendant's application for discharge from the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board, and the defendant appealed.
State v. March, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1140 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was acquitted of manslaughter by a jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) because of mental disease or defect. Defendant was committed to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board. The court denied defendant's application for discharge from the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury reasonably found that defendant drowned her five and one-half month old child while in a dissociative psychotic state. The trial court concluded that defendant had failed to meet her burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that she was a person who should be discharged pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593. Relying largely on the psychiatric security review board's revocation of defendant's conditional release, and applying the definition of "psychiatric disabilities" found in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-458(a), the trial court found that defendant had psychiatric disabilities to the extent that discharge would constitute a danger to herself or others. The supreme court found that although the trial court looked to the wrong statute for the proper definition of "psychiatric disability," the definition in Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17a-581-2(a)(5) was the proper one, it nonetheless applied the correct standard and properly found that defendant posed a danger if released. Further, the trial court's determination that defendant was not a person who should be discharged was not arbitrary, fundamentally unfair, or intended to facilitate her perpetual confinement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

300 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fort Trumbull Conservancy v. City of New London


SC 16661


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 423; 829 A.2d 801; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 332


February 13, 2003, Argued  
August 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected February 10, 2004.
Related proceeding at Fort Trumbull Conservancy, LLC v. City of New London, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 147 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Fort Trumbull Conservancy, L.L.C. v. Alves, 262 Conn. 480, 815 A.2d 1188, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 75 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant limited liability corporation (LLC) sought review of the Connecticut trial court which granted the motion of appellees, a city, an agency, and others, to dismiss the LLC's complaint for lack of standing based upon the LLC's failure to allege facts sufficient to demonstrate either statutory or classical aggrievement.


OVERVIEW: An environmental impact evaluation was prepared. The city and agency eventually adopted the development plan. Certain property was then condemned and demolished. The LLC sought various legal and equitable remedies, including declaratory relief and an injunction prohibiting the implementation of the plan. The LLC's complaint challenged both the legality of the process pursuant to which the city adopted the development plan and the necessity of the demolition component of the plan. However, the appellate court held the allegations provided no indication as to how or why the adoption and implementation of the development plan was likely to cause unreasonable harm to the environment, as it was not evident how the failure to follow certain procedural requirements in adopting the development plan or to consider alternatives to the demolition of buildings was likely to cause harm. The LLC failed to demonstrate how its members had been "specially and injuriously affected" by appellees' conduct. The LLC's claims of statutory aggrievement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 and classical aggrievement had to fail.


OUTCOME: The trial court properly granted the motions to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

 

301 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Egan


(SC 16730)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 301; 828 A.2d 549; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 322; 20 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 510


January 17, 2003, Argued  
August 12, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, defamation, false imprisonment, civil conspiracy and violations of the plaintiff's civil rights under the state and federal constitutions as a result of the defendants' alleged misconduct, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, McLachlan, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court denied the defendants' motion for reconsideration and reargument of their motion to dismiss, and the defendants appealed.
Miller v. Egan, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2572 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 6, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee sued defendants, a former high sheriff, a former chief deputy sheriff, former special deputy sheriffs, and the State, alleging false imprisonment, defamation, civil conspiracy, and violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New London, Connecticut, denied defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that in retaliation for his whistle-blowing, some defendants falsely imprisoned him in a jury room and made defamatory statements about him to a newspaper. The trial court held that (1) the civil conspiracy claims fell under the exception to sovereign immunity for actions by state officers in excess of their statutory authority; and (2) as to the remaining claims, the legislature had waived sovereign immunity by enacting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-30a (Rev. to 1999), which required sheriffs to obtain liability insurance. The supreme court disagreed. It overruled Shay v. Rossi, 253 Conn. 134, 749 A.2d 1147 (2000), and Antinerella v. Rioux, 229 Conn. 479, 642 A.2d 699 (1994), to the extent they held that sovereign immunity did not bar monetary damages actions against state officials acting in excess of their statutory authority. As the employee sought only money damages, and had not sought permission of the claims commissioner, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(a), to sue the State, his civil conspiracy claims were precluded. The remaining claims were also barred, as the enactment of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-30a was not a waiver of sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying defendants' motion to dismiss was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to grant the motion, and to render judgment dismissing the complaint.

 

302 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Prigge v. Ragaglia


(SC 16787)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 338; 828 A.2d 542; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 324


January 10, 2003, Argued  
August 12, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' allegedly reckless conduct, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the case was transferred to the Complex Litigation Docket at Waterbury; thereafter, the court, Sheldon, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss and the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the Appellate Court denied the plaintiffs' motion to dismiss the defendants' appeal, and the appeal was transferred to this court.
In re Joshua S., 260 Conn. 182, 796 A.2d 1141, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 197 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff guardians sued defendants, public officials and employees, in both their official and individual capacities, alleging defendants had discriminated against them in child custody proceedings, and seeking injunctive relief and damages. Defendants moved to dismiss on sovereign immunity grounds; the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury, Connecticut, denied the motion. Defendants' appeal was transferred to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: After the guardians were appointed testamentary guardians of four children, the children's mother killed the father and two of the children. The guardians alleged that defendants' decision not to place one of the children with them was based on their religion, and that defendants acted in excess of their statutory authority. They alleged willful, wanton and reckless misconduct in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985(3), and 1986, and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The trial court held that sovereign immunity did not bar those claims against defendants in their official capacities that sought monetary damages, as defendants allegedly acted in excess of statutory authority. The supreme court reversed, based on a recent decision in which it held that the exception to sovereign immunity for actions by state officers in excess of their statutory authority applied only to actions seeking declaratory or injunctive relief, not to claims for money damages. As the guardians had not received permission from the office of the claims commissioner to bring their claims for money damages against the State, these claims were barred.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying defendants' motion to dismiss was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to grant the motion and to render judgment dismissing the guardians' claims against defendants in their official capacities seeking monetary damages.

State v. Deloreto


(SC 16908)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 145; 827 A.2d 671; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 311


April 15, 2003, Argued  
August 5, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected September 24, 2003.
Related proceeding at DeLoreto v. Karengekis, 104 Fed. Appx. 765, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 13643 (2d Cir. Conn., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Information, in each of two cases, charging the defendant with the crime of breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, A. dos Santos, J.; judgment of guilty of two counts of breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Deloreto, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 502 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), of breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(1), (3), and (5), after his motion to dismiss and for a judgment of acquittal challenging the constitutionality of the statute were denied. The appeal was transferred pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, although unprovoked, threatened to "kick the ass" of two police officers in separate incidents. Defendant argued that his convictions of disturbing the peace were unconstitutional violations of his free speech rights under the state and federal constitutions. The appellate court held that the statements were true threats, and, as such, were not protected by the federal and state constitutions. Further, defendant properly was convicted under § 53a-181(a)(3) as he, with intent to cause inconvenience, annoyance, or alarm, or recklessly creating a risk thereof, threatened to commit a crime against the officers. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the trial court properly determined that § 53a-181(a)(3) was neither unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant nor overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

304 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mello v. Big Y Foods, Inc.


(SC 16909)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 21; 826 A.2d 1117; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 296



July 29, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the alleged negligence of the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Rogers, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court, Holzberg, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved two questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; subsequently, the reservation was transferred to this court.
Mello v. Big Y Foods, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3421 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 18, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Court answered first reserved question in the affirmative, second reserved question in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Waterbury (Connecticut). The trial court reserved two questions of law governing a case arising from a workers' compensation claim against defendant employer, namely, whether her claim for permanent and significant scarring on her foot and ankle was barred by the exclusivity provision, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284(a), and if so, whether that bar violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained a compensable burn injury to her foot and ankle, which resulted in permanent scarring. Her employer paid for medical costs and lost wages. However, the workers' compensation commissioner denied benefits for the scarring itself after finding that it was not the kind of scarring that was compensable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308(c). The employee filed a negligence suit against the employer, and the trial court reserved two questions. The court held that the employee's negligence claim was barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284(a) because her scarring arose from a compensable injury. The employee could not "unbundle" a noncompensable part of her underlying injury from the compensable part and bring an action on the former while seeking workers' compensation for the latter. The exclusivity provision was also not unconstitutional as applied to the facts of the case. The employee had received prompt compensation for the burn injury, and the worker's compensation act, when viewed as a whole, provided the employee with a reasonable alternative to her prior common law right to bring tort claims for injuries suffered in the course of employment.


OUTCOME: The court answered the first reserved question in the affirmative and the second reserved question in the negative.

 

305 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Higgins


(SC 16403)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


265 Conn. 35; 826 A.2d 1126; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 298



July 29, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of capital felony and three counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), wherein he was convicted of capital felony and assault in the first degree. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fired a gun at a group of people sitting outside a house during a drive-by shooting, killing a 13-year old boy and injuring others. Defendant was tried and convicted, and was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of release, as well as an additional imprisonment term. On appeal, the court found that the doctrine of transferred intent was properly applied under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(8), and that defendant did not need to know the age of his victim in order for imposition of the greater degree of liability. The court found that § 53a-54b(8) was constitutional in its mandatory imposition of life imprisonment because it was not disproportionate to the crime and did not violate U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV. Under a rational basis standard of review, there was no equal protection violation because the punishment protected against the killing of a child. The jury verdict as to findings of intent on the various conviction was not inconsistent, and denial of defendant's motion for a mistrial due to the presence of uniformed correction officers at his trial was proper where no actual prejudice was shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

306 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brocuglio


(SC 16590)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


264 Conn. 778; 826 A.2d 145; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 268



July 22, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault on a peace officer and three counts of the crime of interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, where the court, Owens, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Pellegrino, Dranginis and Hennessy, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Brocuglio, 64 Conn. App. 93, 779 A.2d 793, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 325 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court convicted defendant of two counts of interfering with a police officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a. The Appellate Court of Connecticut, in reversing and remanding, concluded that the trial court improperly denied defendant's motion to suppress on the ground that his conduct constituted a new crime that broke the chain of causation, dissipating the taint of police officers' unlawful entry. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue in the certified appeal was whether defendant's conduct in response to the police officers' illegal entry into the backyard of his residence to ticket cars dissipated the taint of their unlawful entry and thereby precluded defendant from invoking the exclusionary rule to suppress evidence derived from the unlawful entry. The Connecticut Supreme Court, in overruling part of its Gallagher decision, (1) adopted the exception to the exclusionary rule that the commission of a new crime dissipated the taint from evidence of that crime obtained as the result of an illegal entry into one's home, and (2) concluded that because, at the time of the relevant events, defendant had a limited common-law right to resist an unlawful, warrantless entry into the backyard of his residence, it could not retroactively apply the new crime exception to defendant. The Supreme Court did not have to consider whether to engraft an officer's bad faith limitation to the new crime exception, and did not abrogate the common law privilege to offer reasonable resistance, not rising to the level of an assault (not common law assault, but the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c crime) to an unlawful entry.


OUTCOME: The Supreme Court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Reynolds


(SC 15258)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


264 Conn. 1; 836 A.2d 224; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 556


September 23, 2002, Argued  
July 15, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 7, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Reynolds v. Connecticut, 541 U.S. 908, 124 S. Ct. 1614, 158 L. Ed. 2d 254, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1939 (2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Claims of Racial Disparity v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Reynolds v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1558 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, and tried to the court, West, Fasano and Keller, Js.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the penalty phase of the proceedings was tried to the jury before Fasano, J.; verdict finding that the state had proven the existence of some aggravating factors and that the defendant had failed to prove the existence of any mitigating factor; subsequently, the court, Fasano, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the verdicts and sentenced the defendant to death, and the defendant appealed to this court, which thereafter denied the state's motion to dismiss the proportionality review and granted in part the defendant's motion to expand the universe of cases for proportionality review.
State v. Reynolds, 824 A.2d 611, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 209 (Conn., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) for murder and a capital felony, as well as his subsequent sentence of death. Defendant asserted 52 assignments of error including prejudice due to pretrial publicity and prosecutorial misconduct.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant, who was carrying drugs, and had him lean up against the car. The officer let go of defendant after attempting unsuccessfully to extract defendant's hand from defendant's pocket. Defendant bumped the officer with his arm, noticed the officer was wearing a bullet-proof vest, and then spun around and shot the officer in the head. The officer subsequently died. Defendant waived his right to a jury trial and elected to be tried by a three-judge court. Defendant's motion to suppress certain statements was denied. Defendant also asserted he was entitled to a new probable cause hearing because the information did not specify that the officer was acting within the scope of his duties. The appellate court rejected all of defendant's claims. The evidence amply supported the trial court's finding that an apartment occupant voluntarily consented to the officers' request for permission to enter her apartment. The evidence did not reasonably support the conclusion that defendant continued to fire at the officer with the intent to torture him psychologically. The death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The finding of an aggravated factor involving torturing the victim psychologically was reversed. The remainder of the judgment of the trial court was affirmed. In regard to defendant's claim of racial bias in death penalty cases, the proper course was to afford defendant an opportunity to renew his claim by way of a habeas corpus petition. The State's motion to dismiss the proportionality review was denied.

 

308 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moran


(SC 16731)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


264 Conn. 593; 825 A.2d 111; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 263



July 8, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the first degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and robbery of an occupied motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, and presented to the court, Rodriguez, J., on a plea of guilty to the crimes of conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and robbery of an occupied motor vehicle; thereafter, the court rendered judgment in accordance with the defendant's plea, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Superior Court, Fairfield Judicial District, after defendant's guilty plea, convicted him of, inter alia, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 53a-134(a)(2) conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and sentenced him in accordance with his plea. Defendant appealed and claimed he was improperly sentenced under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(b) to a five-year nonsuspendable mandatory minimum sentence for that conviction.


OVERVIEW: The trial court also convicted defendant of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 53a-122 conspiracy to commit first degree larceny and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136a robbery of an occupied vehicle. Under the Trent principle regarding the sentence for Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-51 inchoate crimes, such as attempts and conspiracy, defendant was subject to the specific sentence delineated for the most serious offense attempted. Thus, the sentence for conspiracy to commit first degree robbery equaled the sentence for first degree robbery. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(b) mandated a five-year nonsuspendable mandatory term of imprisonment for first degree robbery. The supreme court applied rational basis review to determine the § 53a-134(b) sentence complied with the Equal Protection Clause. There was a rational basis for the punishment of conspiracy to commit first degree robbery to be greater than the punishment of conspiracy to commit murder, two separate and distinct crimes. The legislature could have believed in regard to conspiracy to commit first degree robbery that (1) trial courts were less likely to impose a minimum five-year sentence, and (2) a more severe penalty was required to deter it.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Breton


(SC 15876)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


264 Conn. 327; 824 A.2d 778; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 244


September 9, 2002, Argued  
June 24, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Breton v. Connecticut, 540 U.S. 1055, 124 S. Ct. 819, 157 L. Ed. 2d 708, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 8701 (Dec. 1, 2003)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Claims of Racial Disparity v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Breton v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2241 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of capital felony and two counts of the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Heiman, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found the existence of an aggravating factor and no mitigating factor, and the court rendered judgment of guilty of capital felony and imposed the death penalty, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed the judgment with respect to the imposition of the death penalty and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing; on remand, a three judge court, Fasano, Damiani and Vertefeuille, Js., found the existence of an aggravating factor and no mitigating factor, and, merging the murder counts with the capital felony count, rendered judgment imposing the death penalty on the capital felony count, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Breton, 235 Conn. 206, 663 A.2d 1026, 1995 Conn. LEXIS 319 (Aug. 22, 1995)
State v. Breton, 212 Conn. 258, 562 A.2d 1060, 1989 Conn. LEXIS 225 (July 25, 1989)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a three judge panel that, following a remand, found that the State had proven that defendant had committed the murders of his wife and son. Defendant originally appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury that convicted defendant of one count of capital felony and two counts of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed several statutory mitigating factors and nonstatutory mitigating factors. The panel found that the State had proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had committed both murders in an especially cruel manner. The panel also found that defendant had proved by a preponderance of the evidence the factual underpinnings of certain claimed nonstatutory mitigating factors, but that none of the proved facts alone or in combination constituted mitigation considering all of the facts and circumstances of the case. The panel did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion for a continuance. The appellate court found further that the panel reasonably could have concluded that defendant's abuse as a child did not constitute such a reason. The appellate court concluded that defendant's proof did not compel a finding of mitigation. Finally, to the extent that defendant claimed that his extreme emotional disturbance met the requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(g), his claim was rejected. Finally, the evidence was sufficient for the jury to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed both murders in an especially cruel manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DiMartino v. Richens


(SC 16818)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


263 Conn. 639; 822 A.2d 205; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 208; 19 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1750; 148 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P59,733


January 6, 2003, Argued  
May 27, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended action in thirteen counts to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged violation of the plaintiff's constitutional rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Peck, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike one count of the plaintiff's revised complaint; thereafter, the matter was tried to a jury before Bryant, J., on the remaining twelve counts of the revised complaint; verdict for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court denied the defendants' motions to set aside the verdict and for remittitur, and granted the plaintiff's motion for attorney's fees, and thereafter rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and awarded the plaintiff attorney's fees, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff government employee had sued defendants, individuals and department of transportation, for violating his constitutional rights, and for other relief. Defendants appealed the verdict of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which was in favor of the employee. The trial court denied defendants' motions to set aside the verdict and for remittitur, and granted the employee's motion for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a supervisor of carpentry at the airport. Someone had been improperly gaining access to his office, calling into question the security of the airport. The employee was transferred and demoted after he cooperated with the state police in a criminal investigation of several fellow employees, including the individual defendants. The conduct was under color of state law. Given the risk of terrorism, the appellate court held the employee's speech could fairly be considered to relate to a matter of political and social concern to the community. The individual defendants did not dispute that they were substantially motivated by the employee's speech when they took action against him. The First Amendment interest in encouraging, rather than suppressing, the employee's speech about this breakdown in airport security was great. By contrast, the State's interest in promoting the efficiency of its services by taking action against the employee for his speech about a critical breach of airport security was minimal. The reassignments were highly degrading, indicating that the true motive was vengeance and the claimed governmental objective was pretextual.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Stepney, LLC v. Town of Fairfield


(SC 16929)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


263 Conn. 558; 821 A.2d 725; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 194


March 13, 2003, Argued  
May 20, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from enforcing a certain municipal health code regulation requiring landlords to furnish certain information in completing applications necessary to obtain certificates of rental occupancy, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Housing Session at Bridgeport, where the case was thereafter transferred to the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Complex Litigation Docket at Stamford, and tried to the court, Tierney, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed.
Stepney, LLC v. Town of Fairfield, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1731 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 24, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction to dismiss action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to enjoin defendant town from enforcing a certain municipal health code regulation, the town appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) that found in favor of plaintiff limited liability company. On appeal, the town challenged whether the trial court had jurisdiction to consider the action.


OVERVIEW: The company owned two single-family homes, and for many years has rented both properties to various tenants. The company annually completed an application and obtained a certificate of rental occupancy in compliance with the town's health code regulations governing rental dwellings. In 1999, the town amended the regulation to require more specific information regarding any potential tenants. The company failed to apply for certificates that year. Instead, the company filed an action challenging the constitutionality of the amended health code regulation. The appellate court concluded that the commissioner of public health had the authority and the expertise necessary to determine whether Fairfield, Conn., Health Code Reg. § 3.3 exceeded the town's authority pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-207, and to fashion an appropriate remedy. Further, the fact-finding inherent in evaluating a claimed violation was entrusted by the legislature to the commissioner, and the appellate court found no reason to usurp his authority to handle the company's claim. Because the company could have obtained review of the town's order, the company was required to do so before seeking redress in court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the action was dismissed.

Bhinder v. Sun Co.


(SC 16674)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


263 Conn. 358; 819 A.2d 822; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 161; 20 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1558


October 21, 2002, Argued  
April 29, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where Main Avenue Sunoco intervened as a plaintiff, and where the court, Karazin, J., granted the defendant's motion to cite in Raul Garcia, Jr., as a defendant for apportionment of liability and to file a complaint for apportionment against the apportionment defendant; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion to strike the apportionment complaint, granted the defendant's motion for judgment on the stricken complaint and rendered judgment thereon for the apportionment defendant, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; the appeal was subsequently transferred to this court, which reversed the trial court's judgment; thereafter, the court, Lewis, J., granted the plaintiff's renewed motion to strike the apportionment complaint, and the court, Mintz, J., granted the defendant's motion for judgment on that stricken complaint and rendered judgment thereon in favor of the apportionment defendant, from which the defendant appealed.
Bhinder v. Sun Co., 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2941 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 9, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate filed a wrongful death action against defendant station owner. The station owner filed an apportionment complaint alleging that apportionment defendant, the shooter, acted recklessly and wilfully and wantonly. The estate moved to strike the apportionment complaint. The station owner appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) striking the apportionment complaint.


OVERVIEW: The station owner argued that the trial court erred in granting the estate's motion to strike the apportionment complaint against the shooter because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-572h(o) precluded apportionment of damages between parties on any basis other than negligence. The station owner argued that the retroactive application of 1999 Conn. Acts 69, § 1(o) violated the doctrine of separation of powers and the due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The supreme court held that the trial court properly determined that the legislature clarified Conn. Gen. Stat. § 25-572h (Rev. to 1997) in enacting 1999 Conn. Acts 69, § 1(o), and, therefore, retroactive application of the statute, as amended, did not violate the state and federal constitutions. The station owner also contended that application of 1999 Conn. Acts 69, § 1(o) deprived it of a vested property interest. The supreme court concluded that since the legislature merely clarified what its intent was when enacting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-572h, the amendment clearly satisfied the rational basis test. In addition, the supreme court concluded that the station owner never had a vested interest in the claim.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Rayhall v. Akim Co.


(SC 16685)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


263 Conn. 328; 819 A.2d 803; 2003 Conn. LEXIS 160


January 9, 2003, Argued  
April 29, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal and cross appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the second district that awarded disability benefits to the plaintiff and determined that the amount of disability benefits paid by the defendants could be offset by the social security old age benefits received by the plaintiff, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed and the defendants cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Workers' Compensation Commissioner, Second District, awarded to plaintiff employee retroactive compensation for temporary partial incapacity, and ordered defendant employer, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e), to deduct $ 1,002 per month as a Social Security offset from prospective compensation to the employee for temporary total incapacity. The employee appealed and the employer cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer's insurer was also one defendant. The supreme court transferred the employee's Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-301b appeal to itself under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199 (c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 65-1. The employee injured both legs in a work accident and needed right knee, then left knee, replacements to achieve maximum medical improvement (MMI) respectively for each leg. The supreme court determined the rational basis, rather than strict scrutiny (disability and age classes were not presumptively invidious), test applied to the employee's equal protection and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20 arguments against the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e). Section 31-307(e) was constitutional; reducing costs by reducing payments to persons retired from the workforce was a reasonably conceivable rational basis for applying the offset to one subset of the disabled, the totally incapacitated, but not to another subset, the partially incapacitated. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-295(c), 31-308(b), the supreme court held that the employee, who sustained an injury to more than one body part, could delay his permanency benefits until all injured members achieved MMI.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision.

State v. Luurtsema


(SC 16745)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


262 Conn. 179; 811 A.2d 223; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 492


September 24, 2002, Argued  
December 24, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Luurtsema, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 765 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 24, 2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Luurtsema v. Comm'r of Corr., 299 Conn. 740, 12 A.3d 817, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 12 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute two part information charging the defendant in the first part with the crimes of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, attempt to commit murder and assault in the second degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Mulcahy, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Mulcahy, J., on the first part of the information; verdict of guilty of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and assault in the second degree; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court, Clifford, J., on a plea of nolo contendere on the second part of the information; the court, Mulcahy, J., thereafter, rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), denied defendant's motion to suppress and after a jury trial convicted him of attempted sexual assault in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49, 53a-70(a)(1); kidnapping in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A); assault in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60(a)(1); and being a persistent dangerous felony offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant restrained the victim and sexually assaulted her in her apartment. The supreme court, in affirming, explained its Geisler III exclusionary rule exception (the attenuation decision). Under the totality of the circumstances, including (1) 11 hours between defendant's arrest and incriminating statement after his improper warrantless arrest in his home, but based on probable cause; (2) defendant's twice receiving Miranda warnings; and (3) police misconduct that was neither purposeful nor flagrant, defendant's statement was sufficiently attenuated from the taint of the arrest and was properly admitted by the trial court. Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7 protections were broader than the Fourth Amendment's, so the supreme court used the analytical framework of the U.S. Supreme Court's facts-and-circumstances attenuation (the Brown test) and rejected the U.S. Supreme Court's Harris test. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), kidnapping did not requiring carrying the victim away; it required abducting and restraining, to prevent the victim's liberation, with the requisite intent to inflict physical injury or sexually abuse, and was not incidental to or merged with the assault.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

Cumberland Farms v. Town of Groton


(SC 16501)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


262 Conn. 45; 808 A.2d 1107; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 434


January 10, 2002, Argued  
November 19, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Hon. D. Michael Hurley, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion to strike the case from the jury docket; thereafter, the court, Martin, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.
 Cumberland Farms v. Town of Groton, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3008 (Conn. Super. Ct. Nov. 4, 1999). Cumberland Farms v. Town of Groton, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 205 (Conn. Super. Ct. Jan. 19, 2001).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed from an order and judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which granted defendant town's motion to strike the action, seeking damages for an alleged inverse condemnation of the owner's property, from the jury docket, and which also granted summary judgment to the town on the basis of collateral estoppel.


OVERVIEW: The owner alleged that the zoning variance denial by the town's zoning board of appeals, which was affirmed on appeal, constituted an inverse condemnation. The owner sought compensation under the takings clauses of U.S. Const. amend. V and Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. The property was a gas station that sold snacks and the owner wanted to add a convenience store. The trial court's holding that collateral estoppel barred the litigation of facts that had been decided by the board was reversed by the court, which found no bar to the presentation of facts that were pertinent to the claim on the basis of policy considerations. Further, the court found that the factual issues were not actually litigated in the administrative appeal. The owner was entitled to a de novo review without reliance on the board's prior fact finding. The holding that there was no right to a jury trial under Conn. Const. art. I, § 19 was affirmed. The court noted that the inverse condemnation action was an adequate post-deprivation remedy. Accordingly, if any taking occurred, it was not tortious and therefore not an action at law, but rather one in equity, similar to an eminent domain proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings. The court affirmed that aspect of the trial court's judgment which held that the owner was not entitled to a jury trial.

 

317 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ.


(SC 16650)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


261 Conn. 475; 803 A.2d 318; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 325


May 20, 2002, Argued  
August 20, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1632 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 28, 2003)
Appeal dismissed by Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2637 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a certain state statute vesting regional boards of education with the authority to determine and assess the amount that each town in their respective regional districts must pay for educational expenses, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, DiPentima, J., granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by the town of Salisbury; thereafter, the court, Cremins, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Richard Blumenthal and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the plaintiffs' action, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Seymour v. Region One Bd. of Educ., 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 7 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 2, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a board of education and the attorney general, seeking, inter alia, a judgment declaring Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-51(b) unconstitutional. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), dismissed the complaint on the grounds that the taxpayers' claims were nonjusticiable because they presented a political question. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The costs of educating high school and certain elementary students were assessed on towns by the board according to a formula set out in § 10-51(b). Under that formula, each town paid that percentage of the district's expenses equivalent to the percentage of the total number of students served by the district that resided in that town. The taxpayers claimed § 10-51(b) unfairly discriminated against small towns by forcing them to pay an unequal share of the expenses of educating students as compared to their bigger and wealthier neighbors, in violation of the due process and equal protection provisions of the federal and state constitutions. The sole remedy, the taxpayers claimed, was to make the district a single taxing district, with a uniform mill rate, which would assess each town an amount based on the value of the real property in that town. The supreme court held that the trial court's granting of such a remedy might violate the political question doctrine, but simply determining the constitutionality of § 10-51(b) would not. However, the record was insufficient to allow the supreme court to determine whether the taxpayers had suffered sufficient injury to give them standing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a hearing on the question of the taxpayers' standing, and for further proceedings according to law.

 

318 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCahill


(HHB CR99-0005116-T), (SC 16574)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


803 A.2d 901; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 328


November 27, 2001, Argued  
August 20, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at State v. McCahill, 261 Conn. 492, 811 A.2d 667, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 543 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for bail review filed by the state, in the first case, and writ of error filed by the victim advocate, in the second case, from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Hon. Bernard D. Gaffney, judge trial referee, denying the state's request that the defendant in error James A. McCahill be held without bail pending an appeal of his conviction of the crimes of burglary in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree. Order affirmed; writ of error dismissed.
State v. McCahill, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2836 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Victim's writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of first degree burglary and first degree sexual assault in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), the trial court granted defendant an appeal bond, in spite of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-63f's prohibition on bail for a defendant convicted of an offense involving physical force. The State appealed, and the victim filed a writ of error.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found the statute interfered with the judicial magistracy. The supreme court held the victim's ultimate argument that the trial court erred in finding the prohibition of defendant's release unconstitutional was also the State's position so it was unnecessary to decide her standing to bring a writ, and the court would not address a constitutional question unless required to. The legislature's attempt to limit the court's discretion to release a defendant on bail in cases involving the use of force applied to so many cases that it impermissibly interfered with the trial court's orderly functioning, on its face. The statute interfered with the trial court by: (1) rendering the right to appeal meaningless, as the incarceration required could end before an appeal was decided; (2) requiring incarceration of a defendant pending sentencing who might be sentenced to probation or a fine; (3) interfering with a trial court's discretion to find a defendant's conviction legally flawed, as defendant's incarceration was required pending a decision on that issue; and (4) interfering with a court's ability to impose an incarceration alternative, such as treatment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order releasing defendant on bail was affirmed, and the victim's writ of error was dismissed as moot.

320 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sostre


(SC 16670)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


261 Conn. 111; 802 A.2d 754; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 290



July 30, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Sostre, 48 Conn. Supp. 82, 830 A.2d 1212, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3418 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, kidnapping in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, larceny in the second degree and attempted larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the state filed a notice of aggravating factors; thereafter, the court, Lavine, J., denied in part and granted in part the defendant's motions to dismiss the aggravating factors and the state, on the granting of certification to appeal on a question involving substantial public interest pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a, appealed to this court.
State v. Sostre, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3592 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 19, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged, inter alia, with the crimes of capital felony, murder, and felony murder. The State notified defendant that it intended to seek the death penalty on the basis of aggravating factors set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(1), (6). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) dismissed the State's proposed action under § 53a-46a(i)(6), and the state supreme court granted certification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, inter alia, with the crimes of capital felony, murder, and felony murder after he shot and killed a police officer who was dispatched to investigate a noise complaint. The complaint was filed after defendant and three other people broke into an apartment with the intent to commit robbery and assaulted the person who lived in the apartment. When defendant heard the sound of a police radio, he took the victim's gun, entered a common hallway, and shot the officer in the head as he passed by. Prior to trial, the State notified defendant that it would seek the death penalty, inter alia, on the basis of the fact that he committed the murder "in expectation of the receipt of" something of pecuniary value, an aggravating factor under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(6). The trial court blocked that action, however, on the basis of its finding that § 53a-46a(i)(6) applied only to killings that were an essential prerequisite to obtaining something of pecuniary value and not to capital offenses committed during the course of a robbery. The state supreme court held that the trial court's interpretation of § 53a-46a(i)(6) was correct.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

321 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neil


(SC 16177)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


261 Conn. 49; 801 A.2d 730; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 276


January 17, 2002, Argued  
July 23, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. O'Neil, 65 Conn. App. 145, 782 A.2d 209, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 421 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for murder. Defendant claimed the trial court improperly delivered a Chip Smith instruction that, by its language, was coercive upon minority view members of the jury and admitted into evidence information regarding two unrelated criminal matters that were pending at the time of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been charged in connection with a death. While awaiting trial on the murder charge, defendant also was charged with attempt to commit murder as a result of a letter he sent requesting the primary witness be killed. His first trial resulted in a mistrial as to the murder charge. Thereafter, he was convicted in a second trial following a Chip Smith instruction. The appellate court held the trial court properly utilized the Chip Smith charge in instructing the jury. The instruction struck a fair balance between aiding the jury in the deliberative process and reminding jurors not to surrender their conscientiously held beliefs, notwithstanding the language instructing minority view jurors to reconsider their position in light of the position of majority view jurors. Even so, the appellate court set out a specifically worded instruction to be used in the future in order to avoid questions of coercion. The trial court also carefully weighed the probative value of the evidence of defendant's other criminal acts against its prejudicial effect and properly determined that any resulting prejudice did not outweigh the probative value of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
