City of Waterbury v. Town of Wash.


(SC 16509)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 506; 800 A.2d 1102; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 250


November 30, 2001, Argued  
July 2, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in one case, for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, whether the named plaintiff's diversion of water from the Shepaug River breached a certain contract with the named defendant, and action, in a second case, for, inter alia, an injunction to restrain the named plaintiff from diverting water from that river, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the cases were consolidated and transferred to the Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the defendants withdrew their complaint in the second case and filed their claims as counterclaims in the first case, and the state attorney general, the commissioner of environmental protection and the Connecticut Fund for the Environment were permitted to intervene as defendants; subsequently, the matter was tried to the court, Hodgson, J., who issued a memorandum of decision ruling in part for the defendants on the complaint and on their counterclaims, regulating the amount of water that could be diverted daily from the river; the court thereafter granted in part the named plaintiff's motion for reargument and granted its motions for articulation and clarification, and issued [***2] a supplemental memorandum of decision, and the named plaintiff appealed and the named defendant et al. cross appealed.
 City of Waterbury v. Town of Washington, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 355 (Conn. Super. Ct. Feb. 16, 2000).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sued appellee town in the Superior Court in Waterbury (Connecticut), for a declaratory judgment that it did not breach an agreement; that it did not unreasonably pollute, impair, or destroy the public trust; and that its conduct did not constitute a public or private nuisance, or a violation of any existing riparian rights. The trial court found for the town and entered an order for injunctive relief. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed that its operation of a dam on a river did not breach of its contract with the town; did not violate the Connecticut Environmental Protection Act (CEPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-14 et seq., by impairing the public trust; did not create a public or private nuisance; and did not violate the town's riparian rights. The town claimed that the city's excessive diversions of water from the river violated the CEPA; was a public nuisance; was a private nuisance; interfered with the town's riparian rights; and constituted a breach of the contract. On appeal, the court found that (1) the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over the CEPA claims; (2) the town was not required to exhaust administrative remedies before bringing the CEPA claim; (3) the trial court's finding of an unreasonable impairment was not consistent with the statutory scheme in the area of watercourse management; (4) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-141 governed the substantive analysis of whether the city's conduct resulted in the unreasonable impairment of the river; and (5) the trial court improperly concluded that the city did not establish a prescriptive easement against the town's riparian rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the public trust claim and the riparian rights claim, and for a new remedy on the contract claim.

 

323 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Stepney Pond Estates, Ltd. v. Town of Monroe


(SC 16656)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 406; 797 A.2d 494; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 198


February 15, 2002, Argued  
June 4, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the defendant's assessment of a conveyance tax on the sale of certain real property by the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Gormley, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed.
 Stepney Pond Estates v. Town of Monroe, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1750 (Conn. Super. Ct. June 27, 2001).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner filed an action against defendant town alleging that the town's imposition of a conveyance tax was illegal. The town filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-504d, the exclusive remedy available to the owner was an appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-111, 12-112. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Connecticut, denied the town's motion. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the town was not authorized to declassify the property for purposes of initiating a new 10-year holding period, and that it illegally imposed the conveyance tax. The town argued that the trial court erred in concluding that (1) it had jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 to hear the owner's claim; and (2) that the transfer of the property to the owner did not initiate a new 10-year holding period for the purposes of assessing a conveyance tax. The appellate court held that (1) as the owner's claim challenged the validity of the tax in the first instance, the trial court had jurisdiction; and (2) the transfer from the executors to the owner was an exempt transaction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-504c(k) as it was transferred as a result of death by devise. The date of the acquisition was the date that the executors acquired the land and since the executors acquired the land by a devise, the date of their acquisition related back to the date of the original classification in 1971. Accordingly, since the subsequent sale by the owner was not within a 10-year period, the transfer was not subject to a conveyance tax under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-504a(b).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Ferguson


(SC 15964)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 339; 796 A.2d 1118; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 195


February 14, 2002, Argued  
May 28, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of murder, two counts of the crime of capital felony and one count each of the crimes of arson in the first degree and arson in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of five counts of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), two counts of capital felony in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(8), and two counts of arson, one in the first degree and one in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-111(a), 53a-112(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised six challenges to the validity of his convictions. The appellate court concluded that: (1) defendant's right of confrontation and right to present a defense were not violated by the trial court's exclusion of a certain photograph because the photograph was irrelevant and was insufficient evidence upon which to base a third party defense; (2) the trial court properly admitted defendant's threats to inflict violence on prior tenants because the admissions were evidence of motive; (3) double jeopardy ban was not violated because defendant committed multiple murders and the murders occurred in two sets, at distinctly separate times; (4) the trial court properly denied defendant's request for a Franks hearing because there were sufficient facts for the North Carolina magistrate to find probable cause to issue the warrant; (5) defendant was not denied a fair jury array; and (6) there was no possibility that the challenged language of the jury instruction, when read in the context of the entire charge regarding reasonable doubt, misled the jury in its understanding of the State's burden of proving defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

325 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ball


(SC 14646)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 275; 796 A.2d 542; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 183


December 6, 2001, Argued  
May 21, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendants with the crime of obstructing or interfering with the lawful taking of wildlife, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, where the court, Dranginis, J., denied the defendants' motions to dismiss; thereafter, the cases were presented to the court on conditional pleas of nolo contendere and the court, Gill, J., rendered judgments of guilty, from which the defendants filed a joint appeal to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the appeal was transferred to this court, which reversed the denial of the defendants' motions to dismiss and remanded the case to the Superior Court for further proceedings to determine, inter alia, the nature and extent of the public interest served by the statute under which the defendants had been charged; on remand, the court, Dranginis, J., conducted an evidentiary hearing and determined that state lands on which hunting is permitted are not public fora and that the statute under which the defendants had been charged was narrowly tailored to serve a substantial governmental interest.
 State v. Ball, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3003 (Conn. Super. Ct. Oct. 3, 2000).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with violation of the Hunter Harassment Act (Act), specifically Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183a. The Superior Court, Litchfield (Connecticut), denied defendants' motion to dismiss. Defendants then pled nolo contendere and were convicted. Defendants appealed and the case was transferred. Following a remand, the trial court made findings. Defendants again appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants had interfered with a legal bow hunter in a state wildlife management area. Defendants argued that the Act was an unconstitutional restriction on the First Amendment. The appellate court held that forum classification was determined by the traditional uses and principal purpose of the land, and not by the presence of some incidental characteristics typical of another type of forum. State forests were nonpublic fora, and thus the State was allowed to enforce time, place and manner regulations, and reserve the forum for its intended purposes, communicative or otherwise, as long as the regulation on speech was reasonable and not an effort to suppress expression merely because public officials opposed the speaker's view. The government's decision to restrict access to a nonpublic forum needed only be reasonable; it did not need to be the most reasonable or the only reasonable limitation. Connecticut had a significant interest in supporting regulated hunting, trapping and fishing. The Act was narrowly tailored to protect the act of taking of wildlife and left open ample alternative means of communication. Thus, the Act did not violate the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Maxwell v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


(SC 16567)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 143; 794 A.2d 535; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 131


November 28, 2001, Argued  
April 16, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant ordering the disclosure to the defendant Steven Edelman of certain of the plaintiff town of Windham's legal fee billing documents, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Wiese, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.

Maxwell v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 511 (Conn. Super. Ct. Feb. 15, 2001).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, town controller and town, appealed from a decision by defendant freedom of information commission ordering the disclosure to defendant citizen of certain of the town's legal fee billing documents. The matter was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut) affirmed the commission. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen requested disclosure by the plaintiffs of all of the town's legal bills, receipts, itemized statements and similar instruments since a certain date. The controller did not allow the citizen to view certain billing invoices of the town counsel because they involved pending litigation. The citizen subsequently filed a complaint with the commission requesting that plaintiffs be compelled to disclose the invoices. The supreme court held there were two issues. First, whether retroactive application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-146r would prevent the disclosure of certain documents pursuant to the Freedom of Information Act, specifically Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-210. Second, whether § 1-210(b)(10) unconstitutionally delegated to the freedom of information commission the authority to define the attorney-client privilege in violation of Connecticut's separation of powers doctrine. The supreme court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-146r, if applied retroactively, did not prevent the disclosure of the documents at issue, and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-210(b)(10) was constitutionally sound. The commission correctly concluded that the invoices were not exempt from disclosure.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Miranda


(SC 16271)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


260 Conn. 93; 794 A.2d 506; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 130


November 2, 2000, Argued  
April 16, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Miranda v. Connecticut, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6777 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Miranda v. Connecticut, 537 U.S. 902, 154 L. Ed. 2d 175, 123 S. Ct. 224, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6777 (2002)
Later proceeding at State v. Miranda, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3033 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with twenty-five counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and one count of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Fracasse, J.; judgment of guilty of one count of risk of injury to a child and six counts of assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Landau and Heiman, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty on the six counts of assault in the first degree, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which reversed the Appellate Court's judgment and remanded the case to that court for further proceedings; thereafter, the Appellate Court, Foti, Landau and Dupont, Js., reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty on the six counts of assault in the first degree, and, on the granting of certification, the state appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.

State v. Miranda, 56 Conn. App. 298, 742 A.2d 1276, 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 5 (2000).
State v. Miranda, 56 Conn. App. 298, 742 A.2d 1276, 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 5 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An Appellate Court (Connecticut) judgment reversed in part the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of six counts of assault in the first degree and one count of risk of injury to a child and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment of not guilty on the assault charges. The State appealed and defendant cross appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his girlfriend and her two children and was not the biological father of either child, but took care of them and considered himself to be their stepfather. Defendant's assault convictions were based on two separate acts of omission, which led to two, not six, discrete injuries to the baby daughter. As a result of defendant's failure to help, the child was exposed to conduct which created a risk of death to her and the child suffered subsequent serious physical injuries. Defendant had an affirmative duty to act and criminal liability was imposed for defendant's failure to act pursuant to that duty. The State's alleged failure to introduce sufficient evidence to prove that the mother had caused the victim's abuse did not mean that there was insufficient evidence on which to convict defendant under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(3). The evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that defendant was actually aware of and consciously disregarded the abuse. Double jeopardy was not violated since (1) there were two separate acts of omission; and (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-21, 53a-59(a)(3) were not the same offense for double jeopardy purposes.


OUTCOME: The supreme court remanded the case to the appellate court with direction to (1) affirm the trial court's judgment of guilty only as to two counts of assault in the first degree and one count of risk of injury to a child, and, (2) under the aggregate package theory of sentencing, to remand the case to the trial court to resentence defendant for those crimes to a term of not more than his original sentence of 40 years.

 

328 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hammond v. Comm'r of Corr.


(SC 16220)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 855; 792 A.2d 774; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 107


December 6, 2000, Argued  
March 26, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, W. Sullivan, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti, Spear and Hennessy, Js., which affirmed the habeas court's judgment, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

 [***2] Hammond v. Commissioner of Correction, 54 Conn. App. 11, 734 A.2d 571, 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 263 (1999).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: While serving a sentence for two crimes, defendant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, seeking presentence confinement credit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d for, inter alia, the period during which he was incarcerated in Massachusetts while contesting extradition to Connecticut. The Appellate Court, Connecticut, affirmed the habeas court's dismissal of the petition. Defendant appealed, and his petition for certification was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 18-98d entitled him to presentence confinement credit for the periods during which he was (1) incarcerated in Massachusetts before his extradition, (2) in transit from Massachusetts to Connecticut, and (3) confined at a Connecticut police department before his arraignment. Based on case law interpreting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98, which was a similar statute applicable to defendants who committed offenses prior to July 1, 1981, the state supreme court held that defendant was not entitled to the credit he sought. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d essentially authorized presentence credit for pretrial detainees whose confinement was subject to the control of the Connecticut Commissioner of Correction. Defendant was not subject to such control during any of the three periods for which he sought credit. Contrary to defendant's contentions, denial of the presentence credit at issue did not involve a fundamental right, and such denial did not violate defendant's substantive due process or equal protection rights, as there was a rational basis for distinguishing between detainees who were subject to the commissioner's control and discipline and those who were not.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

329 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Donahue v. Town of Southington


(SC 16497)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 783; 792 A.2d 76; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 109


October 30, 2001, Argued  
March 26, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the sixth district prohibiting the defendants from utilizing certain statutory weekly benefit tables in calculating the plaintiff's compensation rate and ordering the defendants to calculate the benefits manually, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Case was remanded with directions.  [***2] 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a town and its workers' compensation provider, appealed from a decision of the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the workers' compensation commissioner's approval of the use of a manual calculation method rather than the statutory compensation tables in calculating benefits for appellee, a workers' compensation claimant.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the use of wage tables in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-310(b) was limited to injured employees who contributed to the Federal Insurance Contributions Act (FICA) by the plain language of the statute, as well as its legislative history. The town had standing to appeal the workers' compensation review board's decision, basing its appeal on its own injury. The town was litigating a nonconstitutional issue, namely, the proper construction of § 31-310(b), and was affected adversely by the construction of that statute. Therefore, the town had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 31-310(b). The legislation neither created a suspect classification nor impinged upon a fundamental right for the purposes of the Equal Protection Clause. Thus, the constitutional challenge was analyzed under the rational basis test. Because there was a plausible reason for the legislature's action, the fact that the workers' compensation scheme set forth in § 31-310(b) ultimately resulted in a somewhat higher compensation rate for certain employees was of no constitutional import, and the statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the compensation review board with direction to establish the rate of interest and to calculate the amount of the award of interest pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-301c(b).

Aposporos v. Urban Redevelopment Comm'n


(SC 16450)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 563; 790 A.2d 1167; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 86


October 25, 2001, Argued  
March 5, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from taking by condemnation certain real property owned by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Novack, J., granted the plaintiffs' application for an ex parte temporary restraining order pending a hearing on the plaintiffs' application for temporary injunctive relief; thereafter, the court, Karazin, J., granted the motion of the city of Stamford to intervene as a party defendant; subsequently, the court, D'Andrea, J., granted the defendant's motion to stay the municipal and state regulations related to the acquisition of the plaintiffs' property; the plaintiffs thereafter filed an amended complaint against both the defendant and the intervening defendant and the matter was tried to the court, Ryan, J., on the request for both temporary and permanent injunctive relief; judgment for the defendant and the intervening defendant denying the injunctive relief, from which the plaintiffs appealed.

Aposporos v. Urban Redevelopment Comm'n of the City of Stamford, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2917 (Conn. Super. Ct. Oct. 31, 2000).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The instant court transferred to itself the appeal of plaintiff property owners from a judgment of the Superior Court, Stamford-Norwalk Judicial District (Connecticut), denying a permanent injunction against defendant city and its urban renewal commission's efforts to condemn their property.


OVERVIEW: Almost 40 years before the instant appeal, the city adopted a redevelopment plan proposed by its urban renewal commission. More than a decade after that, the property owners purchased a diner on land that was not included in the original redevelopment area. Many years later, in response to competition from a planned suburban mall, downtown merchants lobbied for and secured an updated redevelopment plan, now including the diner, and the city commenced condemnation proceedings. The high court held that despite the deference accorded to urban renewal commission findings, the owners' property was not validly condemned. It had never been determined to be blighted within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-125, and there was no evidence the blight findings in the original plan, which had concededly already been largely carried out, were still valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for entry of the injunctive relief sought.

State v. Aponte


(SC 16546)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 512; 790 A.2d 457; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 74


November 29, 2001, Argued  
February 26, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Landau, Zarella and Daly, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

 [***2] State v. Aponte, 63 Conn. App. 82, 774 A.2d 1035, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 202 (2001).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an appellate judgment that affirmed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, claiming that the jury instructions improperly shifted the burden of proof and deprived him of a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: After defendant and two others fired their weapons at the victim, defendant was convicted of murder and conspiracy to commit murder. He did not object to the jury instructions at trial, but claimed on appeal that they violated his constitutional rights. The state supreme court held that the intent instructions did not deprive him of a fair trial. Each element of the crimes of murder and conspiracy were set forth sufficiently and the jury was not misled. The trial court also instructed the jury on the state of mind required for conspiracy. Although the trial court's deadly weapon instruction was properly qualified, the permissive nature of the inference could have created juror misunderstanding. Therefore, future jury instructions were not to include the words that a defendant "will be deemed to have intended" the probable result of his acts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

332 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Russo


(SC 16430)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 436; 790 A.2d 1132; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 60


May 31, 2001, Argued  
February 19, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Writ of certiorari denied: Russo v. Connecticut, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6441 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Russo v. Connecticut, 537 U.S. 879, 154 L. Ed. 2d 134, 123 S. Ct. 79, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6441 (2002)
Related proceeding at Russo v. Glasser, 279 F. Supp. 2d 136, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14765 (D. Conn., 2003)
Appeal after remand at State v. Russo, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 211 (Conn. App. Ct., May 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with thirty-two counts each of the crimes of obtaining a controlled substance by forgery of a prescription and forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Schimelman, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court granted the state's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment dismissing the information, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the matter was transferred to this court.
State v. Russo, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2156 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 15, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Case remanded with direction to deny defendant's motion to suppress and for further proceedings.  [***2]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) judgment, after granting defendant's motion to suppress prescription records, dismissed a substitute information charging defendant with 32 counts each of the crimes of obtaining a controlled substance containing codeine, by forgery of a prescription and forgery in the second degree. The State's appeal was transferred by the appellate court to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's allegedly forged prescriptions were uncovered in connection with an investigation of the frequency with which a certain physician was prescribing controlled medications. The pharmacy consented to release of its prescription records to investigators without a search warrant. Defendant maintained that the release of his prescription records without a search warrant violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-265 and his Fourteenth Amendment right to privacy. The supreme court held that by its plain language, § 21a-265 affirmatively authorized federal, state, and local law enforcement personnel to review controlled substance prescription records subject to consideration of the pharmacist's constitutional rights. The investigator was acting with the police when he obtained defendant's prescription records and was authorized under § 21a-265, to obtain those records with the pharmacist's consent. Section 21a-265's statutory scheme, like New York's in Whalen, adequately safeguarded the privacy interests of persons who obtained prescriptions for controlled substances and § 21a-265 did not violate defendant's Fourteenth Amendment privacy rights.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with directions to deny defendant's motion to suppress and for further proceedings according to law.

 

333 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vega


(SC 16391)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 374; 788 A.2d 1221; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 56


October 23, 2001, Argued  
February 12, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Vega v. Connecticut, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6213 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Vega v. Connecticut, 537 U.S. 836, 123 S. Ct. 152, 154 L. Ed. 2d 56, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6213 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Vega v. Warden, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1794 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 25, 2005)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Vega, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3086 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Gormley, J., granted the state's motion in limine to introduce certain evidence of prior misconduct by the defendant; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to remove defense counsel and the matter was tried to the jury before Gormley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Superior Court, Fairfield (Connecticut), convicted defendant for assault in the first degree and kidnapping. He was sentenced to a total effective term of 60 years and appealed his conviction. The state's highest court transferred the appeal to its court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-1 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant held the victim captive and then brutalized her. The state's highest court held that defendant's constitutional rights were not violated and that the trial court properly admitted the expert testimony of the clinical social worker and defendant's prior misconduct. First, the trial court's inquiry was sufficient to establish that defendant's grievance against his counsel did show prejudice or adverse representation for a conflict of interest. Second, the social worker, as an expert on battered women's syndrome, provided the jury with a framework within which it could place and possibly explain the victim's alleged behavior. Third, the evidence of defendant's prior incidences of violence toward the victim was relevant as it corroborated the social worker's testimony. Moreover, the evidentiary substantiation of the vicious depravity of the conduct for which defendant was charged far outweighed the prejudicial impact of the prior misconduct. Finally, the police had reasonable cause to suspect that defendant was dangerous. Accordingly, searching the coat before placing it on defendant was reasonable under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Crockett v. Pastore


(SC 16481)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 240; 789 A.2d 453; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 37


September 26, 2001, Argued  
January 29, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff maternal grandmother seeking visitation rights with the defendant's minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Axelrod, J., ordered visitation rights be granted to the plaintiff, and the defendant appealed; thereafter, the court, Robaina, J., denied the defendant's motion to vacate the court order granting the visitation rights, and the defendant filed an amended appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An action was brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) by the plaintiff maternal grandmother seeking visitation rights with defendant father's minor child. The trial court ordered visitation rights be granted to the grandmother, and the father appealed. The trial court denied the father's motion to vacate its order, and the father filed an amended appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appeal concerned the constitutionality of the trial court's application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59, in awarding visitation rights with the father's minor child to the child's maternal grandmother. The father claimed that in light of the United States Supreme Court's decision in Troxel, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 was unconstitutional as applied to the facts of the case under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Tied to the challenge was his claim regarding the threshold issue of jurisdiction. The supreme court concluded that, because the grandmother failed to allege and establish that she had a parent-like relationship with the child and that the child would suffer real and significant harm if visitation with the grandmother were denied, the trial court improperly granted the visitation petition in contravention of the father's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to dismiss the petition.

Roth v. Weston


(SC 16565)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 202; 789 A.2d 431; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 36


September 26, 2001, Argued  
January 29, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff maternal grandmother and the plaintiff maternal aunt seeking visitation rights with the defendant's minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Hon. Romeo G. Petroni, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion to open the judgment and the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Romeo G. Petroni, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment granting visitation rights to the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed.

Roth v. Weston, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1182 (Conn. Super. Ct. Apr. 23, 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Remanded with direction to dismiss petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, maternal grandmother and maternal aunt, sought visitation rights with defendant father's minor children. A Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) granted plaintiffs' motion to open the judgment for the father and rendered judgment granting visitation rights to plaintiffs pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought visitation three months after the mother had committed suicide and did not contend that the father was in any way an unfit parent. The father objected to visitation with plaintiffs because he believed their morals, values, and ethics were inconsistent with his own and those that he wished to instill in his children, ages two and four. The supreme court addressed the issue of first impression, namely, whether § 46b-59 was constitutional under the Due Process Clauses of U.S. Const. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. The supreme court determined that § 46b-59 was unconstitutional as applied to the extent that the trial court, pursuant to § 46b-59, permitted third party visitation contrary to the desires of a fit parent and in the absence of any allegation and proof by clear and convincing evidence that the children would suffer actual and significant harm if deprived of the visitation. Plaintiffs also failed to establish that their ongoing relationship with the children rose to a requisite parental type level required under § 46b-59. The cited Troxel case expressed a parent's fundamental liberty interest in the care, custody, and control of his children.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with direction to dismiss the petition. The supreme court concluded that (1) the allegations were facially insufficient to demonstrate the required relationship for standing and to invoke properly the court's jurisdiction; and (2) the evidence could not, even under a generous interpretation, satisfy the requisite burden of persuasion that the supreme court articulated.

Cox Cable Advisory Council v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


(SC 16538)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


259 Conn. 56; 788 A.2d 29; 2002 Conn. LEXIS 8


September 13, 2001, Argued  
January 15, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of certiorari denied: Cox Cable Advisory Council v. Conn. Dep't of Public Util., 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5569 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision of the named defendant granting the defendant CoxCom Connecticut, Inc.'s application for renewal of its statewide cable television franchise, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the motions to dismiss filed by the named defendant and the defendant CoxCom Connecticut, Inc., and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.  [***2] 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cable company filed an application with defendant department for renewal of its franchise. The department offered to renew the franchise. Plaintiff council appealed to the superior court. The cable company moved to dismiss. The council filed an amended appeal. The department moved to dismiss. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Connecticut, dismissed the original appeal. The council appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the council claimed that its appeal was not preempted by the Cable Communications Policy Act of 1984, 47 U.S.C.S. § 521 et seq., the original appeal alleged sufficient facts to establish aggrievement, and the amended appeal should have been considered by the court. The supreme court held that federal law preempted parties other than cable operators from appealing the renewal of a franchise. The court noted that 47 U.S.C.S. §§ 546, 555 allow for judicial review of a franchise renewal in limited circumstances, none of which were present. The supreme court concluded that in light of congress's intent to limit the parties and circumstances under which review could be sought, the court could not conclude that there was otherwise an inherent right to appeal the terms and conditions of a franchise renewal. Although there was a state statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-2a(a), that enabled the council to appeal, the supreme court held that said statute could not control since the federal legislation restricted such a right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

OVERVIEW: The owner had been allowed to intervene by the superior court, and then was substituted as defendant by the appeals court after it concluded its purchase from the seller. Connelly v. Comm'r of Corr.


(SC 16277)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 374; 780 A.2d 890; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 376


November 30, 2000, Argued  
October 9, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and referred to Hon. Thomas H. Corrigan, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification,  [***2] appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that the 40-year sentence he received after a jury convicted him of two counts of kidnapping in the second degree and two counts of assault in the second degree violated his due process rights. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) dismissed the petition and the prisoner appealed. The state supreme court transferred the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was prosecuted in 1990 for kidnapping and assault, but he was acquitted by reason of lack of capacity. After that finding, the trial judge placed the prisoner in the custody of the Connecticut Commissioner of Mental Health for 10 years. In 1993, the prisoner filed a successful action to vacate the trial court's judgment, but as a result, he was retried. The state supreme court held that the prisoner's due process rights were not violated because he was convicted and sentenced to 40 years in prison after a second trial because (1) it was highly questionable whether his successful challenge to the first trial provided a proper predicate for application of the Pearce rule; and (2) even if the court assumed that the sentence imposed after the prisoner's second trial was greater than that imposed after his first trial, evidence cited by the second trial judge which showed, inter alia, that the prisoner refused to accept responsibility for his misconduct, lacked remorse for his crimes, and refused to acknowledge his mental illness was sufficient to justify the second sentence.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Whipper


(SC 16181)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 229; 780 A.2d 53; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 372


February 13, 2001, Argued  
October 2, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Whipper v. Warden, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 652 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 19, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder and felony murder and two counts each of the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of the crimes of murder, felony murder and manslaughter in the first degree, and two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) entered a judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting defendant of one count each of murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, manslaughter in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(1), and two counts of robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(3). Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous points of error. In response, the state supreme court held, first, that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to grant defendant a new trial, because the verdict was not based on conclusions that were scientifically impossible. Second, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's motion for a mistrial, because there was nothing in the record that demonstrated that the jury disregarded the trial court's instructions to ignore a certain expert's stricken testimony when it was deliberating. Third, the prosecutor's closing remarks, though improper, did not deprive defendant of due process and his constitutional right to a fair trial. Fourth, the representation of defendant's palm print as being bloody, though improper, was not so harmful that it likely affected the trial's result. Lastly, defendant's constitutional right against double jeopardy was violated, because he was convicted of intentional and felony murder of the same victim, and the jury was improperly instructed to find him guilty of intentional manslaughter in the first degree in the event that it found him guilty of intentional murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction of manslaughter in the first degree was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to: (1) vacate defendant's conviction of manslaughter in the first degree; (2) combine defendant's convictions of felony murder and intentional murder; and (3) vacate the sentence for defendant's felony murder conviction. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Burton


(SC 16348)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 153; 778 A.2d 955; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 369


March 21, 2001, Argued  
September 25, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, risk of injury to a child, criminal attempt to commit sexual assault in the third degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Richards, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, risk of injury to a child and criminal attempt to commit sexual assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) convicted defendant, upon a jury verdict, of first degree kidnapping, risk of injury to a child, and third degree criminal attempt to commit sexual assault, and imposed a total sentence of 20 years, execution suspended after 7 years, followed by 10 years of probation. Defendant appealed to the Appellate Court. The appeal was transferred to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 (Rev. to 1999) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the instant case; (2) the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the elements of risk of injury to a child; (3) the prosecutor's comments during his rebuttal argument were improper; and (4) the evidence was insufficient to prove that defendant had committed kidnapping in the first degree. The state supreme court held, first, that defendant was on sufficient notice that his conduct would be considered likely to impair the morals of the victim and, therefore, § 53-21 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the instant case. Second, the overinclusive jury charge did not deny defendant his due process rights, because jurors were well-equipped to analyze evidence that contained a factually inadequate theory. Third, the single impropriety in the prosecutor's comments was not sufficiently egregious to infect the whole trial. Finally, there was sufficient evidence of kidnapping, because the jury reasonably could have found that defendant used both physical force and intimidation to interfere with the victim's liberty and confine her to the car.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Queach Corp. v. Inland Wetlands Comm'n of Branford


(SC 16486)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 178; 779 A.2d 134; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 370


June 1, 2001, Argued  
September 25, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant amending certain inland wetlands and watercourses regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and referred to Hon. John T. Downey, judge trial referee, who granted the motion of the Connecticut Fund for the Environment, Inc., to intervene as a party defendant; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Blue, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which held that the amended regulations implemented by defendant, the Branford, Connecticut, Inland Wetlands Commission, the agency for defendant town, were valid. The Appellate Court granted certification to appeal, and the reviewing court transferred the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' preliminary application to alter property containing 55 acres of wetlands was rejected for reasons relating to excessive density. The landowners later challenged the amendments made by the commission to Branford, Conn., Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Regs. §§ 2.1jj, 2.1oo(5). The reviewing court held that the trial court property limited its review to the facial validity of the regulations. The regulations were within the scope of authority given a local agency to adopt regulations to carry out the purposes of the Connecticut Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Act. There was ample evidence for the commission to approve a 100-foot setback. The landowners failed to establish the invalidity of the regulations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

343 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


COBHAM v. COMMISSIONER OF CORRECTION


(SC 16393)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 30; 779 A.2d 80; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 361


May 24, 2001, Argued  
September 11, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Procedural History

Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Hon. Thomas H. Corrigan, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent corrections department noted confusion with petitioner's sentence, the trial court clarified the sentence. Petitioner challenged his sentence in an amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner appealed the petition's dismissal by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut). Upon certification, the appeal was transferred to the Connecticut Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contested his sentence three years after the sentence was imposed, alleging that the trial court improperly sentenced him to two consecutive mandatory minimum sentences. The appellate court held that the petition was premature. Since petitioner failed to file an appeal or a Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 43-22 motion challenging the sentence, and did not challenge his sentence or move to withdraw his plea before petitioning for a writ of habeas corpus, petitioner's claims were reviewed under the cause and prejudice standard of Wainwright. Petitioner failed to satisfy the cause and prejudice standard for the procedural default. He did not allege in his habeas petition or maintain before the habeas court that his failure to challenge his sentence before the trial court or on direct appeal had been caused by some objective factor external to his own defense and that the default was prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

344 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


(SC 16415)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


258 Conn. 1; 778 A.2d 186; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 356


May 30, 2001, Argued  
September 4, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of using a motor vehicle without the owner's permission and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Conway, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Conway, J.; at the end of the state's case, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal as to the charge of using a motor vehicle without the owner's permission; subsequently, the jury returned a verdict of guilty of criminal possession of a firearm, and the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Landau and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the Connecticut Appellate Court's reversal of defendant's conviction by the Hartford Superior Court for criminal possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant gave an account of his actions which conflicted with that of the State. The State asserted defendant drove up to a house in a car that was not his, got out of the car, went to the front door and subsequently walked away leaving a gun on the passenger seat of the car. Defendant stated he drove up to the house with another person in a different car in order to get a compact disk out of the car in question. He obtained the key to the car and was arrested before he could access the car. The appellate court held the defendant was entitled to an instruction on the doctrine of nonexclusive possession because there was a question as to who possessed the gun and thus reversed the trial court. The supreme court held defendant's version of events did not warrant such an instruction as he argued he never had possession, not that he had joint possession. The State's version also did not support joint possession because the State argued defendant either was sitting on the gun or set it on the seat and thus was in sole possession.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

 

345 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammond


(SC 16424)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 610; 778 A.2d 108; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 351


May 30, 2001, Argued  
August 21, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine, possession of heroin, possession of heroin with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of heroin with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of cocaine, possession of heroin, possession of heroin with intent to sell as a lesser offense included in the charge of possession of heroin with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, and possession of heroin with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, Zarella and Spallone, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment convicting him of possession of cocaine, possession of heroin, possession of heroin with intent to sell, and possession of heroin with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, and sentencing him. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the convictions. The reviewing court granted defendant's petition for certification to appeal questions regarding the seizure and double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: An anonymous caller told police that drug sales were taking place at a church in an area known for previous drug sales. Officers saw subjects matching the description, but neither saw any conduct indicative of narcotics-related activity. After officer surrounded the subjects, defendant dropped a bundle to the ground. The bundle contained narcotics. The reviewing court held that the tip contained no predictive information, and the police could not test the caller's knowledge and credibility. The officers had been unable to corroborate the allegations of drug dealing during their close surveillance. The description of the clothes was only partial. Thus, the evidence should have been suppressed, and defendant's statement was fruit of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with direction to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to the trial court with direction to grant the motion to suppress. The certified question on whether the appellate court properly found that defendant was not illegally seized was answered in the negative.

State v. Spillane


(SC 16215)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 750; 778 A.2d 101; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 355



August 17, 2001, Motion Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of larceny in the third degree, risk of injury to a child and reckless endangerment in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain,  [***2] geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Susco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Spear and Healey, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial; the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court, which reversed the Appellate Court's judgment; subsequently, the defendant filed a motion for reconsideration and reconsideration en banc.

Original Opinion of April 24, 2000, Reported at: 2001 Conn. LEXIS 116.



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration granted, relief denied; reconsideration en banc denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the trial court convicted defendant of larceny in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-124(a). The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed and ordered a remand. The State appealed and was granted certification. The reviewing court reversed the appellate court's judgment. Defendant moved for reconsideration and reconsideration en banc of certain claims.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a towing company and was charged with larceny when he improperly towed a vehicle from the street. The intermediate appellate court found that in its instruction to the jury on the elements of larceny the trial court improperly omitted the definition of the term "appropriate" set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-118(a)(4)(B). The Supreme Court of Connecticut concluded that the evidence in the State's case-in-chief was sufficient to support the judgment of guilty of larceny in the third degree. Thus, it did not need to review the waiver rule.


OUTCOME: The motion for reconsideration was granted, but the relief requested is denied; reconsideration en banc was denied.

 

347 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


City Recycling, Inc. v. State


(SC 16418)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 429; 778 A.2d 77; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 322; 53 ERC (BNA) 1374


April 25, 2001, Argued  
August 14, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a statute prohibiting the commissioner of environmental protection from authorizing the construction of a new volume reduction plant within one-quarter mile of a child day care center in a municipality with a population of greater than 100,000 persons, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Hickey, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved two questions of law for the advice of this court, which declined to answer the reserved questions and remanded the case for further proceedings for a determination of whether the plaintiff's proposed expansion posed any environmental hazards; on remand, the court, D'Andrea, J., filed findings of fact and a memorandum of decision in favor of the plaintiff finding that the proposed expansion presented no reasonable possibility of environmental hazards and, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, again reserved two questions of law for the advice of this court.



DISPOSITION: With respect to the reserved questions: We decline to answer the first question; we answer the second question in the affirmative. The [***2] case is remanded for further proceedings according to law. No costs will be taxed in this court to any party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recycling company had sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-208a(a) (as amended by 1997 Conn. Acts No. 97-300, § 2). After remand by the Supreme Court of Connecticut, the trial court filed findings of fact, issued a memorandum of decision in favor of the company, and reserved two questions of law for the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The company had purchased a building and was altering it to accept additional recylables. It had passed several levels of local review and appeared on its way to obtaining permission to implement its volume reduction facility. However, legislation was enacted prohibiting such a facility within one quarter mile of a child day care center in a city of greater than 100,000 population. The company was the only company affected in the state by the legislation. The trial court found there was no evidence of any possible adverse environmental impact. The supreme court held there was no rational basis for the legislation as it was not related to any legitimate state interest. The language of the legislation along with its legislative history indicated the company was specifically targeted. Therefore, the legislation was unconstitutional in that it violated the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The statute was declared unconstitutional as it violated the equal protection doctrine.

State v. McMahon


(SC 16322)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 544; 778 A.2d 847; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 333


May 22, 2001, Argued  
August 14, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 19, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 684.
Writ of certiorari denied McMahon v. Connecticut, 534 U.S. 1130, 122 S. Ct. 1069, 151 L. Ed. 2d 972, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 684 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed McMahon v. Warden, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 286 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 3, 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied McMahon v. Lantz, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90399 (D. Conn., June 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with one count each of the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, criminal trespass in the third degree, illegal hunting of deer and hunting on Sunday, three counts of the crime of illegal hunting of deer with a firearm, and two counts of the crime of violation of hunting regulations, and, in the second part, with commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Kaplan, J.; verdict of guilty on all counts of the first part of the information; thereafter, the defendant pleaded guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-55(a)(3), 53a-55a, and imposed a total effective sentence of 35 years of incarceration, with execution suspended after 19 years, and 5 years of probation. Although defendant was also convicted and sentenced for other offenses, he appealed only the manslaughter conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from a hunting incident that caused the victim's death. On appeal, the state supreme court held, first, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the instant case because, in light of the plain meaning and judicial interpretations of the phrases "extreme indifference to human life" and "grave risk of death," a person of ordinary intelligence would have had fair warning that defendant's actions were proscribed under § 53a-55(a)(3). Second, on the basis of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k's plain language, its legislative history, and prior court decisions, the application of § 53-202k's sentence enhancement to first degree manslaughter with a firearm, a Class B felony, did not violate double jeopardy. Third, on the basis of § 53-202k's language and its legislative history, the trial court properly applied § 53-202k's sentence enhancement to defendant's split sentence. Finally, the State proved that defendant's culpable mental state had risen beyond the level required for a finding of mere negligence to the level of aggravated recklessness required for a finding of first degree manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Zeoli v. Norwalk Hosp.

Bd. of Educ. v. Town of Naugatuck


(SC 16399)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 409; 778 A.2d 862; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 341


March 23, 2001, Argued  
August 14, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of certain amendments to the named defendant's charter regarding the plaintiff's budget and membership, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Shortall, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, Schaller and Spear, Js., which dismissed the appeal, vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court with direction to render judgment dismissing the plaintiff's action for mootness, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory judgment to determine the validity of certain amendments to defendant town's charter, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) granted plaintiff board of education summary judgment. The town appealed to the Appellate Court, which dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and remanded the case to the trial court to dismiss action as moot. The instant appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue was whether a dispute regarding the legality of certain provisions of the town's charter was rendered moot as a result of subsequent amendments to the charter. The board sought a declaratory judgment invalidating two amendments to the town charter that had been adopted in 1996. The supreme court concluded that the actual controversy recognized by both the parties and the trial court survived 1998 amendments to the town charter and remained in existence. Because the 1998 amendments did not cure the alleged underlying defects with respect to these two provisions, there remained an actual controversy capable of, and requiring, adjudication. The substantive validity of the disputed charter provisions was a matter capable of judicial resolution. Because a controversy regarding the charter provisions remained in effect, and because the board articulated a request for specific relief, the trial court was able to afford practical relief. Because the challenged portions of those provisions, as amended in 1996, were unchanged by the 1998 ordinance, the dispute regarding their legality remained justiciable.


OUTCOME: The supreme court concluded that the controversy was not moot and reversed the judgment of the Appellate Court.

 

351 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Genden v. Am. Airlines


(SC 16454)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 520; 778 A.2d 58; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 342


March 20, 2001, Argued  
August 14, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the named defendant et al. from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district determining that the issue of whether the plaintiff had a preexisting condition so as to merit the transfer of liability for the plaintiff's disability benefits to the defendant second injury fund had to be referred to a statutorily authorized medical panel, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the named defendant et al. appealed to the Appellate Court, which, sua sponte, ordered supplemental briefing on the issue of whether the appeal was moot and whether there was a final judgment; thereafter, the appeal was transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district (Connecticut). The employer claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349c(a) violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 10. The fund argued that the employer's claim was moot in light of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349h.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee injured his back during the course of his employment. The injury was found to be compensable under the workers' compensation act, and compensation was paid by the employer and its insurer. The employer then sought to transfer the claim to the second injury fund, claiming that the employee had a preexisting physical impairment. The fund argued that, even though Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349c(a) precluded an appeal to the commissioner from the decision of the physician panel, the employer should have waited until after that decision was issued to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. However, the ripeness of the constitutional claim was irrelevant to the question of whether the commissioner or the board had jurisdiction to decide the claim, because those bodies did not have jurisdiction to consider constitutional claims. By the time the board issued its opinion, the physician panel had issued its decision. Thus, the claim was ripe at the time of the appeal to the court. The existence of a decision by the physician panel was a ripeness issue that affected only the jurisdiction of the reviewing court, not the finality of the board's decision.


OUTCOME: For the reasons set forth in Giaimo, the decision of the board was reversed and the case was remanded to the board with direction to remand it to the commissioner for further proceedings according to law.

Giaimo v. City of New Haven


(SC 16460)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 481; 778 A.2d 33; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 339


March 20, 2001, Argued  
August 14, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the named defendant et al. from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district denying the request by the named defendant et al. for a formal hearing on the finding of a statutorily authorized medical panel that the plaintiff did not have a preexisting disability for purposes of transfer to the defendant second injury fund of liability for disability benefits awarded to the plaintiff, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the named defendant et al. appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A workers' compensation review board (Connecticut) decision affirmed denial of defendant city employer's application to transfer its liability for plaintiff policeman employee's workers' compensation claim to defendant second injury fund pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349 (Rev. to 1987) and based upon the employee's preexisting medical condition. The employer's appeal was transferred by and to the supreme court from the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The treating physician opined that the employee's preexisting coronary artery disease was the necessary substrate upon which the employee's work activities acted as a catalyst to precipitate the heart attack. The supreme court (1) interpreted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-349h to determine the issues were ripe and not moot, (2) concluded that when a due process claim was raised by an applicant for a statutory benefit, the applicant had a protected property interest in the benefit when, under the governing statute, here the decision-making body would have no discretion to deny the application if the applicant could establish at a hearing that it met the statutory criteria, (3) decided that under 31-349(a), the commissioner did not have such discretion if statutory criteria were met, so the employer had a protectible property interest in a transfer of liability to the fund, (4) gave its reasons for concluding that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 349c(a) violated state and federal due process since the procedures applied to this case did not comply with minimal requirements, and (5) summarized minimal procedural and review requirements to correct clearly erroneous findings.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the board and remanded the case to the board with direction to remand the case to the workers' compensation commissioner for further proceedings according to law.

 

353 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Leydon v. Town of Greenwich


(SC 16356), (SC 16357)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


257 Conn. 318; 777 A.2d 552; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 321


March 15, 2001, Argued  
July 26, 2001, * Officially Released


* July 26, 2001, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from limiting the use of the defendant town's recreational beach park area to town residents, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Karazin, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Lavery and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to render judgment for the plaintiff, and the named defendant et al. and the defendant Lucas Point Association, Inc., on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals with this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to enjoin defendants from limiting the use of the defendant town's recreational beach park area to town residents, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) ruled for the defendants, from which plaintiff individual appealed to the Appellate Court, which reversed the judgment and remanded the case. The town and defendant association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether a municipality could constitutionally restrict access to a municipal park to its residents and their guests. The instant court concluded that such a restriction was prohibited by the First Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4, 5, and 14, based on the federal and state constitutional guarantees of freedom of expression and freedom of association. The court first examined the individual's claim that the ordinance violated the First Amendment as applied and on its face. In view of the facility's amenities it was clear that it qualified as a park for First Amendment purposes. The town lawfully could not bar the individual solely because he was a nonresident, because the park was a public forum. Because the town's ordinance restricting the park's use by nonresidents could not be justified on the ground that it was narrowly tailored to meet a compelling need, it was facially overbroad. The challenged ordinance also unquestionably violated the individual's right to engage in protected expressive and associational activities under the more speech protective test adopted for purposes of §§ 4, 5, and 14.


OUTCOME: Judgement was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with direction.
