State v. Pappas


(SC 16257)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 854; 776 A.2d 1091; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 284


November 1, 2000, Argued  
July 24, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Schimelman, J., denied the defendant's motion  [***2] to suppress and his motions in limine to exclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict of guilty of robbery in the third degree and larceny in the second degree; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty of being a persistent  [***3] serious felony offender and the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of third degree robbery and second degree larceny. Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-123(a), 133, 136(a). Defendant pled guilty to being a persistent felony offender. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) entered judgment accordingly, and defendant appealed. The appeal was transferred.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was identified as the robber of a bank. Police observed defendant, who fit the robber's description, running along railroad tracks. An officer observed cash scattered along the tracks. The reviewing court held that the motion to suppress hair samples was properly denied because the affidavit supporting the warrant was sufficient to establish probable cause to seize hairs from defendant. Thus, a Franks hearing was not necessary. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to exclude mitochondrial deoxyribonucleic acid (mtDNA) evidence on the basis that it was sufficiently reliable under the Daubert standard. Its probative value was not outweighed by undue prejudice. The trial court's limiting instruction cured any prejudice arising from hearsay testimony, and the hearsay was cumulative of other properly admitted evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Thalheim v. Town of Greenwich


(SC 16363)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 628; 775 A.2d 947; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 274


April 18, 2001, Argued  
July 17, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Writ of error from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Karazin, J., imposing certain sanctions on the plaintiff in error for his alleged violation of the rules of practice; thereafter, this court granted the motion to intervene as defendant in error filed by the attorney general. Writ of error dismissed.



DISPOSITION: The writ of error is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error attorney filed a writ of error appealing the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Connecticut) which dismissed the attorney's appeal of a trial court order which imposed sanctions on the attorney for filing an amicus brief in a case without first obtaining permission from the court or filing an appearance in an underlying case.


OVERVIEW: In an underlying matter, an attorney filed an amicus brief. The attorney did not receive permission from the trial court, nor did he file an appearance in the matter, and the trial court issued an order directing the attorney to show cause why he should not be sanctioned under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-84 for filing an amicus curiae brief without following the rules of practice. The trial court informed the attorney that it was his burden to show the court which rule he had followed in filing the brief. The trial court sanctioned the attorney, and the attorney appealed. The intermediate court dismissed the appeal because the attorney was not a party to the underlying action, and the attorney filed a writ of error. The appellate court found that because no fundamental right had been implicated, the attorney's facial challenge failed. Further, the appellate court found that the attorney was adequately warned and on notice that court permission was required prior to the filing of an amicus brief in the trial court. Therefore, he was expected to have superior knowledge on court procedure based on his status as an attorney and his ability to access literature on court procedure.


OUTCOME: The writ of error was dismissed.

State v. Revelo


(SC 16226)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 494; 775 A.2d 260; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 226


October 26, 2000, Argued  
June 26, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 26, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10800.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of the sale of cocaine and with one count each of the crimes of operating a drug factory and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Gill, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to one count of the sale of cocaine; subsequently, the remaining charges were nolled and the court, Damiani, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the defendant's plea of nolo contendere, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Foti and Landau, Js., with Shea, J., dissenting, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Connecticut) which affirmed a trial court's judgment finding defendant guilty of one count of the sale of cocaine in accordance with defendant's nolo contendere plea, and sentenced defendant to a nine-year prison term.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction for sale of cocaine defendant appealed, contending that the trial court erred by participating in plea negotiations and offering defendant one sentence but threatening a longer sentence if defendant pursued his motion to suppress evidence. The court of appeals affirmed, finding defendant waived his right to appeal such issues by his guilty plea. Defendant petitioned for certification to the highest court. On certification, the appellate court found that defendant's due process claim did merit appellate review and, furthermore, that the plea agreement and resulting imposition of the nine year sentence did not satisfy the requirements of due process. The appellate court found, further, that the trial court, in wielding its power as it did, discharged its sentencing function in a manner that was legally indistinguishable from the kind of unilateral imposition of a penalty upon a defendant who has chosen to exercise a legal right that has been held unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed with instructions to remand the case to the trial court on the issue of defendant's sentence.

 

357 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hill


(SC 16370)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 412; 773 A.2d 931; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 203


January 9, 2001, Argued  
June 12, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the court, Harper, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed revocation of his probation by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield, geographical area number two (Connecticut), claiming that the violation was not wilful. The Supreme Court of Connecticut granted transfer of the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assaulting his wife. The State agreed to drop the charge, when he pleaded guilty to a charge of failure to appear. His sentence was suspended and he was placed on probation. After violating the probation, he was incarcerated. When his incarceration ended, he was again placed on probation with the condition that he attended meetings at an alternative to incarceration center. After he missed several meetings, his probation was revoked. He claimed on appeal that the violation was not wilful. The supreme court held that because willfulness was not a specific requirement of the statute, any violation would result in revocation. The trial court's findings were not clearly erroneous or an abuse of discretion because defendant knew the conditions of his probation and he was no longer a good risk. His behavior was inimical to public safety.


OUTCOME: The revocation was affirmed.

 

358 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Andresen


(SC 16437)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 313; 773 A.2d 328; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 180


March 22, 2001, Argued  
May 29, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with five counts each of the crimes of the sale of unregistered securities and securities fraud, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Hiller, J.; judgment of guilty of five counts of the sale of unregistered securities, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of five counts of selling unregistered securities, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36b-16 (Rev. to 1995), after a bench trial in the superior court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), and she appealed. The state supreme court transferred the appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with selling unregistered securities and with securities fraud, in violation of the Connecticut Uniform Securities Act (CUSA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 36b-2 to 36b-33, after she sold shares in a company which her husband and two other people incorporated in Delaware. Evidence showed that the corporation's securities were not registered in Connecticut, and that defendant sold securities after Connecticut authorities issued a cease and desist order. The appellate court held that (1) the offense of willfully selling an unregistered security required proof that defendant sold or offered a security in Connecticut, that the security was not registered under CUSA, and that defendant had a general criminal intent; and that (2) although defendant could have avoided conviction by showing that securities she sold were exempt under state statute from registration requirements, defendant carried the burden of raising the exemption as an affirmative of defense, and of proving the exemption by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

359 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Modern Cigarette, Inc. v. Town of Orange


(SC 16259)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 105; 774 A.2d 969; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 122


September 27, 2000, Argued  
May 8, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the validity of a municipal ordinance adopted by the named defendant banning all cigarette vending machines within its borders, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Pittman, J., granted the state of Connecticut's motion to intervene as a defendant; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Silbert, J.; judgment for the plaintiff declaring the ordinance invalid, from which the defendants and the intervening defendant filed a joint appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tobacco product distributor sued defendant town for declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the validity of Orange, Conn., Ordinance Regulating Advertising Tobacco Related Products & Prohibiting Cigarette Vending Machines Town Orange (May 18, 1998). Intervening defendant State was allowed to intervene. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), ruled for plaintiff. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff operated about 100 cigarette vending machines throughout intervening defendant State, and one was in defendant town. Defendant town adopted Orange, Conn., Ordinance Regulating Advertising Tobacco Related Products & Prohibiting Cigarette Vending Machines Town Orange (May 18, 1998) banning all such machines within its borders. Plaintiff removed its one machine from defendant town, sued, and won. On appeal, the Connecticut Supreme Court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-289a, regulating the placement of such machines, did not preempt the ordinance. Merely because intervening defendant stopped short of imposing a ban on cigarette vending machines did not translate into an intent by the legislature to preserve the vending machine industry. There was no clear legislative intent to preclude local action. Defendant's power to regulate was derived from its general public health powers in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(7)(H)(xi), not just from Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-289a(h). The ordinance was consistent with intervening defendant's objective in limiting youth access to tobacco products.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and judgment was directed for defendants.

 

360 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



State v. Kelly


(SC 16020)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


256 Conn. 23; 770 A.2d 908; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 121


December 8, 1999, Argued  
May 8, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Tierney, J., who, at the close of the state's case, granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal of kidnapping in the first degree; subsequently, the jury returned a verdict of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree and the court rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Stamford-Norwalk Superior Court (Connecticut) which rendered judgment on the verdict, after a jury found defendant guilty of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a), and sentenced defendant to 20 years imprisonment, execution suspended after 16 years, and 10 years probation. The supreme court transferred the appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, the trial court: (1) improperly denied his pretrial motion to sequester the jury due to pretrial publicity surrounding the case; (2) improperly denied his motion in limine to preclude the state from offering evidence of his flight from the country; and (3) violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws by imposing a 10 year probationary period. The supreme court concluded the trial court's decision not to sequester the jury did not constitute an abuse of its discretion because there was nothing in the record to suggest the trial atmosphere was utterly corrupted by media coverage. Further, the supreme court found that because the jury reasonably could have inferred a guilty conscience motivated defendant's flight, the evidence was relevant and admissible. Finally, the supreme court agreed the trial court violated the constitutional prohibition on ex post facto laws. By employing Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-29 (as amended), the trial court improperly imposed "additional punishment," more than that which was prescribed at the time of the offense.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment with respect to the imposition of a 10 year probationary period and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to reduce the term of probation from 10 years to five years. The supreme court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.


 

361 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spillane


(SC 16215)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 746; 770 A.2d 898; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 116


October 26, 2000, Argued  
April 24, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Reconsideration Granted, Relief Denied, Reconsideration En Banc Denied August 17, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Conn. LEXIS 355.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of larceny in the third degree, risk of injury to a child and reckless endangerment in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Susco, J.; judgment of guilty of larceny in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Spear and Healey, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the trial court convicted defendant of larceny in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-124(a). The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed and ordered a remand. The State appealed and was granted certification.


OVERVIEW: The defendant operated a towing company and was charged with larceny when he improperly towed a vehicle from the street. The intermediate appellate court found that in its instruction to the jury on the elements of larceny the trial court improperly omitted the definition of the term "appropriate" set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-118(a)(4)(B). The Supreme Court of Connecticut found that the dictionary meaning of the word "appropriate" was different from the definition in § 53a-118(a)(4)(B), and therefore the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on the statutory meaning of the word was error of constitutional magnitude. However, since the defendant had not brought forth facts at trial contesting this element, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The defendant also argued that the waiver rule was unconstitutional, but as he had failed to provide a complete record, the Connecticut Supreme Court declined to address this argument. Since the defendant failed to provide a complete record, his argument on sufficiency of the evidence was not addressed. Finally, there was no permanency element required under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-118(a)(4)(B).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case remanded to that court to consider the defendant's remaining grounds for appeal.

 

362 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Joyner


(SC 16297)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 477; 774 A.2d 927; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 66


September 20, 2000, Argued  
March 20, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the second degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Licari, J., granted the defendant's motion to exclude from evidence certain of the alleged victim's testimony from a prior proceeding; thereafter, based upon the state's representation that it would not be able to proceed on the sexual assault counts without the excluded evidence, the court dismissed those counts of the information, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) granting defendant's motion to exclude certain evidence and then dismissing the sexual assault counts against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree. He subsequently filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which was granted on the grounds that his trial counsel had a conflict of interest and had provided ineffective assistance. A new trial was ordered. In the interim, the victim died. Defendant then filed a motion to exclude the victim's testimony from the new trial, which was granted. The sexual assault claims were dismissed. The appellate court reversed. First, plaintiff State's willingness to have the charges dismissed provided the necessary assurance that the procedure had not been resorted to lightly. Next, the dismissal of the sexual assault charges constituted a final judgment. Finally, a finding of inadequate cross-examination was not necessary to either the habeas court's conflict of interest finding or its ineffective assistance of counsel finding.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed because there were assurances that the appellate procedure was not taken lightly, dismissal of the sexual assault charges was a final appealable order, and a finding of inadequate cross examination was not necessary to the habeas court's other findings.

 

363 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ferreira v. Pringle


(SC 16229)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 330; 766 A.2d 400; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 30


November 3, 2000, Argued  
February 13, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the plaintiff as a result of the alleged negligence of the defendants, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Mihalakos, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and rendered judgment thereon for the defendants; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion to reargue and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut), granting defendant municipality's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, in plaintiff's action alleging that defendant created or had participated in the creation or maintenance of a public nuisance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action against defendant municipality, alleging that defendant created or had participated in the creation or maintenance of a public nuisance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n(a)(1)(A). The trial court dismissed plaintiff's action, holding that plaintiff's exclusive remedy for his injuries was under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, and the complaint was legally insufficient because he failed to plead under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149 and he failed to comply with its notice requirements. Plaintiff appealed, claiming that his injury was not caused by a highway defect under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, which was also unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed, holding that plaintiff's exclusive remedy for his injuries was under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, and because plaintiff did not comply with the notice provisions, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the action, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed because plaintiff's exclusive remedy for his injuries was under the state highway defect statute, plaintiff did not comply with the notice provisions, and the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

364 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


(SC 16258)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 268; 764 A.2d 1251; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 16


September 29, 2000, Argued  
January 30, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Wiese, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, DiPentima, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to possession of narcotics with intent to sell and failure to appear in the first degree; subsequently, the remaining charge was nolled and the court, DiPentima, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the plea, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction on charges of possession of narcotics with intent to sell under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) and failure to appear under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172(a)(1) and the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress cocaine seized pursuant to a warrantless patdown search for weapons.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the trial court properly denied the defendant's motion to suppress cocaine seized from his socks pursuant to a warrantless patdown search for weapons. The defendant claims that the search and seizure violated his constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9. Defendant contended that his initial detention and patdown was not based upon a reasonable and articulable suspicion that he had committed or was about to commit a crime. The Supreme Court of Connecticut disagreed and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Specifically, the appellate court found that the bulge in the defendant's sock added to the officer's reasonable suspicions that the defendant was either carrying a weapon or was in the process of committing a felony. Accordingly, the arrest itself was supported by probable cause, therefore, the search of the defendant's sock and the seizure of cocaine therefrom were sufficiently contemporaneous with his arrest so as to qualify as a search incident to a lawful arrest. Accordingly, the trial court properly denied the defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress cocaine seized from his socks pursuant to a warrantless patdown search for weapons was affirmed where the arresting officer had sufficient, objective reasons for believing that the defendant was involved in drug trafficking and that, because of that connection, he might have been armed and dangerous.

Gangemi v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


(SC 16208)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 143; 763 A.2d 1011; 2001 Conn. LEXIS 1


June 1, 2000, Argued  
January 2, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiffs' application to invalidate a certain condition of a previously granted variance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Gormley, J., granted the motion to intervene as defendants filed by Judith Kramer et al.; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, White, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court, Landau, Schaller and Daly, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a grant of certification, plaintiffs appealed a decision by the Appellate Court (Connecticut) which affirmed a decision by defendant denying plaintiffs' application to invalidate a no-rental condition of a previously granted zoning variance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs obtained a zoning variance to allow them to enlarge their nonconforming beach house. The variance granted contained a no-rental condition. Plaintiffs later sought to invalidate the no-rental condition, and defendant zoning board denied the application. The trial court and appellate court affirmed, and plaintiff appealed the decisions after a grant of certification. The court held the continued maintenance of the no-rental condition violated a strong public policy against restrictions on free alienability of property. The court noted that under Fairfield, Connecticut, Zoning Regulations § 11.1.1, beach property was limited to a single detached dwelling for one family, which could not be occupied by more than four unrelated persons. The regulations did not preclude renting of beach property. Under zoning regulations, plaintiffs were prevented from renting the property on a year-round basis rather than seasonally. The condition also reduced the value of the property, as the house would bring less when sold due to the inability to rent it. The court noted that the no-rental condition did not apply to any other property in the area.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision, because the continued maintenance of the no-rental condition violated a strong public policy in favor of free and unrestricted alienability of property.

 

366 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Seymour v. Elections Enforcement Comm'n


(SC 16167)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


255 Conn. 78; 762 A.2d 880; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 431


December 9, 1999, Argued  
December 19, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 4994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant finding, inter alia, that the plaintiffs had violated certain provisions of the state elections laws and ordering prospective compliance therewith, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, McWeeny, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) affirming defendant elections commission's decision finding that plaintiffs had violated the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-333w(a) campaign law and ordering plaintiffs' future compliance with that provision.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff election candidates contested in the trial court a decision of defendant elections commission finding that plaintiffs had violated the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-333w(a) campaign law and ordering plaintiffs' future compliance with that provision. The trial court affirmed and plaintiffs appealed, contending that § 9-333w(a) was violative of U.S. Const. amend. I, that defendant's handling of the relevant complaints violated plaintiffs' constitutional rights, and that defendant's composition violated Connecticut's separation of powers doctrine. The court affirmed. Section 9-333w(a) was constitutional because it was narrowly tailored to serve the state's compelling interests in preventing corruption in candidate elections, advancing the state's ability to investigate campaign finance laws, providing the electorate with information, and deterring fraud. Defendant had not violated plaintiffs' constitutional rights via its handling of the relevant complaints. The composition of defendant did not violate Connecticut's separation of powers doctrine, as, in Connecticut, the appointment of high ranking state officers was not exclusively under the control of the executive branch.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was affirmed. Composition of defendant elections commission did not violate Connecticut's separation of powers doctrine since appointment of high ranking state officers was not exclusively under the control of the executive branch.

 

367 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ramos v. Town of Vernon


(SC 16152)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


254 Conn. 799; 761 A.2d 705; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 387


May 31, 2000, Argued  
November 21, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of the named defendant's nighttime curfew ordinance, and for other relief, brought to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut, and tried to the court, Nevas, J.; judgment determining that the ordinance did not violate the United States constitution; thereafter, the court certified to this court questions of law concerning the constitutionality of the ordinance under certain provisions of the Connecticut constitution.
Ramos v. Town of Vernon, 48 F. Supp. 2d 176, 1999 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7288 (D. Conn., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Answer to certified questions one through six is: No.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the District of Connecticut, with plaintiffs' appeal pending in the federal court of appeals, certified six questions to the court in plaintiffs', mother and minor son, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendant town for a declaration that its nighttime juvenile curfew, Vernon, Conn., Ordinance § 8-4, violated plaintiffs' Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 4, 5, 7, 8, 9, 10, 14, and 20 rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant town enacted Vernon, Conn., Ordinance § 8-4, a nighttime juvenile curfew. Plaintiffs, mother and minor son, challenged § 8-4 under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The federal district court upheld § 8-4 as to the federal constitution and certified to the court six questions whether § 8-4 violated Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 4, 5, 7, 8, 9, 10, 14, and 20. The court answered all questions "no," in defendant's favor. Section 8-4's provision that plaintiff son might have had to face juvenile authorities gave him standing to sue. The court read § 8-4's exemption for minors exercising U.S. Const. amend. I rights at night to apply to similar state constitutional rights. Although the Connecticut Constitution potentially protected individual rights more than the federal constitution, the burden was on plaintiffs to detail such an argument and plaintiffs did not show that § 8-4 violated rights that went beyond those provided by the federal constitution. Suspected violation of § 8-4 itself justified police seizure of such suspects. Section 8-4 was not overbroad nor too vague, nor violative of equal protection, due process, free speech, assembly, personal liberty, or search and seizure rights.


OUTCOME: Certified questions were all answered "no," in defendant's favor. Plaintiffs failed to carry their burden to detail how curfew violated rights beyond those given them in the federal constitution. Suspected violation of the curfew itself justified police seizure of such suspects. The curfew ordinance was not overbroad, too vague, nor violative of equal protection, due process, free speech, assembly, or personal liberty rights.

 

368 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gibbs


(SC 15943)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


254 Conn. 578; 758 A.2d 327; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 292


June 1, 2000, Argued  
September 19, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As corrected January 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and one count of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Spada, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain District (Connecticut), convicting him of two counts of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, and one count of capital felony in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, and one count of capital felony in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(8), and was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of release. On appeal, the court rejected all of defendant's claims and affirmed. An alleged underrepresentation of Hispanics in the jury array did not violate defendant's constitutional rights to a jury made up of a fair cross section of the community or to equal protection of the law. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-217(a)(3) (Rev. to 1995), which disqualified non-English speaking persons from serving on juries, and the death qualification of the jury did not violate his rights. The State's evidence was sufficient to meet its burden of proving every element of § 53a-54b(8) beyond a reasonable doubt because, although the murders were separated by several hours, they took place in the course of a single transaction. Defendant's motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds was properly denied because defendant had no authority to make the motion pro se while represented by counsel.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; the contested jury selection procedures did not violate defendant's rights, the evidence was sufficient to convict him of capital felony because the two murders took place in the course of a single transaction, and defendant could not make pro se motion to dismiss while represented by counsel.

 

369 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Murphy


(SC 16282)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


254 Conn. 561; 757 A.2d 1125; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 291


May 24, 2000, Argued  
September 12, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with one count of the crime of harassment in the second degree and two counts of the crime of criminal attempt to commit harassment in the second degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, and tried to the jury before Dranginis, J., on the first part of the information; verdict of guilty of one count of criminal attempt to commit harassment in the second degree; thereafter, the court declared a mistrial on the second count of criminal attempt to commit harassment in the second degree; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury on the second part of the information; verdict of guilty of being a persistent offender; the court thereafter rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdicts, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction of criminal attempt to commit harassment in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-183(a)(2), 53a-49, by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield, Geographical Area Number 18 (Connecticut), which subsequently also found him guilty of being a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40d persistent offender for contacting his ex-girlfriend by mail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of assault for domestic violence against victim girlfriend. Later defendant forced her to have intercourse with him and a protective order issued prohibiting him contacting her. Defendant sent 10 letters to victim in which he blamed her for ruining his life and tried to phone her 5 times. Defendant was convicted of sexual assault, sentenced to five years, and forbidden to contact victim. Defendant sent her letters and called her from prison. Victim felt threatened by defendant and his first letter, and gave other letters to officers unread. Defendant was convicted of criminal attempt to commit harassment, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-183(a)(2), 53a-49. Defendant's unpreserved argument on appeal, that § 53a-183(a)(2) had been unconstitutionally applied against his U.S. Const. amend. I free speech right, was reviewed under the Golding standard and the Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 60-5 plain error doctrine. The court affirmed. Section 53a-183(a)(2) proscribed harassment by mail, not the content of the mail, and its recitation in a jury instruction without the express statement that it did not proscribe content, was sufficient, as was the evidence.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed. Defendant's free speech challenge on appeal, reviewed for plain error, did not prevail because the evidence showed that victim felt threatened by defendant's contact and he knew it, and the criminal statute proscribed harassment by mail, not the content of the mail. Recitation of the statute in the jury instruction without the express statement that it proscribed conduct not content was sufficient.

 

370 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Valinski


(SC 16132)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


254 Conn. 107; 756 A.2d 1250; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 252


April 19, 2000, Argued  
August 8, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license, one count of the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drug, and with the infraction of failing to drive on the right, and, in the second part, with previously having been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drug, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, and tried to the jury before Kocay, J., on the two counts of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license and the count of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drug; verdict of guilty; thereafter, with respect to the infraction of failing to drive on the right, the matter was tried to the court, which rendered a finding of guilty; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the second part of the information charging him with previously having been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence [***2] of intoxicating liquor or drug; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict with respect to one count of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license and rendered judgment of guilty of one count each of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license and operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drug, and the infraction of failing to drive on the right, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, O'Connell, C. J., and Landau and Daly, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial on the one count of operating a motor vehicle with a suspended license, from which the state appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the Appellate Court's (Connecticut) reversal of defendant driver's conviction of driving under suspension, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c), and remand of the case for a new trial on that count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's driving privileges were suspended and he was issued a permit to drive to work. Defendant was convicted of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-215(c), 14-227a, and 14-230 for, respectively, driving under suspension, under the influence, and on the wrong side of the road. The appellate court found that the trial court's instruction to the jury, that defendant was required to prove by a fair preponderance of the evidence that he was driving his vehicle within the scope of his work permit, unconstitutionally diluted the State's burden of proving the defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and reversed only that conviction. The court reversed and remanded. Section 14-215(c) defined driving under suspension and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-37a provided the work permit exception to culpability for a § 14-215(c) violation. Where an exception to a prohibition in a criminal statute was situated separately from the enacting clause, the exception was to be proven by the defense. Thus defendant bore the burden of persuasion on the § 14-37a affirmative defense to the § 14-215(c) violation.


OUTCOME: Reversal was reversed and the case remanded for consideration of defendant's other claims. Defendant was required, as an affirmative defense, to prove that he was driving within the scope of his work permit to combat the driving under suspension charge, because the statutory enacting clause of the offense was separate from the statutory exception.

 

371 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Heredia


(SC 16182)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


253 Conn. 543; 754 A.2d 114; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 201


March 22, 2000, Argued  
July 4, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Habeas Corpus Dismissed October 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2862.
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Heredia v. Strange, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2862 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at State v. Heredia, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3782 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of attempted murder, assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and attempted robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Murray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) which convicted him following a jury trial of attempted murder, kidnapping in the first degree, and attempted robbery in the first degree. Defendant claimed that his constitutional rights to be present at trial, to confront witnesses against him, and to testify on his own behalf were violated by comments relating to interpreter use.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty after a jury trial of attempted murder, kidnapping in the first degree, and attempted robbery in the first degree. Defendant had entered a fast food drive-in to rob the store. The robbery was unsuccessful, but in the process defendant shot and wounded an employee, tried to shoot another, locked an employee in a freezer, escaped, and was found hiding by the canine unit. Defendant's questions and instructions to the employees were in English mixed with Spanish. He was positively identified by employees. At trial defendant claimed he was not the perpetrator, because he could not speak much English and needed his interpreter. The State's closing comments to the jury, based in part upon the evidence of defendant's employment history in an English speaking environment, indicated that defendant was faking that he could not understand English. Under these circumstances the court affirmed that the comments were not improper. The comments did not deny defendant's constitutional rights to be present at trial, to confront the witnesses against him, and to testify on his own behalf.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The prosecutor's comments relating to interpreter use were not constitutionally improper, because defendant's defense was based upon mistaken identity. Defendant claimed that he could not speak much English and therefore needed an interpreter. However, the victims who positively identified defendant testified as to defendant's extensive English comments to them.

 

372 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bell Atl. Mobile, Inc. v. Department of Pub. Util. Control


(SC 16147)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


253 Conn. 453; 754 A.2d 128; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 189


January 18, 2000, Argued  
June 13, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant determining that the plaintiff was subject to an assessment to fund a statewide program for the subsidization of basic home telephone service for low income telephone customers, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, McWeeny, J.; judgment for the defendants dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commercial mobile radio service provider appealed a judgment of Superior Court in judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut) dismissing plaintiff's appeal from defendant utility agency's decision that 47 U.S.C.S. § 332(c)(3)(A) did not preempt Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-247e and that assessment methodology did not violate federal law and was not discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff commercial mobile radio service provider appealed a trial court judgment dismissing its appeal from defendant state utility control agency's decision requiring plaintiff to contribute to a state universal service program under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-247e. The state program was permitted under 47 U.S.C.S. § 254(f) to assure high quality telecommunications to residents and business. The issue was whether certain federal law, notably 47 U.S.C.S. § 332(c)(3)(A), preempted the state from collecting those payments, because that constituted setting rates. The court affirmed the judgment determining that there was no preemption because the program was included within "other terms and conditions" of § 332(c)(3)(A) so such contributions could be required by states without a finding that the providers served as a substitute to land line service for a substantial portion of the state. Step one of the Chevron statutory interpretation review tool, clear Congressional intent, was satisfied. Assessments based on interstate revenue were not shown to rely on or burden federal funding mechanisms and were not prohibited. No inequitable burden on cellular providers was shown.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Phrase "other terms and conditions" in federal statute, which states could regulate without having to satisfy the substitutability requirement, encompassed universal service funding requirements; assessment based partly on interstate revenue was not shown to rely on or burden federal funding mechanisms and was not prohibited; and an inequitable burden on cellular providers was not shown.

 

373 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Velasco


(SC 16134)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


253 Conn. 210; 751 A.2d 800; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 140


January 20, 2000, Argued  
May 16, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at, Summary judgment denied by Velasco v. Warden, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 178 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 18, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty of felony murder and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree; thereafter, the court found the defendant guilty of commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm and rendered judgment of guilty on all three counts, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) convicting defendant of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 53a-134(a), and commission of robbery with a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, conspiracy to commit robbery under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 53a-134(a), and commission of robbery with a firearm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k. Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted on the first two counts, and sentenced to 60 years' imprisonment. The trial court then determined, based on evidence presented at trial, that defendant had used a firearm during the commission of the offenses, and imposed an additional five-year sentence to run consecutively. The principal issue on appeal was whether the trial court, rather than the jury, could find that defendant, who was convicted by a jury of a felony, had used a firearm in the commission of such felony. Evidence that defendant used a proscribed firearm was neither overwhelming nor uncontested, nor was such a finding implicit in the verdict. The trial court's failure to instruct the jury on whether defendant utilized a proscribed firearm was not harmless. The case was remanded for a new jury trial on the issue of whether defendant used a proscribed firearm in the commission of the underlying offenses.


OUTCOME: Because court concluded that finding that defendant used firearm was not indispensable to verdict, and that evidence neither overwhelmingly nor incontrovertibly established that defendant was armed, judgment was reversed in part and case remanded with direction to vacate sentence and for new jury trial on issue of whether defendant used proscribed firearm in commission of underlying offenses. Judgement was affirmed in all other respects.

 

374 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Shay v. Rossi


(SC 16212)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


253 Conn. 134; 749 A.2d 1147; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 143


January 12, 2000, Argued  
May 3, 2000, * Officially Released


* May 3, 2000, the date that this opinion was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, personal injuries sustained as a result of the conduct of the defendants, in their official and individual capacities, in conducting an investigation into possible child neglect and abuse by the named plaintiff et al., and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, and referred to Hon. Walter M. Pickett, judge trial referee, who granted in part the defendants' motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered partial judgment thereon dismissing the action against the defendants in their individual capacities, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendants cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants and plaintiffs appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut) that denied dismissal of the action against defendants in their official capacities based upon sovereign immunity, and granted dismissal in their individual capacities under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, in plaintiff family member's action based upon defendant social workers' attempts to remove children from family unit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff parents took child to hospital for leg broken after mother tripped while breast feeding. Because family had sought medical assistance for other children and the physician's initial report suggested abuse, defendants' initiated proceedings to remove children from the family, and persisted their attempts even after that and three other physicians stated no abuse and neighbors stated an overprotective family. Plaintiff family sued defendants in official and individual capacities. Trial court's order denying defendants' motion to dismiss on the basis of sovereign immunity was an appealable final order, because sovereign immunity affects liability and right to sue. The order denying dismissal of suits against defendants in official capacities affirmed and individual capacities reversed, because defendants' alleged actions would exceed the scope of their statutory authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. Facts indicated defendants persisted in efforts to remove children to justify their prior unjustified actions, which were sufficiently egregious to constitute conduct in excess of statutory authority and of sovereign immunity protection.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings; order denying motion to dismiss affirmed on the basis of sovereign immunity was an appealable final judgment, because sovereign immunity is immunity from liability and suit; order denying dismissal of suits against defendants in official capacities affirmed and individual capacities reversed, because defendants' alleged actions would exceed the scope of their statutory authority.

State v. Johnson


(SC 14801)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


253 Conn. 1; 751 A.2d 298; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 144


October 26, 1999, Argued  
May 2, 2000, Officially Released * 


* May 2, 2000, the date that this opinion was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


NOTICE:

[EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 2 OF 2. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


PRIOR HISTORY: Amended information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder, capital felony, burglary in the first degree and larceny in the third degree and twenty counts of the crime of stealing a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham at Putnam and presented to a three judge court, Corrigan, Spada and Potter, Js., on pleas of guilty to the charges of murder, capital felony and burglary in the first degree; thereafter, the penalty phase of the proceedings was tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict finding the existence of two aggravating factors and no mitigating factor in the commission of the crime of felony murder, and the court, Corrigan, J., rendered judgment of guilty of murder, capital felony and burglary in the first degree in accordance with the pleas and the verdict and, merging the murder and capital felony counts, imposed the death penalty on the latter count and a term of imprisonment on the burglary count; subsequently, the state nolled the remaining charges and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant felon sought review of judgment of Superior Court in judicial district of Windham at Putnam (Connecticut), convicting him of murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a (1991), capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b, 53a-54a(a), (c) (1991), and burglary in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. 53a-101(a)(1), (2) (1991), and imposing the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant felon was convicted of capital felony for the murder of a state police officer acting within the scope of his duties in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54b(1), 53a-54a(a),(c), burglary in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-101(a)(1), (2), and murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. Appellant had broken into a gun shop, where he stole weapons and ammunition. During the course of the break-in, a state police officer on routine patrol approached the gun shop, whereupon appellant fired upon him, fatally wounding him. After appellant's guilty plea, a separate sentencing hearing was conducted, the jury sentencing him to death, having found an aggravating factor but no mitigating factor. Appellant challenged both the conviction and the sentence, raising 28 issues, of which the court considered five. The court affirmed the judgment of convictions on all counts. However, because there was insufficient evidence of the existence of an aggravating factor, the court reversed the judgment with respect to the imposition of the death penalty, and remanded the case with direction for the imposition of a life sentence without the possibility of release.


OUTCOME: Convictions were affirmed. Trial court's implicitly finding appellant competent in accepting guilty pleas was not abuse of discretion; failure to provide competency evaluation did not deprive appellant of due process, constituting harmless error. Death penalty judgment was reversed and case remanded with direction to impose life sentence without possibility of release; trial evidence did not support jury's finding of aggravating factor.

State v. Ehlers


(SC 15937)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


252 Conn. 579; 750 A.2d 1079; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 91


September 24, 1999, Argued  
March 28, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 4, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of child pornography, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, where the court, Stanley, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the information; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possessing child pornography from Superior Court in Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss, determining that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-196d was not unconstitutionally vague even though it failed to define "minor." The appellate court concluded that since constitutionally protected speech was not implicated, even if the statute were vague as applied in some hypothetical case, defendant could not prevail on his facial challenge under U.S. Const. amend. I. Based on similar child pornography statutes, the term child pornography as used in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-196d included material covered by the definition of child pornography in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-193(13). Since defendant conceded that he possessed materials depicting persons under 16 years and had fair warning that his conduct was prohibited under the most stringent interpretation, the statute was not void for vague. A photographer taking pictures constituted an audience under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-196d, which was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because child pornography statute was not unconstitutionally vague, defendant conceded that he possessed materials depicting persons under 16 years, defendant had fair warning that his conduct was prohibited under most stringent interpretation, and evidence was sufficient to support his conviction.

Moore v. Continental Cas. Co.


(SC 16100)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


252 Conn. 405; 746 A.2d 1252; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 67


December 7, 1999, Argued  
March 13, 2000, * Officially Released


* March 13, 2000, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine whether the defendant was obligated to defend and indemnify the plaintiff pursuant to a homeowner's insurance policy it had issued to the plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, DiPentima, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Spear and Healey, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from appellate court affirmation of Superior Court of District of New Haven's (Connecticut) summary judgment for defendant in declaratory judgment action to determine whether defendant was obligated to defend plaintiff under homeowner's policy. Sole issue was whether emotional distress arising out of economic loss triggered duty to defend.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was insured under a homeowner's policy issued by defendant. Plaintiff's sister sued plaintiff for conversion, fraud, and intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress, over a jointly-owned property with her mother. She alleged plaintiff obtained a power of attorney and used it to obtain a line of credit secured by the property, resulting in loss of the property's value. Plaintiff brought declaratory judgment action seeking adjudication that defendant had a duty to defend him against his sister's complaint. The parties filed cross motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted defendant's motion and denied plaintiff's motion. The appellate court affirmed. Conceding there were no disputed questions of fact, the plaintiff claimed defendant had a duty to defend because the insurance policy defined "bodily injury" broadly enough to include emotional distress. The Supreme Court also affirmed, holding defendant had no duty to defend under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: Supreme court concluded allegations of emotional distress arising from economic loss did not trigger defendant's duty to defend under homeowner's policy, and affirmed the judgment of the Appellate Court.

State v. Webb


(SC 14409)


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


252 Conn. 128; 750 A.2d 448; 2000 Conn. LEXIS 19


October 28, 1999, Argued  
February 15, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5313.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Claim dismissed by Webb v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2877 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 8, 2003)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Claims of Racial Disparity v. Comm'r of Corr., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Webb v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 225 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 25, 2011)

PRIOR HISTORY: Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, kidnapping in the first degree, criminal attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found the existence of aggravating factors and no mitigating factor, and the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and imposed the death penalty on the first three counts and terms of imprisonment on the remaining counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for consideration of the defendant's claim that death by lethal injection was unconstitutional as cruel and unusual punishment, with this court retaining jurisdiction for the purpose of appellate review of the trial court's determination of that claim; on remand, the court, Fasano, J., rendered judgment denying the defendant's challenge to the state's method [***2] of execution under the state's constitution.
State v. Webb, 1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1911 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 1, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) on remand denying defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VIII challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-100 which establishes lethal injection as the state's present method of execution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the superior court on remand denying defendant's U.S. Const. amend. VIII challenge to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-100 which established lethal injection as Connecticut's method of execution. On appeal, the defendant argued that lethal injection constitutes cruel and unusual punishment because the protocol developed by the commissioner of correction carries an unacceptably high risk that the execution procedure will be botched, and because there is a high risk that the defendant would experience excruciating pain and a lingering death. Plaintiff state responded that lethal injection is the most humane method available for imposing capital punishment. The court affirmed because it concluded that the record failed to establish any reason to infer that the protocol would not be administered properly. On the basis of the testimony introduced regarding the agents utilized pursuant to the protocol and the corresponding dosages, there was no reason to believe that defendant would experience anything more than the insertion of the intravenous catheter followed by unconsciousness.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The record failed to establish any reason to infer that the protocol would not be administered properly. Furthermore, on the basis of the testimony introduced regarding the agents utilized pursuant to the protocol and the corresponding dosages, there was no reason to believe that defendant would experience anything more than the insertion of the intravenous catheter followed by unconsciousness.

Williams v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 37909


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


169 Conn. App. 776; 153 A.3d 656; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 462


September 15, 2016, Argued 
December, 2016, Officially Released on the 20th of December, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
State v. Williams, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1664 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant's certification to appeal was properly denied when defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus based upon alleged ineffective assistance of counsel in regard to prosecutorial impropriety. HOLDINGS: [1]-The habeas court correctly concluded that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge statements the prosecutor made in closing argument because the prosecutor did not express his own opinion or provide facts not in evidence, and, thus, his statements regarding the trustworthiness of a witness for the prosecution and defendant's brother were not improper; [2]-The habeas court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's petition for certification to appeal because there was no reasonable probability that, but for appellate counsel's failure to raise a claim of prosecutorial impropriety, defendant would have prevailed in his direct appeal.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.

State v. Andriulaitis


AC 38367


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


169 Conn. App. 286; 150 A.3d 720; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 415


September 14, 2016, Argued 
November 8, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of criminal lockout and with the crime of disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the court, Schuman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of disorderly conduct, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of offensive or disorderly conduct (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2)), as it allowed the trial court as fact-finder to infer that he shouted profanities in an angry and threatening manner with the intent to impede his daughter's ability to engage in the lawful activity of retrieving her belongings from his home, and that he accomplished this through conduct that was grossly offensive under contemporary community standards; [2]-Whether defendant's language amounted to fighting words was immaterial because his conduct consisted of more than mere speech; in addition to shouting profanities and that he did not want her to enter the home, defendant stood in the entrance hallway near the door, and, through that conduct, prevented her from engaging in the lawful activity of entering the home to retrieve her personal possessions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Collymore


AC 37703


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


168 Conn. App. 847; 148 A.3d 1059; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 393


January 14, 2016, Argued 
October 11, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Collymore, 2017 Conn. LEXIS 32 (Conn., Jan. 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, and with the crimes of felony murder, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Cremins, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly applied Conn. Gen. V was not violative of defendant's rights because he did not establish either the prosecutorial misconduct or effective defense theory; [3]-Defendant's unpreserved claim that the trial court improperly lengthened his sentence as punishment for going to trial lacked merit, as a comment about defendant's failure to accept responsibility for his actions was a proper sentencing comment based on defendant's own statements wherein he blamed the prosecutor.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Robert H.


AC 36742, AC 37544


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


168 Conn. App. 419; 146 A.3d 995; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 357


November 17, 2015, Argued 
September 20, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Robert H., 2016 Conn. LEXIS 372 (Conn., Nov. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the first case was tried to the jury before Suarez, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of risk of injury to a child; thereafter, defendant was presented to the court in the second case on a plea of guilty; judgments of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant filed separate appeals with this court, which consolidated the appeals.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was convicted of two counts of risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of a child (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21), he could not raise the unpreserved claim that his statement to police that he had masturbated in the victim's presence on more than one occasion was insufficient to convict him of the second count due to the lack of corroboration, because the corpus delecti rule was solely a rule of admissibility and he had not objected at trial to the admission of his confession; [2]-The evidence was sufficient to convict him of two counts of violating § 53-21, as the jury was free to credit his admission to masturbating in the victim's presence on at least two occasions over her testimony that she remembered him masturbating in her presence on only one occasion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

AC 37588


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


167 Conn. App. 786; 145 A.3d 317; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 335

OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; matter remanded for a new trial.

State v. Palmenta


AC 37891


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


168 Conn. App. 37; 144 A.3d 503; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 340


May 12, 2016, Argued 
September 6, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Palmenta, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 335 (Conn., Oct. 18, 2016)
Appeal dismissed by State v. Palmenta, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 336 (Conn., Oct. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information in the first case charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of burglary in the second degree, criminal mischief in the second and attempt to commit larceny in the third degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, and two part information in the second case charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of burglary in the third degree, identity theft in the third degree and larceny in the fifth degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, where the defendant was presented to the court, Gill, J., on pleas of guilty; judgments of guilty in accordance with the pleas; thereafter, the court, Ginnochio, J., denied the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Palmenta, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2101 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 21, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-"And" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(c) was conjunctive as § 53a-40(c) addressed two preconditions for a persistent serious felony offender status exemption--that the present conviction be for a crime enumerated in § 53a-40(a)(1), and that the prior conviction be for a crime other than those enumerated in § 53a-40(a); [2]-Defendant was not exempt under the plain language of the statute as he was not convicted of a crime listed in § 53a-40(a)(1); [3]-Because defendant had not been convicted of any of the felonies listed in § 53a-40(a)(1)(A), application of the exemption to defendant would frustrate the purpose of the statute; [4]-A conjunctive reading of the word "and" would not lead to an illogical result or create disharmony in the statute's structure; [5]-The rule of lenity did not require that the exemption be read disjunctively.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Dumas v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 36974


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


168 Conn. App. 130; 145 A.3d 355; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 345


January 19, 2016, Argued 
September 6, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Dumas v. Comm'r of Corr., 2016 Conn. LEXIS 415 (Conn., Dec. 13, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Cobb, J.; judgment dismissing in part and denying in part the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Cobb, J., issued an articulation of its decision.
Dumas v. Comm'r of Corr., 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1931 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Claims made under Graham v. Florida were moot due to the October 1, 2015 enactment of Conn. Gen.
