VIII, the 30-year sentence imposed on the inmate did not violate the Eighth Amendment; [6]-The inmate's petition for certification to appeal was properly denied.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.

 

389 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kinch


AC 37433, AC 37434


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


168 Conn. App. 62; 144 A.3d 509; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 342


April 12, 2016, Argued 
September 6, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Kinch, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 330 (Conn., Oct. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Cronan, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; thereafter, upon the defendant's failure to appear for sentencing, the state filed an information charging the defendant with failure to appear in the first degree and the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdicts, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court; subsequently the appeals were consolidated.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Brendlin concerned the seizure of a passenger, not the search of the vehicle itself, and had no bearing on whether a passenger had standing to challenge the search of the vehicle and the seizure of items contained therein; [2]-Connecticut adhered to the reasonable expectation of privacy standard in assessing whether a defendant had standing to contest the search of a vehicle or the items discovered therein under the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV; [3]-Defendant did not assert a possessory interest in the vehicle or the items discovered therein; [4]-Defendant was merely a passenger in a vehicle in which contraband was discovered, which the officer observed from the outside of the vehicle; [5]-Defendant lacked standing to challenge the search as he did not show that he possessed an expectation of privacy in the area of the vehicle where the evidence was seized.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

Cornelius v. Rosario


AC 37210


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


167 Conn. App. 120; 143 A.3d 611; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 300


January 20, 2016, Argued 
July 26, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to quiet title to certain real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the action was withdrawn as against the defendant Edward Baum; thereafter, the court, Hon. Robert Satter, judge trial referee, granted the motion to strike filed by the defendant Alberta Ward et al.; subsequently, the court, Aurigemma, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the named defendant et al. and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court; thereafter, the Supreme Court denied the plaintiff's petition for certification to appeal; subsequently, the United States Supreme Court denied the plaintiff's petition for a writ of certiorari; thereafter, the court, Vacchelli, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to open the judgment; subsequently, the court, Vacchelli, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to reargue; thereafter, the court, Vacchelli, J., denied the named defendant's motion for attorney's fees and costs; subsequently, the court, Vacchelli, J., granted the named defendant's motion to reargue; [***2] thereafter, the court, Vacchelli, J., granted in part the named defendant's motion for attorney's fees and costs, and the plaintiff appealed and the named defendant cross appealed to this court.
Cornelius v. Rosario, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1829 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 28, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-140 allowed an award of reasonable attorney's fees incurred by tax collectors in successfully defending tax sale challenges; [2]-The taxpayer was the delinquent taxpayer for § 12-140 purposes; [3]-The recovery of attorney's fees under § 12-140 was not preempted by 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988; [4]-The former tax collector's motion for attorney's fees was untimely under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 11-21 with regard to the attorney's fees incurred in defending the taxpayer's motion to open; [5]-The tax collector's motion for attorney's fees initially incurred at the trial court was untimely under § 11-21; [6]-Rizzo Pool Co. and Jacques All Trades Corp. did not hold that a prevailing party in the trial court could await the outcome of any appeal before moving for attorney's fees incurred in prevailing in the trial court.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part. Case remanded with direction.

State v. Panek


AC 36820


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


166 Conn. App. 613; 145 A.3d 924; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 281


October 22, 2015, Argued 
July 5, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Panek, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 285 (Conn., Sept. 20, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three informations charging the defendant, in each case, with the crime of voyeurism, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the court, Wenzel, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.
State v. Panek, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 922 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 21, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The dismissal of three consolidated informations charging the defendant with violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-189a(a)(1) was proper because, under the plain and unambiguous language of the video voyeurism statute, the perspective from which the "not in plain view" element of voyeurism must be evaluated was that of the defendant, not that of the general public; [2]-Because the video voyeurism statute concerned conduct involving two and only two persons, the complainant whose image was allegedly recorded without her knowledge and consent and defendant who allegedly recorded that image of her when she was not in plain view, it must logically be defendant as to whom the complainant was not in plain view when her image was recorded, for she will always have been in plain view of herself.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Staurovsky v. City of Milford Police Dep't


AC 37670


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


164 Conn. App. 182; 134 A.3d 1263; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 131


January 4, 2016, Argued 
March 29, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Staurovsky v. City of Milford Police Dep't, 321 Conn. 915, 136 A.3d 645, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 147 (2016)
Appeal dismissed by Staurovsky v. Milford Police Dep't, 2017 Conn. LEXIS 39 (Conn., Feb. 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the Workers' Compensation Commissioner for the Fourth District awarding certain disability benefits to the plaintiff, brought to the Workers' Compensation Review Board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; decision directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Workers' Compensation Review Board erred in affirming the workers' compensation commissioner's award of heart and hypertension benefits to plaintiff retired police officer under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c. HOLDINGS: [1]-The Board properly found that plaintiff's claim, filed a month after he had a heart attack, was timely; Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-294c(a)'s one year limitation period was not triggered when he consulted a cardiologist nine years before the heart attack, as the cardiologist did not diagnose heart disease or hypertension; [2]-However, as plaintiff's heart disease was not manifested until he had a heart attack after he retired, he was ineligible for heart disease and hypertension benefits because he did not suffer any condition or impairment of his health caused by hypertension or heart disease during the course of his employment with the police department.


OUTCOME: The Board's decision was reversed.

Harnage v. Lightner


AC 37539


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


163 Conn. App. 337; 137 A.3d 10; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 78


October 28, 2015, Argued 
March 1, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Harnage v. Lightner, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 273 (Conn., Sept. 13, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for alleged violations of the plaintiff's federal constitutional rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Peck, J., granted in part the defendants' motion to dismiss, and the plaintiff appealed to this court, which dismissed the appeal for lack of a final judgment; thereafter, the court, Hon. Constance L. Epstein, judge trial referee, granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment and the defendants' motion to dismiss, and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiff inmate sued state employees for allegedly violating his constitutional rights, he failed to properly serve them in their individual capacities under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-57(a), as service on the Attorney General's office under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-64 was permissible only when the state employees were sued in their official capacities; thus, his claims against them in their individual capacities were properly dismissed; [2]-As his indigence and inmate status did not exempt him from liability to pay costs, the recognizance bond requirement applied to him; but as former Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-185 and 52-186 infringed on his right of access to the courts, the appellate court interpreted them as allowing the trial court to waive or reduce the bond on a showing of the inmate's indigency and inability to find someone else to enter into a bond on his behalf.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part and affirmed in part.

Edgewood St. Garden Apts., LLC v. City of Hartford


AC 36946


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


163 Conn. App. 219; 135 A.3d 54; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 65


September 14, 2015, Submitted on Briefs 
February 23, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Edgewood St. Garden Apts., LLC v. City of Hartford, 321 Conn. 903, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 101 (Conn., Apr. 6, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged violation of the plaintiff's federal and state constitutional rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Swienton, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Edgewood St. Garden Apts., LLC v. City of Hartford, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1313 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 27, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiff failed to establish a claim against a city under § 1983 based on its demolition of plaintiff's building because there was no evidence of any city policy that directed the building inspector to demolish the building; rather, a city ordinance directed him to evaluate the condition of the property and determine its safety, and evidence suggesting he was mistaken in concluding that the building posed an imminent danger to adjoining properties was insufficient to prove the required causal link between the city's policy and the alleged violations of plaintiff's constitutional rights; [2]-The demolition of plaintiff's building did not amount to a taking, as there was no evidence the city's exercise of its police power was unreasonable or confiscatory or that no reasonable use could be made of plaintiff's property, which it still owned.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Goodwin v. Colchester Probate Court


AC 36214


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


162 Conn. App. 412; 133 A.3d 156; 2016 Conn. App. LEXIS 12


October 22, 2015, Argued 
January 19, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Goodwin v. Colchester Probate Court, 320 Conn. 924, 133 A.3d 878, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 61 (Conn., Mar. 2, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order and decree of the Probate Court for the district of Colchester, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Cosgrove, J., granted the motion to intervene as defendants filed by Stephen Fedus, Jr., et al.; thereafter, the court, Hon. Thomas F. Parker, judge trial referee, granted the motion to intervene as defendants filed by Madeline Goodwin et al.; subsequently, the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Joseph Q. Koletsky, judge trial referee; thereafter, the court, Hon. Joseph Q. Koletsky, judge trial referee, denied the motion to dismiss for failure to present a prima facie case filed by the defendant John Fedus et al.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal, from which the defendant John Fedus appealed to this court.
Goodwin v. Colchester Probate Court, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2172 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 28, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-There was no sufficient objection to a decedent's will under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-288(a) as plaintiff had presented the probate court with an authenticated and exemplified copy of the decedent's will that the court found was proved and established by a court of competent jurisdiction, the Philadelphia register of wills; [2]-Defendant did not show that the decedent's will did not comply with Pennsylvania law as to the execution of a will, that it was not properly probated or that the record of the proceedings proving the will in Pennsylvania were not in order; [3]-He did not show that plaintiff had failed to request that copies of the documents submitted be filed and recorded or failed to provide a description of the Connecticut property; [5]-Defendant's Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 15-8 motion failed as whether the will was legally sufficient was not at issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Fetscher


AC 36615


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


162 Conn. App. 145; 130 A.3d 892; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 489


October 14, 2015, Argued 
December 29, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Fetscher, 321 Conn. 904, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 114 (Conn., Apr. 13, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, and with the infractions of traveling unreasonably fast and failure to drive in the proper lane, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Truglia, J., denied the defendant's application to participate in the alcohol education program; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs; thereafter, the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the charges of traveling unreasonably fast and failure to drive in the proper lane; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.
